# Igros Kodesh

## Volume 24

## 339

B"H, Between Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Rabbi Yoel Sperka, shlita,

Shalom u’Bracha,

With significant delay, I received your letter along with the enclosed draft for a request for forgiveness (*mechilah*). Your suggestion to publicize this matter on the widest possible scale is correct, as requesting *mechilah* from one’s fellow is among the most essential matters, as our Sages of blessed memory state in the Mishnah at the conclusion and seal of Yom Kippur. Surely you have approached the various rabbinical organizations and associations regarding this. For although there is importance in publicizing this through letters, it certainly does not compare to the impact if the Rabbis were to speak about this in their addresses; at that moment, they have the ability to facilitate the request for *mechilah* for all those present during the speech, and so on.

I am sending this letter quickly so that there will still be time to act on this matter before Yom Kippur.

For various reasons, I am not in a position at this time to issue a letter with the content you suggest or anything similar, although I read your letter with special interest.

With respect and with the blessing of *Chasimah v’Gmar Chasimah Tovah* to you and to all the members of the Vaad HaRabbanim, shlita.

***

339

Some of the letters are from the secretariat’s copy and some are from a photocopy of the original letter. They are not marked with footnotes unless the source is different, or if it has already been printed in *Likkutei Sichos* or the like.

**Rabbi Yoel Sperka, shlita**: One of the members of the Vaad HaRabbanim of Detroit.

**Draft for a request for forgiveness**: "I hereby grant complete forgiveness to anyone who has sinned against me, etc."

**As our Sages of blessed memory state in the Mishnah**: Yoma, at the end (85b).

## 332

332

B”H, the day after Yom Kippur, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to the questions of many—following my first letter on this subject—regarding the stance that should be taken now in connection with the Knesset elections, after the deadline for submitting lists has passed, with each of the religious parties going to the elections with its own separate list, and asking for my opinion and reaction to this:

While on the one hand, the greatest sorrow is understandable regarding the aforementioned split, on the other hand—precisely in these last few days, public declarations have appeared that provide hope for rectifying the situation, at least in a significant part of it, as will be explained below. I am referring to the declarations made by **each** of the religious parties in their speeches and official publications, in which each one announces with full force that it is not to blame for the failure to establish a technical religious front, nor is it the one causing the split, etc., but rather that extraneous reasons beyond its control prevented the establishment of the aforementioned front, and it proceeds to detail these reasons one by one.

Since the aforementioned declarations were made by the leaders and captains of each of the parties publicly, and were made orally and in writing and repeated several times, they are certainly responsible and were made with the knowledge of all the decision-makers in the party, and they obligate the entire party. They also announced openly even beforehand, and likewise orally, in writing, in print, and officially, that Heaven forbid that personal interests and the gains of certain individuals (and my hope is that this also refers to excluding the gains of factions within the party) should influence the question of establishing a technical religious front, which is for the benefit of the entire public of the children of Israel in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established (from which it is understood that this is the benefit of all the factions and all the religious parties, and the benefit of each and every one of the children of Israel residing in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established). They also emphasized that they saw tangibly in the last Knesset and the one before it that in several debates a single vote was the deciding factor—which highlights even more the necessity for a technical religious front, which one would hope would have added to the number of representatives, and even more than just one, two, or three representatives.

To all the above, I will add one brief premise: It is customary for every party (in its election platform) to inform the voters and the public of its ideology and its plan of action for the duration of the Knesset that is about to be elected. And on the basis of this election platform, the voters deliberate for whom they will vote.

In light of these premises, a logical proposal is requested in connection with the elections in general, and in connection with the issue of a technical front in particular, and it is:

That each of the religious parties should announce in its election platform, in a special, clear, and detailed clause, its position and decision regarding the question of establishing a technical religious front in the future.

And in order to rule out what just happened, where each party blames the other for sabotaging the front due to hidden agendas, schemes, etc.—each party shall **detail** its position on the aforementioned issue in the **fullest** detail, meaning a specification of all the conditions it sets for the establishment of a technical religious front. It is understood that this specification must be sufficient—so as not to leave room for sabotaging the establishment of a technical religious front in the future with pretexts that "this is not what was intended," etc., and with mutual accusations thereafter. And also to add that since the matter is one of "if you grasp a little," i.e., only the establishment of a **technical** religious front, there is certainly no room for conditions that would only be relevant if the matter were one of a principled union for several years, etc.

The voters, in whose hands the fate of the elections lies, are adults, and they are entitled to demand from each of the parties that it announce its position on such a vital question—a position that is explicit and reasoned with good taste and understanding, in order to give the voter the possibility to judge for himself not only the position of each party but also the reasons and arguments upon which the position is based. Therefore, certainly every condition among the conditions that require explanation—should come with its reason and argument.

As mentioned above, I do not see in the aforementioned proposal anything out of the ordinary, since an election platform includes a plan of action for several years. And even if there were something in this that was out of the ordinary, the situation in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, is **entirely** out of the ordinary—both in material and in spiritual matters, and the intelligent will understand.

And here is the place to emphasize the fact that for the elections in several local authorities, a religious front exists. That is to say, there is a clear decision **in practice** from each of the religious parties, both on the part of the political leadership and on the part of their spiritual leadership, that in principle there is room for a religious front of all the parties. And the law is: if for the elections to the local authorities, where the meetings between the party representatives are more frequent and tighter, and especially in the days of the elections when the propaganda is conducted there in the vast majority by the local people—meaning that a religious front in the locality is more likely to blur the boundaries between them and increase the danger of the influence of the worldview of one party on its fellow—and nevertheless there is room for a religious front, and not just a technical front, but for cooperation throughout all the days of the local government, as is customary in several places—then all the more so is there room in principle for a technical religious front for the Knesset elections.

And furthermore, regarding the election platform, there is no time limit (since it is subject to changes and additions from day to day) until the last moment before the elections, although earlier is better—so that the other religious parties can take a position regarding any addition to the election platform of the party competing with it, so that the platform will be clear to all. That is to say, that same argument that some claimed—that it was impossible to establish a technical religious front because of the shortness of time—is not an argument in the present case.

There is no contradiction in the above to the calls published by each party that one should vote specifically for it, since if each party clarifies its position on a technical religious front in an unambiguous manner, on the contrary, it is possible that this will add strength to its call, since there will be no room to accuse it of evasion and concealing matters from the public, etc.

I am not a prophet, nor the son of a prophet, and all that is said above remains in force even if four years pass until the next elections, and all the more so since, in the opinion of many experts, in light of the split in all the parties, it is highly probable that the new Knesset will not last long and the next elections will be held much sooner.

* * *

Based on the above, the hope is strong that the aforementioned proposal will be accepted regarding the publication of each party's position on the most vital question of establishing a technical religious front in the future. And after the religious parties publish their detailed position, with its reasons and arguments as stated, and since according to common sense and—more importantly—according to the law of our holy Torah, the Torah of life, **the improvement of the religious situation of the broadest strata** of our brethren the children of Israel in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, is the deciding factor, the voter will vote for the list whose representatives will accept upon themselves decisively and without reservation to conduct themselves in accordance with the instruction of our aforementioned Torah.

With respect and blessing.

P.S. Isru Chag of Sukkos:

For a reason and cause, the sending of this letter was delayed. In the meantime, an official copy was received of a declaration signed by all three religious parties (in connection with the "United Religious Front for the Tel Aviv-Jaffa Municipality")—which adds more weight, if there were a need for it, to what was said above. I will copy only a few lines, even though the entire thing pertains to the above, and this is its content:

B”H, between Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, 5726
To the faithful of Israel:
...At a time when every person in Israel communes with his Creator and makes a reckoning of his soul, both private and general—the hearts of the leaders of faithful Judaism were stirred by a good thing...
**To establish a united religious front in the elections for the Tel Aviv-Jaffa city council.**
...This joyous news spread wings and was received with great blessing and enthusiasm by all who heard it. At a time when all the secular lists are united as one in their war against the spiritual character of our city, it is only right that the children of Israel who are faithful to the Torah of Israel and its mitzvos should rise, all as one, and act together for the sake of... strict preservation of religious education... a firm action to increase the observance of our holy Shabbos in our city...
Every voter... should give his strength and his wealth for the consolidation of the united campaign of united Judaism...
And join the faithful camp of the United Religious Front...

And furthermore, to add the public and official opinion of the "Great Ones of Israel... to the holy congregation in the Holy Land" regarding the greatest importance of even one additional representative in the Knesset, a importance and "vital matter for the Judaism of the Torah," and this is its content:
...This time, more than in the past, a condition and situation is liable to be created where an additional representative of Charedi Judaism is liable to tip the scales on fundamental questions that have a vital interest for the Judaism of the Torah, and it is in the hands of the faithful voter to bring this about.
...Let the individual and the many, the private and the general, prove that at the head of their concerns and at the head of their struggles stands our holy Torah, to preserve it and save it from the hand of all who rise up against it, for our holy Shabbos, for the education of our sons and daughters in the way of our ancestors...

- Those points listed in the call for the front in Tel Aviv-Jaffa were copied—that each of the parties committed to defend them with all its might, etc., to the extent that they all agreed to hand over the position of mayor to the representative of one of them in a festive manner, etc.

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Peace and blessing!

Enclosed is a copy of my letter sent to the heads of the three religious parties. May it be the will of Hashem that what is fulfilled in his grandson, may he live, is that the pressure (this *dchak*—in its literal sense) upon him here during Simchas Torah will have the effect described by our Sages: "Rabbi Yochanan said, 'Just as the olive...'" (*Menachos* 53b).

With appreciation, honor, and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 334

[Late Tishrei, 5726]

The primary intent of the aforementioned talk was for those who no longer have a structured schedule **according to Torah** regarding the aforementioned matters. This is not the case for yeshiva students, for whom the primary focus must be learning according to the yeshiva’s schedule. Only during the time **outside** of the scheduled hours is the aforementioned relevant, and even then, not for everyone. This must be done according to consultation and the guidance of a mashpia.

***

**The aforementioned talk**: At the Simchas Torah farbrengen, that everyone must learn Mikra, Mishnah, Gemara, Halacha, Midrash, Chassidus, and Kabbalah, etc.

## 335

[Parshas Bereishis, 5726]

Regarding what I have heard lately—that "bochurim from Tomchei Temimim" need to learn Nigleh and Chassidus with diligence and perseverance, and engage in the avodah of tefillah and the performance of mitzvos, etc.—

What business do they have with questions **pertaining to "Kehot" and the like**? Have they truly already learned and completed everything they were obligated to do, and the only thing they are lacking is knowledge of these matters?

Are they keeping up with Chitas?

Have they finished the Likutei Torah for Shabbos Bereishis?

***

335

Printed in *Heichal Menachem*, Vol. 2, p. 100, and completed based on a photocopy of the Rebbe’s holy handwriting. A response to one of the Temimim who asked about the publication of Chassidic discourses from manuscripts.

**Pertaining to "Kehot"**: See *Igros Kodesh* of the Rebbe Rayatz, Vol. 9, Letter 3145.

**Have they finished the Likutei Torah**: Based on the Rebbe’s instruction on Shabbos Parshas Vayakhel 5725 to study the entire *Sefer Likutei Torah* over the course of the year, meaning that every week they should study the "Chassidic portion" in *Likutei Torah* (see also above, Vol. 23, Letter 8966). Here, the intent refers to the discourses in *Torah Or*.

## 936

B”H, Days of Cheshvan, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter...

May it be the will of Hashem that you bring good tidings among us.

Especially as we—together with all of Klal Yisrael—are coming from the month of Tishrei, the general month of the entire year, which is "the time of our greatest joy," and the conclusion and seal of the festivals contained within it—the festival of the time of our joy in general, and the time of our joy of Shemini Atzeres and Simchas Torah in particular, a great joy of Torah and mitzvos. The matters of this general month are intended to influence and be drawn down into all the days of the year ahead.

With blessings for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

***

In many cases similar to that of your wife (may she live and be well), an increase in the husband’s attention toward his wife adds to her health, etc. Naturally, this must be an increase that she will feel.

***

Regarding your questions concerning the details of your conduct, and specifically the conduct of the home after your wedding (may it be for good and success)—in those matters where there are those who are stringent and those who are lenient—it is understood that not all circumstances, environments, and individuals are the same. As the Sages express it, one must consider the stringencies of the place from which one departed and the place to which one has arrived (and the same applies regarding families, etc.). You should discuss this with the Rav, the Mara D’Asra.

And how wondrous is the virtue of "sanctify yourself in that which is permitted to you." It is explained in Chassidus that specifically through this, one draws down from the level of *Atzmus Ohr Ein Sof* that is above the level of *Tohu* and *Tikkun*, the revelation of the time to come (see the *maamar* beginning "Ve'atem Tihyu Li," 5660).

***

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter—the stories of our Rebbeim, etc., in addition to the lists of those participating in the *shiurim*.

May it be the will of Hashem that you bring good tidings in Torah and mitzvos.

From the inspectors here from the Ministry of Education of the Holy Land, complaints have come regarding your son... (may he live), that when they examined him, they found a lack of knowledge, etc. Surely it is in your power to awaken and encourage him to fill this void (from books, etc.) without your son knowing that they complained to me about this, and so on.

37

By the Grace of Hashem, Days of Cheshvan, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., R. Shmuel, may he live.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the eve of Sukkos, along with the pages of your sefer, *Minchas Shmuel*.

Enclosed are a few notes regarding your aforementioned sefer.

**Sefer Minchas Shmuel, at the beginning:** Regarding Rashi’s commentary on the Mishnah at the beginning of *Berachos*: that the Sages did not decree that the burning of fats and limbs must be completed by midnight (unlike the Rambam). It could be argued that the reason is that the burning is performed by Kohanim, and "Kohanim are diligent" (whereas for the Rambam, we do not apply the principle that they are diligent in this instance; cf. *Pesachim* 85a, bottom of the page, regarding *yotzei*, based on Tosafos there).

- (Now, this has already been questioned regarding the Tosafos there—by the Maharsha and others—and to address the difficulty, one could say that according to the conclusion, Tosafos also holds like the Maharsha, but they preferred a different answer. The Rambam’s reasoning can be explained simply: in the case at hand, where the time for burning began at the moment the sacrifice was offered—which is **several hours** before nightfall (as in *Pesachim* 85a)—if the fats and limbs were not burned by midnight, it is a clear proof that **these specific** Kohanim are not diligent.)

- The reason for Rashi’s position, as mentioned above, is also stated by the Ramaz (cited in *Tosafos Anshei Shem*), the *Chiddushei Maharich*, in the sefer *Nitzotzei Ohr* (by Rabbi Reuven Margolies, may he live), and others. Seemingly, it is puzzling that Rashi did not hint at this at all in his commentary.

In my humble opinion, Rashi himself wrote his reasoning in that very place, explicitly. For what he wrote, "And the burning of fats, etc., the Sages did not say regarding it [that it must be done] by midnight at all," comes as a continuation of what he wrote previously regarding the reason for the decree of "by midnight" for *Krias Shema* and the eating of *kodshim*. His words are: "And they forbade them (*kodshim*) from being eaten before their time so that... one would not incur *kares*; and similarly regarding *Krias Shema*, to urge **the person** (seemingly, these two words are superfluous—unless to emphasize "a person," an ordinary individual) so that... and in the meantime... the time would pass (and since regarding burning after dawn there is no *kares*, and Kohanim are not just ordinary people and there is no need to urge them, it must be concluded: it is valid), and the burning of fats, etc., they did not say [it must be done by] midnight at all (not even *lechatchilah*, as they did for *Krias Shema*)." Furthermore, one can explain Rashi’s addition of "and the time would pass" precisely: because regarding burning, this is not certain, for if it remains on the top of the altar, it may be burned forever, and according to Rabbah, even if they descended, they may be brought back up (see *Zevachim* 87a) and are **not** disqualified—and it is according to his view that Rashi is speaking (in his commentary *d.h. mitzvatan*) here in the Mishnah in *Berachos* (unlike the Rambam, who rules like Rava that they are disqualified even if they are on the top of the altar).

Based on the above, it is understandable why Rashi’s laws of burning are **not** in their place (in *d.h. mitzvatan*), but rather after he explained the reason for the decree of "by midnight" for *Krias Shema*, etc., because only this compels—according to Rashi—the statement that regarding burning, the Sages did not say [it must be done by midnight], etc.

**Ibid:** A person who became tamei—is the tumah something added, or does it come about automatically due to the absence of holiness, etc.? It could be that both exist; therefore, for *terumah*, *erev shemesh* (which removes the tumah) is sufficient, while for *kodshim*, a sacrifice is also required (the drawing down of holiness).

Seemingly, one cannot say it comes about automatically, etc., for there is no tumah for a non-Jew, etc., even though they are the opposite of holiness. Rather, it can be explained that they are not **within the category** of tumah and taharah (during their lifetime).

In any case, in the matter at hand, it is explicit that even a *mechusar kapparah* still has (a faint) tumah upon him (*Zevachim* 17a and there; see there; *Keilim* ch. 1, m. 4; **and in many places**). Rather, there are several levels of tumah, and likewise of holiness, and they correspond to one another. Therefore, a *mechusar kapparah* is forbidden only in *kodshim*, while a *tovel yom* is forbidden even in *terumah*, etc. (*Keilim* there and in many places), and in *kodshim* there is a *revi'i*, unlike *terumah* where there is only a *shlishi*, etc. (*Taharos* ch. 2), and all this is from the Torah. It is worth noting the words of the Arizal in *Shaar HaKavanos* and *Pri Etz Chaim*, *Shaar HaBerachos*, ch. 3.

It is also worth noting that from there it is understood that just as there is a distinction between the holiness of *kodshim* and *terumah*, there is a distinction between the holiness of Shabbos and Yom Tov (and see *Likutei Torah*, *Tzav* 11d). See *Pesachim* (104a). It is difficult to understand *Zevachim* (91a, top of page) that Rosh Chodesh is holier than Shabbos. This can be resolved based on the citation in *Shulchan Aruch Admur HaZaken*, *Orach Chaim*, beginning of section 242, regarding Chol HaMoed, that the term *mikra kodesh* is not used for it, except that it is called such regarding sacrifices, as per Rashi’s precision in *Zevachim* that the *mussafim* of Rosh Chodesh are sanctified, etc. This requires further study, and this is not the place.

938

B"H, 2nd of Menachem Av, 5726

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, the Temimim, Sofrim Stam in Kfar Chabad, may Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your announcement of the good news that you have decided to form an association of Sofrim Stam, etc.,

May it be the will that this be at a good and successful time, and that your work in holiness—the holy work mentioned—shall achieve its holy purpose: proofread Stam, regarding which we have also been commanded separately, and especially when these Sifrei Torah are read from, the Tefillin are worn, and the Mezuzos are affixed, whereby the matter of the blessings recited before the mitzvah, etc., is increased.

And as this matter is explained in many places.

May it be the will that no stumbling block, Heaven forbid, shall emerge from your hands; may you aim for the truth and perform all that is mentioned with joy and gladness of heart.

With blessings for success and for good tidings in all of the above.

## 940

940

B"H, 7 Marcheshvan, 5726
Brooklyn.

To the distinguished Rabbi, learned in Torah, G-d-fearing, and meticulous in his deeds, etc., Rabbi Reuven, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your book, *Nitzutzei Ohr*, [containing] illuminations, notes, etc., which was delivered to me these past few days, as well as the regards from the guests from Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, whom I also asked to convey regards to you.

Many thanks for your thoughtfulness in sending me the aforementioned book, as well as your books *HaMikra VeHaMesorah*, etc., some time ago. I am certain you will continue to do so in the future, and I thank you in advance.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that for many years to come, your strength in Torah will increase, and that you will merit to succeed in publishing your Torah insights—especially since a significant portion of them consists of cross-references, citations, and analytical studies that highlight the unity within our holy Torah: it is one Torah, and since it was given by the Unique One of the world, it is certainly, even beyond that, a singular Torah.

With respect and blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

P.S.

These days, one of the renowned printers, the Shulsinger brothers, may they live—who have merited and succeeded in publishing the Torah of the *Rishonim* and *Acharonim* with both external and internal beauty and splendor, starting from the Five Books of the Torah, the Babylonian Talmud, etc., etc.—is traveling for a visit to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. They are also the printers who published the *Likutei Torah* of the Alter Rebbe, in addition to several Chassidic texts we have printed through them.

Since they have set their hearts on a good endeavor—to publish the Jerusalem Talmud together with the Babylonian Talmud, with all their commentaries, etc.—I suggested to the aforementioned that they visit you to receive your expert opinion regarding the plan for publishing the Talmud and the [Jerusalem] Talmud (Chagigah 10a) together. This is a matter that concerns the many and is for the merit of the many.

Moving from one subject to a related one: I am puzzled that in your *Nitzutzei Zohar*, you did not also include citations from the Jerusalem Talmud. If it is possible, it would certainly be worthwhile to publish them in a separate supplement, and in time, to incorporate them into a second edition of this book.

Since the aforementioned plan is for him to stay in Eretz Yisrael only for a few days, this letter is being sent as urgent/express.

**At the beginning of the book *Nitzutzei Ohr***: That the *Tanaim*, etc., are called *perushim* (commentators) — see there, for their purpose is to explain the Torah.

On the face of it, according to this, their name should be *perushim* (with a *yud*), or at least with a different vocalization than the one common in everyone's mouth. As is apparent in many places, this word was indeed vocalized this way in previous generations. And although "names are not preserved like verbs" (Ibn Ezra, Shemos 2:10), nevertheless, it should be in the same vein.

**At the end**: Regarding the text of the Kaddish (at the conclusion of a tractate), *v'li-achya*... *v'li-vnei*... *v'li-me'akar*... — this requires study, as the matters therein do not follow chronological order. See *Berachos* 49a; *Zohar* Vol. I, end of *Parshas Chayei Sarah* and 130a; *Rambam*, *Hilchos Melachim*, end of Chapter 11; and the letter of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (printed in his collection of letters). Regarding the places where you cited in your *Nitzutzei Zohar* on *Berachos* there: I saw that you cited the *Zohar* there, [referencing] the commentary *Kesem Paz*.

## 941

B"H, 8 MarCheshvan, 5726
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Cheshvan, in which you write regarding a shidduch for your son, the G-d-fearing man of fine character and many accomplishments... and you touch upon the question of the beard.

In my opinion, if the young woman in question is satisfied with your son’s—may he live and be well—merits in Torah, mitzvos, yiras shamayim, etc., and yet she withholds her consent to the shidduch because of the growing of a beard, this is proof that the matters of Torah and mitzvos are not important in her eyes. For the concern of "what will her friends say," etc., outweighs the aforementioned merits.

And if this is the state of the young woman regarding yiras shamayim, our Torah—which is a Torah of life—and the fulfillment of its mitzvos, concerning which it is said, "and he shall live by them", then it requires great deliberation whether this is a suitable shidduch, and the intelligent person will understand.

May it be the will of Hashem Yisbarach, who oversees every individual with Divine Providence, that very soon he will find a truly suitable shidduch for your son—may he live and be well—and that you will see from him much true nachas, that is, Jewish, Chassidic nachas, in addition to the nachas you already receive from his conduct and his affairs.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

**"and he shall live by them"**: Acharei Mos 18:5.

## 942

B"H, 19 Menachem Av, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh, which reached me with some delay, I am responding to the content of the matter not in the usual order, but as an urgent priority.

You write regarding the place where your son, may he live, should continue his studies.

It is surely unnecessary for me to emphasize to someone like you that since there is a definitive ruling of our Torah on this, there is no room for doubt. The instruction is explicit: "A person should always study in the place that his heart desires." Our Sages’ emphasis on this instruction is so great that it is codified as a practical halacha in Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah, end of section 240, that even if the father objects—and even if the objection is due to a concern for danger—he must nonetheless study in the place his heart desires. See there.

It is also simple that since this is an instruction of our Torah—Torah of life—it is **certainly** for the best, not only for the student but also for his parents. Furthermore, since we are speaking of the "desire of the heart," it is understood and clearly visible that it is impossible to decree upon the student, the son, that he should desire a different place. A decree can apply to an actual deed, but not to the desire and feeling of the heart.

All of the above applies even if the question had been posed some time ago. But in the present case, where the son has already been [there] for several months... and we see the situation at home, etc., it is clearly evident that the well-being and health of the parents, as well as the well-being and health of the son, dictate that he should travel as soon as possible to study in another city. According to the aforementioned ruling in the Shulchan Aruch, he must travel to the place his heart desires, especially since he has already traveled to other places—both... and...—and after all of this, his heart desires a specific place.

It is also obvious that for the good of all involved, everything mentioned should be done in ways of pleasantness and through the drawing together of hearts. Generally, "great is peace and the drawing together of hearts," and especially in a home such as yours, which is founded upon the Torah and its mitzvos, of which it is said, "Its ways are ways of pleasantness, and all its paths are peace."

In such a situation, one must demand more from the parents than from the son, for parents are more mature and have greater experience in the ways of life and the relationships within a home, etc.

Furthermore—and this is essential—the son is at an age of adolescence, meaning that by nature his nerves are more strained. Not every person merits that the brain should be master over the heart to calm the nerves completely, etc., and as a person matures, the brain becomes more master over the heart.

It is clear that I do not wish to cause alarm, G-d forbid, but I am compelled to emphasize once again that at all times, and all the more so in our current era, one must be extremely careful and vigilant regarding everything that concerns the nerves of the younger generation—the sons and daughters—when one observes, unfortunately, what is happening among the youth regarding health in general, and specifically in connection with the nerves. Therefore, the sooner everything mentioned is carried out, the better. I emphasize again that this is for the good of all details and all parties: that you and your wife, may she live, should encourage your son, may he live, in his travel to the place his heart desires, and do so as stated above, as soon as possible, etc. Surely, for people such as you, further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

It is understood that I have read with the necessary attention what you wrote regarding the goal and the arrangement of life, and the prospects for changing behavior, etc. But as stated above, this is a matter that does not depend so much on intellectual debate, but rather, as per the instruction of our Sages, on the **desire of the heart**. Added to this, in the present case, is the tension of the nerves and the relationships that are becoming increasingly strained, etc., which requires, for the sake of your wife, may she live, and for the sake of your son, may he live, that the relationships should as soon as possible change to a mode of closeness, leading up to his travel to study in the place his heart desires.

You conclude your letter by stating that, in your opinion, a third party has interfered in this. After asking your forgiveness, I do not know what the **original** cause was, but after speaking several times with your son, may he live, and after speaking with you and your wife, may she live, when you visited here, **the situation now** is as described above. That is to say, the ruling and instruction of our Torah, Torah of life, applies to it in its entirety, for at this time, even your son, may he live, could not change the desire of his heart, even if he truly wanted to.

[In writing "at this time," I mean for a year or two at least.]

My hope is strong that you and your wife, may she live, will set your hearts to what is written above regarding the instruction of our Sages, and consequently, you will arrive at the aforementioned conclusions.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, and with respect.

## 943

943

B”H, 22 MarCheshvan, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter—which was received after a long delay—in which you ask whether my response to a certain individual changes what I wrote to you in response to your question.

One response does not affect another, even if the content of the question were one hundred percent identical. For the response depends on the manner and style of the question, the nature of the questioner’s soul, and so on; in most instances, all of these factors influence the response, and this is self-understood.

Although you do not mention the following, it is my hope that from the inspiration of the days of the month of Tishrei and their themes—beginning with the acceptance of the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven on Rosh Hashanah and concluding with the joy of Torah (and its mitzvos)—you have taken [these themes] for all the days of the coming year, so that they may be permeated with the aforementioned inspiration. Indeed, all the themes of the month of Tishrei are comprehensive, intended to influence the entire year, as explained in several seforim, and there is nothing that can stand before the will.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all that has been mentioned.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

#### ***943***

**As explained in several seforim**: See also above, Letter 936, and the references noted there.

**And there is nothing that can stand before the will**: See Zohar Vol. III, 162a, 272b.

## 944

B"H, 22 Kislev, 5726
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 14 Cheshvan,

I am certain that in the meantime you have already received my response to the question posed in your aforementioned letter.

The primary reason for the delay was not, as you wrote, because of many other highly important matters; rather, the subject you wrote about concerns an "entire world" and the building of an everlasting edifice. My hope had been to receive a letter directly from your daughter, tichyeh, in accordance with the instruction of the Torah: "Let us call the young woman and ask her own opinion". For in matters that depend primarily on the heart and feelings, hearing about them from a second party—even the closest one—is not the same as hearing them from the person herself, and this is well understood. Only when I saw that, apparently, such a letter would not be forthcoming, did I respond as I did.

My hope is strong that since our conversation when you were here, you have utilized the power of our Torah in the commandment to "ascend in matters of holiness" (for the commandment of the Torah is also a bestowal of strength, and furthermore, a promise, as explained by our Alter Rebbe regarding this), meaning that you have ascended and elevated others—especially the members of your family and your students, shiyichyu (who are also called children)—in matters of the holiness of Torah and its mitzvos.

Especially since in such a case we are promised that "one who comes to purify himself is assisted", and "if a person sanctifies himself a little from below, they sanctify him greatly from above".

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 945

945

B"H, Sunday, Parshas Toldos, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the congregation of Yeshurun, lovers and cherishers of Torah and Mitzvos,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and Blessing!

It has often been emphasized that the teaching of the Alter Rebbe, the Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, is that "a Yid must live with the times"—with the Torah-time that is filled with the content and spirit of the weekly Parsha.

We are currently reading the Sedros that tell us about the lives of our Patriarchs, the first Yidden: Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov. Avraham was the father of Yishmael and Yitzchak; Yitzchak was the father of Esav and Yaakov. Yet, regarding Yaakov Avinu, it is said that "his bed was complete"—all twelve of his sons and his daughter remained faithful Yidden.

Despite the fact that Yishmael and Esav had righteous parents and fine Jewish homes, this was not a full guarantee that one would derive true Jewish *nachas* from them. For the Ribono shel Olam has granted free choice (*bechirah chofshis*).

Every person can choose their path in life: the path of life and good, or the opposite. Yishmael and Esav chose the wild, unbridled path of material worldliness; this inevitably led them to a life of "the bow" (*rovah keshes*) and "the sword" (*v'al charbecha tichyeh*), a reality that persists to this very day.

Yaakov Avinu, however, was a **yoshev ohalim**—a dweller in tents. He did not merely sit in the tents of Torah himself, but was constantly concerned that the *ahalei Torah* should have continuity and endurance. Even when he had to go down to Mitzrayim—and indeed, specifically for this reason—he first sent Yehudah to establish a Yeshiva there. He thereby achieved the result that **all** of his children remained faithful Yidden.

One might have thought: How can one, with this approach of a "yoshev ohalim," exist against the "ish sadeh" (man of the field), against the princes of Yishmael and the chieftains of Esav, when Yaakov and his household are but a small minority among them?

The holy Torah teaches us and assures us that although in all generations and all eras Yidden will be a minority among all the nations, a Yid should not be intimidated by this. As long as he maintains the path of Yaakov Avinu, the path of a "yoshev ohalim"—where the father himself has *kevius itim l'Torah* (fixed times for Torah study) and sends his children to learn in *chadrei Torah* and Yeshivos—he is assured that all his children will remain faithful Yidden, and he will derive true Jewish *nachas* from them, not only in *ruchniyus* but also, quite simply, in *gashmiyus*.

I wish to hope that in the spirit of these current weekly Sedros, all lovers of Torah and Mitzvos, and especially the *askanim* of the Yeshiva, will strengthen the preparations for the upcoming annual event of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Tmimim Lubavitch (on the 24th of Teves, may it come upon us for good), to ensure the success of the endeavor, both financially and spiritually. The Ribono shel Olam will certainly not remain a debtor, and "whoever adds, they add to him" blessing and success in *gashmiyus* and *ruchniyus* alike.

With respect and blessing for great success in all the aforementioned,

**M. Schneerson**

## 946

B"H, 26 Mar-Cheshvan, 5726

As is well known from the *Iggeres HaKodesh* of the Baal Shem Tov, this is a time-bound mitzvah: that when his wellsprings spread outward, the Master, the King Moshiach, will come.

With respect and blessing,

P.S. Enclosed is for the shipping expenses, etc.

## 948

948

[27 Menachem Av, 5726]

Regarding your question on *Likutei Torah*, end of *Parshas Kedoshim*, about engraving the Five Books of the Torah of Moshe in the memory of the mind, etc. — while it is true that "words that were written, you are not permitted to recite by heart", the prohibition applies to reciting them [as a formal reading], etc. However, it is certainly a requirement to exert effort and toil so that words of Torah are engraved in one’s memory, both the Written Torah and the Oral Torah. This is a positive commandment from the Torah (see *Hilchos Talmud Torah* by the Alter Rebbe, Chapter 2, sections 3-4).

#### ***948***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 14, p. 237.

**Words that were written, you are not permitted to recite by heart**: *Gittin* 60b, and references cited there. *Tur Shulchan Aruch* and *Shulchan Aruch HaRav*, *Orach Chaim*, section 49.

Nevertheless, if it has already been published, I would be grateful to you if you would include this as well in future shipments.

With respect, blessing, and thanks in advance for the above.

951

A

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Kislev, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished individual, a person of noble character, scion of a noble lineage, R' Schneur Zalman, shlita,

In the spirit of the month of Kislev, which we have entered today, the essence of which—especially for Chassidim and anash, shlita—is the significance of the 19th of Kislev, the 10th of Kislev, and the days of Chanukah, the common denominator of which is mesiras nefesh for the dissemination of "the candle of mitzvah and the light of Torah"—and the light of the oil that shone in a miraculous manner—and their shared point is "may your springs spread outward" in a manner of "spreading forth, increasing, and continuing to increase in light"—

Most importantly, one can see with physical eyes how the promise of the Alter Rebbe (Tanya, end of Chapter 37) is being fulfilled, to the extent that it has been brought into practical halachah in Hilchos Talmud Torah, Chapter 4, end of Halachah 3, that "no one shall be cast away from Him"—literally, in the simplest sense. This means that even those who were "cast away" in the fullest sense of the word and were at the furthest possible distance are being brought close (and now—through the influence of Chabad) in a tight bond, even to the point of a literal revival and a complete transformation in their daily lives.

## 53

5th of Kislev, 5726
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individuals involved in communal affairs,
R’ Binyamin Gershman and R’ Shalom Shkliar

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Kislev, written in your capacity as administrators of the Nusach Ari Shul in Albany Park, Chicago, regarding the study of Maamarei Chassidus in your Shul in general, and specifically during the time of Shalosh Seudos on Shabbos Kodesh, you ask for my opinion on the matter.

As explained in many places by our Rebbes, the greatness of the mission to spread the wellsprings of the teachings of Chassidus wherever a Jew may be found—and especially in a place where many Jews gather, such as a Shul—is self-evident. This is all the more true in a place whose very name bears witness to this, as your Shul is called "Nusach Ari."

In the words of Rabbeinu HaZaken, the Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch: "In these final generations, it is permitted and a mitzvah to reveal this wisdom" (Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 26).

Thus, the importance of this endeavor and the great merit it affords to everyone who participates in it—by engaging in it personally and by influencing friends and acquaintances to do the same—is clear. As the instruction and the adage go: "In the multitude of people is the King’s glory." This is especially and particularly true when it concerns Shabbos Kodesh during the time of Shalosh Seudos, for that is the time of *Reva D'Revin* (the Will of Wills). Regarding this and similar matters, the promise of our Sages holds true: "One who comes to purify himself is assisted."

And in response to your second point:

Having known the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R’ Yaakov HaKohen Katz—a man of fine character—for many years, and knowing the merit he had to personally hear many Maamarim and Sichos Kodesh from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and his devotion to him, as well as the blessings he was privileged to receive, it is understood that when he repeats a Maamar or Sicha, the teaching of our Sages can be fulfilled during the repetition: "It is as if the speaker is standing before him." This adds to the success of the presentation and to the impact that is expected.

"Merit is brought about through a meritorious day." Your letter was written on Rosh Chodesh Kislev, the month of miracles and redemption, and this response will arrive close to the 10th and 19th of Kislev, the days of redemption of Rabbeinu HaZaken and his son and successor, the Mitteler Rebbe.

They are the ones who advocate for every Jew, especially for those who study the teachings of Chassidus and spread them—those who sacrificed themselves for the sake of the teachings of Chassidus, even to the point of actual *mesiras nefesh*, as the history of these days of their redemption is well known.

With respect and regards to all those who participate in the aforementioned Chassidus class, as well as to all the congregants of the Shul, them and their households, may they be well. With blessings for good tidings in all of the above.

## 957

B"H, 14 Kislev, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and accomplished, R' Nissan, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 21 Cheshvan, which arrived on 11 Kislev. May it be the will [of Hashem] that you bring us good tidings, and that darkness be transformed into light and bitterness into sweetness.

## 958

958

B"H, 16 Kislev, 5726
Brooklyn.

To the avreich... may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter of 11 Kislev, requesting a blessing—a *pidyon nefesh*.

Since we have been promised, "You have labored and you have found," you should study *nigleh* and Chassidus with *hasmadah* and *shekidah*, to the point that the Torah calls it "labor," and the study will lead to action—the fulfillment of *mitzvos* with *hiddur*. Then the promise will be fulfilled: "and you have found" (this also applies to the refinement of the heart and the mind-intellect, although the verse states: "Little by little I will drive them out from before you").

With blessings for good tidings regarding the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

S.M. Simpson – Secretary

It is a well-known instruction of the Rebbe Rayatz: Just as it is a person's duty to know their shortcomings, **so too** must they know their virtues. *V'kal l'havin*.

## 965

B"H, Days of Chanukah, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished, G-d-fearing and upright, R' Chaim, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

Through the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing and upright, engaged in communal needs, R' Menachem Shmuel Dovid HaLevi Raitshik, the shaliach, your pidyon nefesh was received, which will be read at the tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. Together with this, the check was received, with the amount left open so that I might determine the sum as I see fit.

In accordance with this month, which is the month of miracles, and these days, which are days of miracles, salvations, and wonders, it is appropriate to set the sum—as your initial contribution to tzedakah, which is equal to all the mitzvos—at three thousand dollars ($3,000).

And since our Sages, of blessed memory, have said that a mitzvah is performed better by oneself than by one's agent, and the giving of tzedakah must be done specifically with joy and a glad heart, the check is enclosed so that you may fill it out in your own handwriting, and as mentioned, with joy and a glad heart, and then return it.

Regarding the matter at hand, enclosed is a copy of a sicha concerning tzedakah and the festival days of this month. May it be G-d's will that the conclusion of the aforementioned sicha be fulfilled in you: "Test Me now with this... tithe, so that you may become wealthy."

With blessings for health and success in the matters contained within the pidyon nefesh, and in your commitment to increase in tzedakah, going from strength to strength, in accordance with the instructions of these days of Chanukah, which increase from day to day, and with blessings for good tidings in all that was mentioned.

## 956

B"H, the fifth night of Chanukah, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chassid, who is involved in communal needs, etc., R' Schneur Zalman, may he live—the Rav of Kfar Chabad, in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established.

Greetings and blessings!

Strange and bizarre rumors have reached me regarding what is being conveyed in my name concerning the elections for the village committee, etc. Initially, I said that I would pay no attention to any of this, since I have said and **warned** **many times** that one should not rely at all on what is said in my name regarding Kfar Chabad. For if I wish to express my opinion, I am able to communicate it in writing, in a direct manner. This is especially true in a matter that concerns the many, where, at the same time, many individual interests are involved—such that it is often not easy to find someone who is not personally affected by one of the aforementioned matters and, consequently, would not be biased.

Nevertheless, since I have recently been inundated with letters from many people—naturally and obviously containing contradictory rumors, each one relying specifically on me, claiming that this is my desire and my decision and that it cannot be otherwise—

I have therefore come once again, and it is my hope that this notice will suffice for the future as well, to reiterate what was written above: do not rely **at all** on oral rumors. Whatever I wish to communicate, I will do so in writing, and no one has any authorization to say in my name that the residents of the village or the committee, etc., must act in one way or another, except for explicit instructions that are provided in writing and signed by me.

Regarding the content of the above, this letter is being sent as a rapid, urgent communication, addressed to the Rav of the village, so that he may deliver and publicize it in the appropriate manner and with the authority of the Rav.

As we find ourselves in the days of Chanukah, the mitzvah of which is to increase in light from day to day—and not only within one’s own four cubits, but rather, specifically at the entrance of one’s house from the outside, and specifically in the public thoroughfare (and not only in the courtyard)—may the light of Chassidus and its Torah, which our Rebbes, our leaders, have bequeathed to us, illuminate the path of each and every resident of the village within the entirety of the community of Chassidim. May they see the truth, that the true path is only the path of the King, the King of the world, illuminated by the light of Torah—which is the Torah of Chassidus. Its foundations are love of Hashem, love of the Torah, and love of a fellow Jew. Consequently, hearts will draw closer until all are as one, and all will unite in the principle that "the deed is the essential thing." In the present case, this means the stabilization of the village and its development in all matters, both material and spiritual, and in the matters that the time calls for—the specific and general construction projects. For this purpose, the drawing together of hearts is essential, and it is obvious that one should **not** stir up divisiveness, quarrels, agitation, and revolutions, etc. Rather, one should strengthen, stabilize, and develop all matters through increased cooperation, combining all the active forces within Kfar Chabad. Surely, even those who have been active until now will, from here on, act and consult in the appropriate manner with those who are suitable for such consultations (even if, until now, this consultation was not as complete as it should have been). It is self-evident that anyone who has the ability to assist, advise, and act for the benefit of the village and its affairs should not take into account petty calculations, matters of imagined honor, and other temptations [the sources of which are impure, and therefore have no place within the four cubits of Bnei Yisrael in general, and among Chassidim in particular]. This is especially true during the days of Chanukah, the nature of which is to "extinguish the foot of the Tarmodites," and even to achieve redemption from the straits of the affairs of Kfar Chabad in a manner of peace, for "in the multitude of people, they were with me."

With blessings for a Chanukah that illuminates and increases in light, and in a manner that the light will be drawn out for the entire year—a "mitzvah candle and Torah light," and the light of the Torah, which is the inner dimension of the Torah and the Torah of Chassidus,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. For the aforementioned reason, please be kind enough to confirm receipt of this letter at your earliest convenience. Many thanks in advance.

## 968

[4 Teves 5726]

Many thanks, many thanks for the good news. May it continue to be good news, and may it reach the highest level of good news, where there are students to the students of [the original] students (which is apparently the meaning of **"his students were forgotten"** [Tosefta Eduyos at the end], and as in Berachos at the end of the first chapter: "The latter ones cause the former ones to be forgotten." And one should not corrupt all the printed editions and manuscripts). The reason for this, one could say, is because from this point forward, there is no need [for the granting of strength—by calling upon the name of the Rebbe—to be a Rebbe or a student, because the Torah (in this manner and level) returns to its rightful place (three generations of a Rebbe).

***

968

From a photocopy of the Rebbe’s handwritten note—on the margin of a letter from the heads of the Yeshiva, Rabbi Y.Y. Piekarski and Rabbi M. Mentlik, in which they reported on the students’ examinations.

**"His students were forgotten"**: (Meaning that there are already students to his students, and if so, his students are "forgotten")—they call him "Rabban." "These and those were forgotten" (meaning that there are already students to the students of his students), etc.

**And one should not corrupt all the printed editions and manuscripts**: See Chasdei Dovid on the Tosefta there: "It is possible that a scribal error occurred here, and instead of 'forgotten' (nishtakchu), it should say 'ordained' (nismachu), etc."

**"The Torah... returns to its rightful place"**: Bava Metzia 85a.

## 6959

B"H, 13 Teves, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Yitzchak Meir, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

Your letter, along with its enclosure, was received after some delay. It is understood that I agree with your honor regarding the content of your letter.

Allow me to add a remark, which I hope you will not take offense at: I am surprised by your bewilderment regarding the conduct of the organizations to which you wrote to express your reaction, for *kam lei b’darbei minei* (he is already familiar with his own ways). What I mean to say is this: since there is an organization whose name testifies and emphasizes that it is a religious organization—such as the Synagogue Council and the like—then every one of the members who participates in it and becomes a part of it is officially acknowledging, before the public, the religious authority of the members of said organization. This is at the very same time that individuals are included in this organization whom the Rambam enumerates in his Hilchos Teshuvah (Chapter 3, Halacha 7 and onwards). Furthermore, if the aforementioned organization was missing that type [of person] with whom the Rambam begins—the one who says there is no G-d—we have recently "merited" that this type, too, has joined and been accepted into the aforementioned organization. Yet, despite this, they continue to be members of said organization; so what significance is there in giving an award to Dr. So-and-so, etc.?

With respect and blessings.

Incidentally, it is worth noting what occurred at one of the meetings of the executive committee of the organization to which your honor wrote your reaction. Although I was not present at that meeting, I heard about it from a source who is trustworthy, and it is this: one of those present proposed a motion that, since it has recently come to light that among the Reform rabbis there are those who say there is no G-d, it is imperative that they at least withdraw now from the aforementioned organization. Of all those gathered, there was not a single person who voted in favor of this motion. And to the wise, a word is sufficient.

## 770

B"H, 13 Teves, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Schneur Zalman
Shy'

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the auspicious day of 19 Kislev and thereafter, and I thank you for your thoughtfulness in informing me of your participation in the farbrengen of 19 Kislev in Kfar Chabad. May it be His will, as you write, that the hisorerus should bring forth fruit throughout the entire year in each and every one of the participants.

And if in the past it might have been possible to wonder what changes could be expected from a single meeting once a year, in our times we see that something small in quantity, if only it is great in quality, can bring about great and hidden things.

And if this is true regarding destruction, then all the more so regarding building.

It is also well known to be precise in the phrasing "your springs shall spread outward" regarding the springs of Chassidus and its influence, for in many springs we see that they begin as mere drops, and afterwards they spread into a mighty river that overflows all its banks.

With respect and blessing.

## 71

B"H, 18 Teves, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the 26th annual dinner
of Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei-Temimim Lubavitch,
May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom u’vracha!

This year’s dinner takes place on the yahrtzeit-hilula of the Alter Rebbe, Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, the founder of the Chabad-Lubavitch movement. One of the primary hallmarks of Chabad-Lubavitch is the emphasis placed on chinuch, which finds expression in broad-reaching, mesiras-nefesh activity in this field. This is a tradition that stems from the Baal Shem Tov, the founder of Chassidus, who began his chinuch activity even before he was revealed, by becoming a melamed for young children. His devotion and love for these little children knew no bounds. His successor, the famous Maggid of Mezritch, wished that he could feel the same love when kissing a Sefer Torah as the Baal Shem Tov felt when he kissed a young child!

This tradition was continued by the Maggid of Mezritch’s student and successor, the Alter Rebbe, and all the Nesi’ei Chabad until the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, who transplanted the Lubavitcher yeshivos onto American soil.

Since this year marks the 100th yahrtzeit-hilula of the Tzemach Tzedek, it is fitting to specifically mention his approach to chinuch, as illustrated by the following story:

The Tzemach Tzedek was, as is known, a giant among the Torah giants of his time—a world-renowned authority in halacha, a gaon in Chassidus and Kabbalah, as his vast and numerous seforim testify. Furthermore, he was the leader of the generation, who was invited multiple times by the government in St. Petersburg for consultations regarding the Jewish situation during that critical time. Nevertheless, he would tear himself away from his own studies and writings and from all his responsibilities in order to **personally** examine his young grandchildren once a month, when he would also give them monetary gifts as a token of appreciation.

These stories—the fact that they are recounted to us is a sign that they are relevant to each and every one of us—teach us how far mesiras-nefesh for chinuch al taharas hakodesh must reach: not only in the easier forms of mesiras-nefesh, such as contributions of money and personal effort, but even in the more difficult form of mesiras-nefesh, when one must tear oneself away from one’s own Torah study and other communal matters, which, however important they may be, are still less important than the matter of chinuch al taharas hakodesh.

Therefore, it is to be hoped that all friends of the Lubavitcher yeshivos and lovers of Torah and mitzvos in general will make special efforts to ensure the success of this annual undertaking in all respects. In return, the Ribono shel Olam will bless each and every one with everything they need, both in gashmius and in ruchnius alike.

With respect and blessing for outstanding success and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 976

[23 Teves 5726]

In response to your questions:

1) Since the child for whom you provided a bris certificate is an *asufi* (a foundling), it is possible that his mother is not Jewish (and consequently, neither is he). The certificate could therefore be misleading, etc. Therefore, you should correspond as soon as possible with one of the elder *poskim* to seek his guidance on how to proceed in such a case.

2) You should continue in the craft of *milah* (though you must verify the identity of the mother in every instance), and the merit of bringing the children of *Bnei Yisrael* into the covenant of our father Avraham will stand by you.

Written on the margin of the letter from Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Shemos 5726.

## 9178

B"H, 24 Teves, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Y. Goldschmidt, Director of the Department of Religious Education

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 7 Teves, along with the materials enclosed—reading sheets, booklets, etc., regarding Rabbeinu HaZaken, the founder of the Chabad movement—for the students of the schools.

It is surely superfluous to emphasize the great value of the matter itself, which is connected with disseminating the fundamental values of Torah and Yiddishkeit, especially among the youth, for any positive influence upon them while they are young brings forth fruit and fruit of fruit throughout all the days of their lives. Therefore, there is no need for me to express thanks for the great deed you have performed, for the reward of a mitzvah is the mitzvah itself. However, my thanks are due to you for your thoughtfulness and effort in sending me all the material; thank you very much.

May it be His will that you see good fruit from your labor in general, and from your labor in the aforementioned matter in particular, such that the students of the various classes who read and study this material regarding the pride and glory of Israel, the personality and Torah of Rabbeinu HaZaken, will find it to be study that leads to action—conduct founded upon love of Hashem, love of Torah, and love of Israel, permeated with the light and vitality of Chassidus, uniting both the heart and the mind.

Following the conversation we had, the memory of which is of course kept by me, there is certainly no need to elaborate on the great value of the points mentioned and their implications. And merit is brought about through a meritorious day, for today is the yahrtzeit-hilula of Rabbeinu HaZaken.

In continuation of the above matter, allow me to enclose a copy of a general letter for Rosh Hashanah in connection with the Shmittah year of this year. I would also like to draw your attention—though it has surely already been brought to your knowledge—that this year is the 100th anniversary of the passing of the grandson (and successor) of Admur HaZaken, known by the name of his books as Admur the Tzemach Tzedek.

With heartfelt thanks for the above, and with respect and blessings.

## 879

B"H, 25 Teves, 5726
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 18 Teves.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires for the good.

Regarding what you wrote about the young woman you have met and the relationship between you, etc.:

If the person in question observes mitzvos in her daily life—meaning, her conduct in daily life conforms to the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of life, and the fulfillment of its mitzvos, of which it is said, "and he shall live by them"—you should add a name to the person in question (in addition to her current name). This addition should be made according to the instruction of a Rav—that is, when reciting the *Mi Sheberach* when called to the Torah, etc. Both of you, you and the young woman, should resolve to establish your home upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, as stated regarding the conduct of your daily lives mentioned above, and marry according to the law of Moshe and Yisrael.

May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all of the above.

It is appropriate that you have your *tefillin* checked, and that every weekday, before putting them on, you set aside a few coins for *tzedakah*. Likewise, ensure that the *mezuzos* in your apartment are checked to ensure they are all *kosher* according to the law.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S. According to what is explained in the *poskim*, when one person has two names (a double name) and the other has only one name, there is no room for the concern you wrote about, whatsoever.

## 890

B"H, 25 Teves, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings,

Your letter was received with a very significant delay, and the response from my side has also been delayed due to an abundance of preoccupations; I ask for your forgiveness.

In your letter, you write that Chabad should hold a seminar for teachers among the yeshiva students, and you write the reasons for this and the great necessity of the matter.

Although I agree with most of your reasons, nevertheless—with apologies—for several reasons, some of which I believe you will find acceptable, I am compelled to say that this is not a Chabad matter, even though regarding the essence of the issue, there is no one who disagrees that it is most necessary.

For if there were a surplus of manpower in general, and in Chabad in particular, and all the matters that cannot be accomplished by others but only by Chabad were already completed and done, then perhaps there would be room to discuss the aforementioned matter. But to our regret, there is a very great shortage of manpower in all the Chareidi movements, including the Chabad movement. Therefore, priority must be given to those matters that obligate the people of Chabad first and foremost, where, despite their dedication to their tasks and their avodah, the work is still great and must be increased and expanded. On the other hand, regarding another activity whose necessity everyone admits and which many are capable of carrying out, I believe that Chabad has no justification—according to fairness, and primarily according to Torah—to involve itself in it. We have before us an explicit sugya (Moed Katan 9, end of a and beginning of b), and the conclusion of the Gemara is that regarding a mitzvah that can be performed by others, the study of Torah is in the category of "all desires cannot compare to it," and the Gemara does not make a distinction between one mitzvah and several mitzvos, or the type of mitzvah. This is not the case regarding a mitzvah that cannot be performed by others, where even a minor mitzvah has priority and must be performed. And surely for one such as yourself, further elaboration is unnecessary.

This is the basis for my position in this matter: that even though the matter of teaching and chinuch is always among the most vital—and all the more so in our generation and in our Holy Land, etc.—it is impossible to push aside a mitzvah that cannot be performed by others, even a small mitzvah.

With respect and blessings,

Based on our meeting and our correspondence, I will take the liberty of expressing my hope that you will mark the auspicious day of 19 Kislev, the details of which—the imprisonment and the redemption—are surely known to you.

#### ***890***

**All desires cannot compare to it**: Mishlei 8:11.

## 883

[6 Shevat 5726]

From this, it is understood: 1) that this is not a *gezeiras hakasuv* (a scriptural decree beyond logical explanation), and 2) that nevertheless, it is possible to derive the death of the owner from the death of the ox (even though, on the face of it, this is deriving *dinei mamonos*—monetary laws—from *dinei nefashos*—capital laws). The *sevara* (logical reasoning) for this is so simple that even Rashi and Tosafos (and not only the Gemara itself) did not find it necessary to spell it out, due to its extreme simplicity. It can be explained simply: the *sevara* is straightforward and understood from the verse itself, "The ox shall be stoned, and also its owner shall be put to death"—meaning, when we judge the ox, it is not merely a matter of *dinei mamonos* as in the rest of the Torah, but rather, "also its owner shall be put to death" (by the hands of Heaven, as is stated in *Kesuvos* and brought simply in Tosafos, *s.v. eima* in *Sanhedrin* 15a: meaning that even according to the *sugya* in *Sanhedrin*, he is put to death by the hands of Heaven if he does not pay the *kofer*).

One may add an explanation for this: the reason for the owner’s punishment can be explained in two ways: a) because he (the **owner**) failed to guard his ox, and it killed (and therefore there is no *kofer* for a *tam*), or b) because his **property** (his ox) killed.

According to the first way, one could say that the owner’s sin and the death caused by the ox are sequential, like any cause and effect. According to the second way, **at the moment** the ox kills, **then** the owner sins (similar to the principle that one’s courtyard is considered his hand). (Based on this, there is a practical legal difference—if he sold the ox on the condition that if the ox kills, the sale takes effect immediately, before the killing.)

The language of the Gemara (*Sanhedrin* 15b), "You do not execute him for the murder of his ox," can be explained according to both ways: According to the first way, because at the moment of the murder, the cause (the **owner**) is no longer present, only the ox. According to the second way, because the **entire** matter of the murder is solely that of the **ox**, and the owner’s entire connection is only in that it is "his ox." Now, if we say it is like the second way, it is more understandable that one cannot separate the discussion regarding the ox from the precision regarding "its owner," since the sin of both is in **one** action.

It can be said that the second way is more compelling:

a) According to the first way, why is there a verse regarding a *tam* that the owner of the ox is clean, and Rabbi Yehuda ben Beseira explains "clean" as being clean from the hands of Heaven—for it is obvious, what could he have done in the case of a *tam*? (It can be said that his colleagues, the Sages, disagree with Rabbi Yehuda ben Beseira on this.)

b) According to the opinion of the Rogatchover (see *Tzafnas Paneach* to *Sanhedrin* 15b), it is mentioned everywhere in the Gemara there (and not as mentioned above).

Now, seemingly, one could say that the Yerushalmi disagrees with the Bavli (which does not mention a *gezeiras hakasuv* in this matter), for it **explains** that it is a **gezeiras hakasuv** that the ox be stoned (*Perek* 1, *Halacha* 2 and *Halacha* 3), and especially according to the *Pnei Moshe* in the Yerushalmi, that it is a **gezeiras hakasuv** that it be stoned **by a Beis Din of twenty-three, like the death of the owner**. But I have not merited to understand the explanation of the *Pnei Moshe*—for if so, the main point (that its death is by twenty-three) is missing from the Yerushalmi! Furthermore, according to his explanation, the fact that the ox is stoned is not even a secondary matter; what is the practical difference for his question there? (And in this vein, his explanation is not understood, for according to this, "money" means that it is judged by three [judges].)

In my humble opinion, the explanation of the Yerushalmi is according to its simple meaning: the ox that is to be stoned is entirely *mammon* (property)—and *mammon* throughout the entire Torah is "penalized" by paying full *mammon* as well. However, here it is a **gezeiras hakasuv** that this **mammon** is also penalized by being stoned (in addition to the giving of money by the owner of the *mammon*). If so, there is no distinction between the *mammon* (which causes the stoning) and the *mammon* (which causes the giving of money). Based on this, the language of the Yerushalmi, "The ox that is to be stoned is **entirely** *mammon*," is sweetened, and *kal v'chomer*.

Yet, it is still *tzarich iyun* (requires further study) that even this *gezeiras hakasuv* is not mentioned in the Bavli. It can be said that each follows their own approach. The Bavli explains (as above) that "also its owner shall be put to death" [means] by the hands of Heaven. (If so: 1) It is not **entirely** *mammon*—for according to this, "entirely" would have to include the owner as well. 2) The question of **Rabbi Ami** in the Yerushalmi: "What is the law regarding him giving money before a Beis Din of three?" would not exist, since the money comes as a result of the death by the hands of Heaven.) In our *sugya* in the Yerushalmi, it can be said that they hold that the *halacha* overrides the verse here (as explained in *Aderes Eliyahu* to *Mishpatim*), **and as it is stated** (*Perek* 1, *Halacha* 2), "Its owner shall be put to death, etc.—a partner of thieves is like a thief, etc. He said to him, you have pushed me off **with a straw**, etc. He said to him, just as the death of the owner, so too, etc."—and *duk* (examine closely), there is no death here at all, and it is entirely *mammon*.

One could elaborate on all this, but this is not the place.

***

It occurred to me, seemingly, to explain the matter of the death of the ox being like the death of the owner (even though this is *dinei mamonos* and that is *dinei nefashos*):

1) According to the *Mechilta* of *Shemos Rabbah*, brought in the *Ramban* (*Beshalach* 17:3) (a matter with a reason, not a *gezeiras hakasuv*), that a person's livestock is his **life**, and this is *halacha* and not *aggadah* (see *Shulchan Aruch Admur HaZaken*, *Orach Chaim* 248:13, from the *Magen Avraham* there). (And it is not difficult from the many laws of his ox that are not like the laws of *nefashos*—for in the verse of the *Mechilta* it is: "**To kill**... your livestock," the **death** of the ox specifically)—but this is not so, for if so, it should also be like *dinei nefashos* regarding the laws of the death of his ox when he handed it over to guardians, and the like.

2) Like the words of the *Rashba* to *Bava Kamma* 112a—if we interpret them according to their simple meaning (as brought in the attached letter), that the death of the ox—**from its own perspective**—is considered like the death of the owner (and not because it is the life of the owner, as above in the *Mechilta*). But according to this, it is a *gezeiras hakasuv* like no other and unlike any other. There is no *sevara* for this, that **only** the law of twenty-three applies to the ox to be stoned, and not the other ten things that apply in *dinei nefashos* (*Sanhedrin* 36b).

In particular, it is *tzarich iyun* according to this, regarding the language of Rashi there, *s.v. lo*: "The *hekkesh* (analogy) comes for the core of the law and its beginning, etc. Why should we have mercy on an ox, etc." Such a back-and-forth belongs to a matter of *sevara* and not a *gezeiras hakasuv* (and especially a *gezeiras hakasuv* like the above—which is the opposite of the *sevara*). Therefore, I explained that the death of the ox is *dinei nefashos* because then "also its owner shall be put to death," and not from its own perspective (as in my writings from before), and the *Rashba* can also be explained this way.
