## 987

987

B.H., the day after the Hilula of 10 Shevat, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished bochur, who seeks the good of his people, a man of noble character, scion of a noble lineage, R' Schneur Zalman, shlita,

Shalom u’vracha!

Under the impression of the Hilula of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, which you surely also marked, one naturally connects with everything related to the master of the Hilula and his concerns, and through this, with our fellow Jews who are still "on the other side." While immersed in this thought, toward the end of the farbrengen, someone approached me and handed me a letter he had received from his brother in the capital city there, stating that the gates are opening wide—or in the writer’s words: "everyone is being let out."

May it be the will of the Ribono shel Olam that our heart’s desires be fulfilled for the good in general, and especially the yearning of all Yisrael: that our brethren who are in distress and captivity emerge very soon from the straits into the expanse, both literally and in every sense.

As is customary during a farbrengen, and especially when some who have recently arrived from there are present, those gathered participate in saying l’chaim, accompanied by blessings from the depths of the heart for our fellow Jews who are still there, and for the "blossoms that have already appeared in the land"—the residents of Kfar Chabad. However, at this Hilula farbrengen, I took the liberty of suggesting that we say the l’chaim in reverse order, prioritizing a "second Kfar Chabad" before the "first Kfar Chabad." May it be the will of Hashem that these desires and aspirations of the heart also be realized in actuality and very soon: that a second Kfar Chabad be established in a suitable place—a place in the literal sense, meaning in the vicinity and proximity of the existing Kfar Chabad, which is necessary for many reasons; and a place suitable in the spiritual sense, where the way of life will be Chassidic life, daily life illuminated by the light and vitality of the teachings of Chassidus, its concepts, and its guidance.

And surely, all those who took part—and especially those who took an active part—in the founding of the first Kfar Chabad will merit to participate in the joy of the founding of the second Kfar Chabad and its completion, to the point that it will be with expansion and spreading out, in accordance with the well-known and famous slogan of late: "westward and eastward and northward and southward."

With appreciation, honor, and a blessing for good tidings—in health, joy, and goodness of heart,

**M. Schneerson**

By the Grace of Hashem, 11 Shevat, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed...
Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated...

We have just emerged from the tenth of Shevat, the day of the histalkus and hilula of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, whose holy resting place you will mention.

In the words of the baal hilula: "The heroes of Yisrael, the protectors of the land—even when they return their souls to the bosom of their Father in Heaven, to Whom they return their souls (Midrash Rabbah, Bereishis, beginning of ch. 1)—not only do they not separate from their flock, but they further prostrate themselves before the footstool of the Throne on High, to stand before the glory of the exalted and uplifted G-d, to defend the people of Yeshurun (see Midrash Rabbah, Bereishis, ch. 44:5), and to demand the mercies and kindnesses of the Father for His son, His people, and His inheritance."

**M. Schneerson**

* * *

Regarding your questions about participating in the administration, etc.—I have already written about this, and for now, it is a private matter.

* * *

Volume two of the Shulchan Aruch of the Alter Rebbe was received in due time. Many thanks.

* * *

Regarding your writing on the printing of your Chiddushei Torah concerning gittin, agunos, etc.—in general, the matter is correct for many reasons. However, since such matters fundamentally belong to the Rabbis and those who issue halachic rulings, you should consult with them.

Regarding the note in Likutei Torah, Shelach (42b) concerning a niddah and zavah in "living waters"—this is the opinion of many of the Geonim, and it is mentioned in the Zohar (Vol. III, 97b) and Tikkunei Zohar (end of Tikkun 50). Some of these sources are cited in my notes to Likutei Torah there (printed in the 5725 edition of Likutei Torah).

Regarding your note in Likutei Torah, Naso (29b) that a voluntary mincha offering is brought in an Egyptian basket, which contradicts the explicit statement in Sotah (14b) that it is disqualified—it is explicitly stated there that the reason is "Present it now to your governor, etc.," and this prohibition is not from the Torah (see Kesef Mishneh, Hilchos Issurei Mizbe'ach, ch. 2, halacha 10; and unlike the view of some of the Acharonim that it is forbidden by Torah law—for according to that, it would be incomprehensible how the poor bring bikkurim in wicker baskets made of willow (Bikkurim, ch. 3, mishna 4), which are certainly inferior to palm-leaf baskets (i.e., an Egyptian basket, as Rashi explains in Sotah there), for the logic of "Present it now" applies even to that which is not offered directly upon the Altar. And this requires further study).

Your letter regarding the above was received. Regarding your responsa on the laws of agunos—it is worthwhile that you first see the sefer Otzar HaPoskim on Even HaEzer, siman 17 (published in Jerusalem), and complete your responsa accordingly, and thereafter, publish them with success.

* * *

Your letter of the 13th of Shevat and its enclosure were received.

The question of why it is easy to kindle fire now, yet it is forbidden on Shabbos, etc.—the explanation is simple: the "Act of Hashem, etc." was even easier (speech, Hashem, Who is Ein Sof), and from this "He rested and was refreshed."

* * *

With blessings for good tidings (including, of course, the appearance—speedily in our days—of the volumes following the 11th volume of the Talmudic Encyclopedia) in good health.

Is the trip—a visit to Nepal—truly necessary?

* * *

In response to your question—the custom in Yisrael is that during the festival of Pesach, a man and his household are together (and in his home), especially the head of the family. Furthermore, it is extremely difficult to be mehader as one desires in matters of Pesach when one is in a different place. And this is well understood.

I enjoyed reading the excerpt from your letter—your essay regarding Shmittah. May Hashem grant you success in the days to come as well.

* * *

It is obvious that the question of housing does not hinder shidduchim.

* * *

In response to your question—it is understood that you must complete your studies. May Hashem grant you success.

* * *

In response to your notes: a) Regarding the sugya in Berachos (32a, bottom), see the Reshimot of the Tzemach Tzedek on Eichah on the verse "Remember, Hashem." b) The public announcement regarding the reading of the Torah—it is understood that it is worthwhile to publicize it in a place appropriate to local conditions, for it was given to be publicized. c) Regarding a visit to the Ohel—propose the matter to three friends and act according to their decision.

909

11 Shevat, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. Nechama
Shichyih

Blessings and Peace!

I acknowledge with pleasure the receipt of your letter of January 29th, in addition to the satisfaction I felt upon receiving greetings from the esteemed Rabbi Shlomo Aharon Kazarnovsky, whom I had asked to convey to you my thoughts regarding the founding of "Beis Nechama." It gave me great joy to hear from him with what warmth you accepted this mission, and your readiness to ensure that "Beis Nechama" will be kosher as it ought to be. This strengthens the hope that the children who will be raised there will be kosher Jews, which provides the true assurance that they will also be good Jews and good people, in every sense of the word.

It is superfluous to emphasize that if such an obligation is required regarding **every** Jewish child, wherever they may be and in whatever conditions they may grow up, it is of special importance regarding children who find themselves in a land that even non-Jews call the "Holy Land." Furthermore, we are dealing here with Jewish children whose young lives, due to various circumstances, have unfortunately not been entirely free of worry and difficulty, as childhood years should be. All of this increases the merit and pleasure of all those who take part in shaping and educating these children in the proper way. At the same time, it increases their responsibility for this; but the Ribono shel Olam ensures that a person who has increased responsibility should be provided with increased capabilities, in order to be able to fulfill all obligations to the fullest extent, and—as with all things connected to the Ribono shel Olam—to fulfill them in a good spirit, with joy and enthusiasm.

I take the liberty of adding one more point: If everything written above applies especially to the institutions and organizations that are named after you, or after your close ones—where the responsibility is clear and explicit, and as mentioned, the merit is entirely yours—it is also valid regarding all those institutions where you can have an influence. Hearing from various sides about the regard for you in different circles in Eretz Yisrael, your influence is very strong, much stronger and much more widespread than you imagine. Thus, any suggestion from you in the aforementioned direction will certainly be accepted, even in such circles where, according to their outlook, this might perhaps be news.

Standing on the day after the Yahrtzeit of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulh"h, nbg"m, zi"e*, it is timely to recall and appreciate his content-rich life path, and especially to emphasize the leitmotif and golden thread that runs throughout his entire life. The lesson from this is that even a single individual, if they stand with the greatest strength for a true ideal, receives immense capabilities to overcome difficulties that, at first glance, appear to be entirely impossible. It is true, indeed, that he possessed extraordinary strengths that are very rare to find in people, as is known to all who followed his life and were personally acquainted with him. On the other hand, however, the difficulties that one encounters now are incomparably smaller than those he encountered in his work.

Wishing you all the best, and that you may be able to report good news about yourself and about those you mentioned in your letter, as well as regarding the content of my letter as written above,

With blessing.

## 991

B"H, 13 Shevat, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, a bochur of the people and elevated above the people, who seeks the good of his people, a man of lofty character, a scion of noble ancestors, R' Schneur Zalman, shlita,

Peace and blessing!

Following my letter to Mrs. Scheuer, tichyeh, it occurred to me that it would be worthwhile to send you a copy of the letter, as it will surely be of interest to you, etc. However, upon reviewing the letter again (and specifically the "lines between the lines"), I saw that the body and essence of the letter (though certainly not its style, etc.) should be directed to you—and it is obvious and simple—regarding many matters, and indeed the entirety of the matter, up to the "essence" (for the essence does not change).

And also—a "part and portion" of it, as is brought in Chassidus in many places that the Baal Shem Tov said: The essence—when you grasp a part of it, you grasp the whole of it.

And the essence of Eretz Yisrael, its matters, and those who stand at its head—and especially the individual who stands at its head as a unique and singular individual—is as our Sages, of blessed memory, have informed us: *Eretz* (land)—that it *ratzah* (wanted/ran—as explained by the Tzemach Tzedek) to do the will of its Creator; *Yisrael*—for you have struggled (*sarisa*) with Elokim and with men, and you have prevailed (*tuchal*).

And the seal is in the word and concept—*tuchal* (you shall prevail).

May it be the will of Hashem that all this be with joy and goodness of heart.

With appreciation, honor, and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

As stated above, this is written based on the "freedom of speech (and writing)" that you granted me in several of your letters, and primarily—from the impression of the day of the Hillula and in continuation of my letter of 11 Shevat.

## 902

13 Shevat, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Board of the "Gemilus Chasadim Shomrei Shabbos" Society, Brooklyn, may they live:

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the Society’s annual report and the news regarding the gathering for the benefit of the Gemach fund.

May it be the will of Hashem that you have great success in all your activities, and in a positive manner—in a way that is good, both revealed and manifest—for the Society and for the recipients.

As we stand in the days close to the day of the passing, the Hillula, of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the Nasi of our generation, and this year being the centennial year of the passing, the Hillula, of the Tzemach Tzedek—may his merit shield us—it is appropriate to contemplate the content and the lesson of the story told by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the Tzemach Tzedek, concerning the matter of Gemilus Chasadim. The story is as follows:

The Tzemach Tzedek was accustomed to seeing his grandfather, the Alter Rebbe, after his passing, whether while awake or in a vision of the night, and he would resolve for him all his doubts in both the revealed and the hidden aspects of Torah.

At a certain time, while the Tzemach Tzedek was sitting in his room, immersed in his studies, several questions accumulated for which he could not find a resolution. He longed greatly to see his grandfather, the Alter Rebbe, as was his custom, but he did not succeed, and he was in great distress over this.

One morning, the Tzemach Tzedek went to pray at the shul of his father-in-law, the Mitteler Rebbe—may his merit shield us. As he was passing through the marketplace, he encountered one of the townspeople, a man named R' Mordechai Eli, a simple, G-d-fearing man who earned his living through trade in the market. Since it was market day, the man asked the Tzemach Tzedek to lend him a small Gemach loan until the evening or the next morning, as he could earn a profit in the market that day. The Tzemach Tzedek replied that after prayer, when he returned home, he would stop by and give him the Gemach loan.

When the Tzemach Tzedek entered the shul, the teaching of Rabbi Elazar came to his mind: "One who gives a coin to a pauper is blessed with six blessings, but one who comforts him with words is blessed with eleven," and also the teaching, "Gemilus Chasadim is greater than Tzedakah." The Tzemach Tzedek reflected that he had not acted properly by not giving the Gemach loan to the aforementioned R' Mordechai Eli immediately. He returned home, took the sum, and went to the market to search for him. In the meantime, the villagers had already gathered with their wagons and merchandise, and it was with great effort that he managed to find him among them. When he found him, he gave him the Gemach loan and returned to the shul to pray.

When the Tzemach Tzedek wrapped himself in his tallis and tefillin, he suddenly saw the Alter Rebbe with a radiant face. He said to him: "One who gives a Gemach loan to a fellow Jew with a complete heart, without any ulterior motive, and who does a favor for a Jew with love, as commanded in 'Love your neighbor as yourself,' the gates of the heavenly chambers are opened before him."

End of quote.

***

The stories of the Nesi'im of Israel are a lesson for all who walk the straight path that they have taught, within the entirety of the Jewish people. It is a lesson and a teaching of life—a lesson for life in this world and for life in the World to Come, as the Sages said in their Mishnah: "Gemilus Chasadim is something whose fruits a person enjoys in this world, while the principal remains for the World to Come."

With respect and with blessings for success in the aforementioned,

**M. Schneerson**

Enclosed is my contribution, G-d willing.

## 934

934

B"H, 15 Shevat, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the attorney, Mr. Yehuda Dick, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

By instruction of the Rebbe, I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter of 10 Shevat, along with the proposal for a new law regarding the matter of *shechita*. Thank you for your attention to this.

Regarding the matter itself, and without entering into the details of the proposal: it is well known that the absolute opinion of the Rebbe is that since the manner of preparation for *shechita* is also part of the *shechita* process, just as there is no place for any government office to deliberate—and certainly not to legislate—anything concerning the laws of *shechita*, so too there is no place for a government office to deliberate or legislate regarding the methods of preparation for *shechita*, as this constitutes an **infringement upon the freedom of religion in this country**.

And it is irrelevant here whether the intentions are desirable, or even if the text of the proposal contains no contradiction to the laws of the *Shulchan Aruch*. What is important here is the fundamental principle that the government has no right or authority to interfere in the religious domain of any minority. Therefore, the very act of deliberation by an organization or government office in the sphere of religion is **fundamentally flawed**, and it is not for the government to decide in instances where there are differences of opinion between rabbis regarding any religious matter whatsoever.

With respect and blessing,

Secretary

## 998

B"H, Erev Shabbos, Shabbos Kodesh Mevarchim Chodesh Adar,
Brooklyn, N.Y.
Parshas Shekalim, 5726
- The centennial year of the histalkus and hillula of the Tzemach Tzedek -

To the annual banquet of the Ladies Auxiliary of Brownsville and East New York for the Lubavitcher Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim

Shalom u’vracha!

I send my greetings and blessing to all the participants in this annual banquet. An undertaking by women, and for such an important cause, deserves the greatest success, and may the Ribono shel Olam help that this success be in all respects, both financially and spiritually.

Included in this is that the members of the Ladies Auxiliary should themselves properly appreciate their meaningful work, and serve as an example and inspiration for others.

Since this event is taking place before Rosh Chodesh Adar, and the focal point of this month is Purim, it is worthwhile to mention once again that although both Mordechai and Esther brought about the Divine salvation and the miracle of Purim, the Megillah is named specifically after Esther herself. Through this, the Torah Hakdosha emphasizes the important role of the Jewish woman—not only in connection with Purim itself, but in all difficult and critical times, including the present time.

And although the "Haman" of the present time and in this country has a different appearance than in the days of Mordechai and Esther, he is essentially the same "Amalek" who seeks to cool off and tear Jews away from Torah and mitzvos, and who wants Jews to bow down to his avodah-zarah—to everything that is **foreign** to the Jewish spirit and the Jewish way of life.

The only way to combat the Haman and the avodah-zarah of the present time is the old, well-trodden, and certain path that also nullified all the decrees of Haman HaRasha: to strengthen chinuch al-taharas-hakodesh, to expand the yeshivos and mosdos chinuch of Torah with yiras-shamayim, which instill in Jewish children an unlimited love for Torah and mitzvos, even to the point of literal mesiras-nefesh, as in the time of Mordechai and Esther in Shushan HaBirah.

The Torah Hakdosha emphasizes—by the fact that the Megillah of Purim bears specifically Esther’s name—that in all fateful times, the responsibility, and along with it the zechus, of the Jewish woman is not "second-rate," chas v'shalom, but rather, on the contrary, it is just as great, and in certain respects even greater, than even the responsibility and zechus of her husband.

May Hashem Yisbarach bring success to your work and bless you and your families, shichyu, in everything you need, both materially and spiritually, with joy and goodness of heart, in an ever-increasing measure.

With blessings for success, for good tidings, and a Purim Sameach,

**M. Schneerson**

## 999

B"H, 2 Adar, 5726
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished Rabbi Nissan, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 1 Shevat, as well as your book, *Nitzanei Nissan*.

May it be the will of Hashem that He fulfill the requests of your heart for the good, that you may succeed in strengthening kashrus in our camp and in every place that your reach extends, and to influence others in this as well.

This is especially true according to what is explained in many places: that one of the reasons for the kashrus of foods is that non-kosher food "clogs" the heart and the mind, etc. From this, it is understood that strengthening the matter of kashrus touches upon the entire Torah and its mitzvos, and this is simple to understand.

And from one matter to a related matter: from the kashrus of the body’s food to the kashrus of the soul’s food—the good opinions and their opposite. That is, that the *mochin* in the head should be filled with the *Chabad* of Torah, the wisdom of Hashem and His understanding, etc., and to give birth from them to good *midos* in one’s heart. Upon this depends a person’s conduct in the study of Torah and the fulfillment of its mitzvos, even to the point of fulfilling what is written: "In all your ways, know Him."

According to this, the obligation upon each and every one to disseminate the teachings of Chassidus Chabad is understood all the more—until it reaches even that which, for the time being, is still "outside."

With respect and blessing.

## 9100

B.H., 7 Adar, 5726
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I confirm receipt of your letter, in which you also write regarding your state of health and the improvement therein.

May it be the will of Hashem that there be a complete recovery, and may this complete recovery come soon. This includes the matter of sadness that you mention; for a healthy Yid is, by definition, a joyous Yid.

Especially as we find ourselves in the month of Adar, regarding which we have been instructed since the first of the month, "increase in joy." An instruction from Torah surely implies that the Giver of the Torah first provides the ability to fulfill His instruction, and also provides reasons so that one can see that the instruction has a strong foundation. Surely, it is unnecessary for me to elaborate on this to you.

Regarding your writing about kosher means to achieve a kosher goal:

It is **well-known** that a thing which is the opposite of kosher (or simply, *treif*) cannot be used for the sake of a mitzvah. As Chazal call this, "a mitzvah that comes through a transgression," and they express themselves very sharply regarding this.

There is, however, another matter (which is sometimes conflated with the former), and that is the utilization of means which, in and of themselves, one would not choose to do, but in order to influence another and bring them to a good thing—Torah and mitzvos—one "overlooks" one's own preference.

For example: A *bochur* in yeshiva could utilize his Shabbos (when the yeshiva schedule does not obligate him) to learn for himself, *nigleh* and *Chassidus*, and do so in tranquility at home or in shul. Instead, he travels somewhere far away, where there is no thought of *oneg Shabbos* and sometimes not even of *menuchas Shabbos*. He utilizes his Shabbos to influence a Yid who knows nothing about Shabbos at all, or knows nothing about Yiddishkeit, and one must begin with him by teaching the *aleph-beis* of Shabbos or the *aleph-beis* of Yiddishkeit—things that the *bochur* absorbed and received directly in his home with simplicity (with certainty and without doubt). For the sake of this other Yid, he sacrifices his own (spiritual) *oneg Shabbos* in order to save a Yid from a transgression punishable by *skilah*, *r"l*, or to learn Torah with him, and the like.

Regarding this, the ruling of the Gemara (see *Maseches Bava Metzia*, 85a) is that this is not only greater than learning in the yeshiva here, but even greater than learning in the *Yeshiva Shel Maalah*.

With blessings for good health, a good mood, and *simcha*, and for a joyous Purim.

## 921

B"H, 7 Adar, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter in which you write regarding your daughter, may she live, and the young man she has met, etc.

I delayed my response, thinking that perhaps the situation would become clearer in the meantime, as the letter was missing several important details. Among the most essential is: is the young man more mature in his intellect and character than his years would suggest? For age is not the determining factor regarding a stable life; rather, it is the strength of one’s judgment, the uprightness of one’s intellect, and so on. Regarding a Jewish man and woman, one of the most essential matters is that they be traditional Jews in their day-to-day lives, for this is the path to a life that is happy and blessed by Hashem, the Giver of the Torah and the Commander of the mitzvos.

Although I have not received further details regarding the aforementioned, since your letter received just now mentions your letter regarding your daughter, may she live, once again, I do not wish to delay the response any longer.

My opinion on your question is that to act with forceful opposition is, on the face of it, not the right path—even if one feels the need to oppose. In our times, forceful opposition from parents immediately triggers a contrary reaction (even if the children in question are good children, etc.), since they interpret such opposition as an attempt to impose authority and force the opinions of the "elders" upon "juniors" who are still in need of guidance, etc. In other words, it is perceived as an affront to their sense of independence.

Regarding opposition in an appropriate manner, in my opinion, the deciding factor is what was mentioned above: whether his conduct in day-to-day life conforms to the tradition of our ancestors—that is, whether it conforms to our Torah, the Torah of life, and its mitzvos, of which it is said, "and he shall live by them." Another important point, though it does not compare in importance to the previous one, is the aforementioned point regarding whether he is more mature than his years.

May it be the will of Hashem—who oversees each and every one with Divine Providence—that you see much true nachas from your daughter, including a good shidduch for her, one that is good in both material and spiritual respects alike.

Especially since we have entered the month of Adar, in which we are commanded to increase in joy, and a command from Hashem also provides the strength and the circumstances that will lead to that joy.

With respect and blessings for good tidings in all the above, and for a happy Purim.

P.S. My heartfelt thanks for the information in your letter of 20 Shevat. Although you were brief and concise regarding your efforts on behalf of Chabad at the gathering you write about and prior to it, I have received additional information from anash, may they live, regarding the "quantity" of your efforts, and even more so regarding the "quality" of your efforts—and in particular, the grace and vitality within them.

***

**"of which it is said, 'and he shall live by them'":** Acharei Mos 18:5.

**"in which we are commanded to increase in joy":** Taanis 29b; Magen Avraham, Orach Chaim, end of 686.

## 903

B"H, 7 Adar, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

I extend my heartfelt thanks for your efforts and for your constant and consistent assistance in all matters concerning Kfar Chabad, and especially its development—a development that I hope will be not only in length and breadth, but also in depth and height, including as the concepts of depth, length, and breadth are explained at the beginning of **Shaar HaYichud** by the Mitteler Rebbe—the very book of which the Nesi'ei Chabad said that it is "the key to the Torah of Chassidus."

And the hand of Hashem will not be shortened, and the salvation of Hashem is in the blink of an eye. In the style of the Torah of Chassidus, the heartfelt wishes of every Jew require a fundamental addition: that all of this should be in a revealed and manifest good, in an abundance of joy, and like the upcoming days of Purim, which are "v'nahafoch hu" (it was turned around), and "the Jews had light and joy, etc.," and "no verse loses its literal meaning."

Indeed, the superiority of the days of Purim over the days of Chanukah is that the joy of Purim is the joy of the body and the soul together.

Moving from one subject to another in the same vein, a mitzvah that they accepted upon themselves with joy is the bringing of your brother's grandson into the covenant of Avraham Avinu. His name in Israel is Chaim Vital. In the traditional style, may it be the will of Hashem that just as they have brought him into the covenant of Avraham Avinu, so may they bring him to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds.

Regarding the conclusion of your letter, the trip to the country in the high mountains*, may it be with success and for the sanctification of the Name of Heaven and the sanctification of the Name of Israel, and may your return—your ascent—be in a good and auspicious time, with joy and gladness of heart.

With appreciation, honor, and blessings for good tidings and a happy Purim,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. I read with interest your letter regarding the invitation of the individuals who head the Chabad activity on college campuses. Incidentally, Prof. Rosenblum, who visited the Holy Land last summer and also visited you, is one of them. In my opinion, the first person worthy of the aforementioned invitation, as I know him among the others, is Prof. Dr. Velvel Green, who is in Minneapolis, Minnesota. His aforementioned name also testifies to him, for he is called—by his own wish—"Velvel" by all.

## 926

926

B"H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Zachor, 5726

## 1008

B"H, Shushan Purim, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the 24th Annual Banquet of the "Netzivei HaYeshiva" supporters of Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch in Montreal, may Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

Since the annual banquet is taking place this year a few days after Purim, it is to be hoped that the participants will be under the fresh impression of this meaningful Yom Tov, which emphasizes that among Yidden, every remembrance is connected with action (**"are remembered and performed"**). Purim reminds us of a time when Yidden were in galus, yet under liberal and friendly rulers, beginning with Koresh, King of Persia, who granted the exiled Yidden in the Babylonian galus freedom and independence to a great extent. Also under Achashverosh, they enjoyed freedom in their religious, economic, and political life, under the spiritual leadership of Mordechai HaTzaddik, a member of the Sanhedrin and a prominent figure in the royal palace (**"sitting at the king's gate"**). Mordechai never forgot that he hailed from Yerushalayim, and that he was in galus (**"who had been exiled from Yerushalayim"** etc.). However, there were Yidden who wanted to forget Yerushalayim and the Beis HaMikdash, and considered it an honor and a stroke of luck to participate in the *treife* royal banquet, and this led to the decree of Haman the Wicked.

Mordechai knew that the way to destroy Haman's decree was by strengthening and expanding the Torah-true chinuch of the Jewish children.

Our Sages, of blessed memory, tell us that Mordechai gathered many thousands of children and studied Torah with them—with such enthusiasm that they were prepared to go together with Mordechai to perform Kiddush Hashem, and this nullified all the decrees of Haman the Wicked.

And even after the great victory, when Mordechai was appointed in Haman's place as **Mishneh LaMelech** (viceroy) and his fame reached all the provinces, he was always and everywhere known as **"Mordechai HaYehudi"**—"Mordechai the **Jew**"—because he always and everywhere conducted himself as a proud Torah-Jew, and this was his entire reality, his true "self."

The story of Purim is a clear directive for all times and circumstances.

Mordechai and Esther are living models for Yidden, men and women, in all generations, including our own time. And the miracle of Purim is an eternal reminder that Torah-true chinuch of Jewish children is the secret and foundation of the existence and future of the Jewish people.

Under the impression of the aforementioned fundamental ideas of Purim, it is hoped that each and every one of the participants will surely better appreciate the vital work of the Lubavitcher Yeshiva in Montreal and will identify more closely with the chinuch activity of this great Torah institution, which has earned such far-reaching merits.

I send my greetings to all the distinguished guests and participants, with the heartfelt blessing that the event be carried out with great success in all respects. May the merit of *hafotzas haTorah v'hamitzvos* ensure that all matters, both communal and personal, be in a manner of **"increasing in joy,"** in both gashmius and ruchnius together.

With respect and blessing for success and good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 919

B”H, 16 Adar, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

And may we proceed from redemption to redemption; for from the redemption of Purim—since we are still the servants of Achashverosh—we shall, after (in the words of the verse) "a small moment," emerge in our time from servitude to freedom and to a "great light," in the true and complete redemption through Mashiach Tzidkeinu.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S.

## 911

B"H, 16 Adar, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

- The Year of Seven, the Year of Shemitah -
To the Avreich, whose work is the work of Heaven...

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

As we stand on the day after the days of Purim—days of light, gladness, joy, and honor—your *pidyon nefesh* will be read at the holy resting place.

With blessings.

Regarding your writing that several concepts in the teachings of Chassidus are new to you—everyone goes through this "stage." Ultimately, this serves to stimulate interest, in accordance with the expression of Chazal (and their exposition): "They should be in your eyes as new." It is obvious that it is strange and forbidden to say that the matter is "foreign" to you—for **every day** we recite the blessing, "He gave us His Torah," and it is one complete Torah.

**The Year of Shemitah:** One of Haman’s accusations was that "their laws are different"—meaning that they observe the *Shevi'i* (Targum Sheni; Agadas Esther).

**The day after the days of Purim:** It is worth noting the *Megillah* (2a) regarding the 16th and 17th, which have a special connection to the days of Purim, as they are subject to the law of "it shall not pass" (*lo ya'avor*). (One could argue that after this time, the law of "it shall not pass" no longer applies, as its prohibition is similar to the prohibition of *bal tosif*, which exists only during its designated time. However, this requires further study in the *Mordechai* at the beginning of *Megillah* and in *Bigdei Yesha* there.)

According to the *Yerushalmi* (ibid.), the entire month is subject to "it shall not pass." (One could explain that this means it does not apply after the month. Based on this, the language of the *Yerushalmi* is easily understood: "The entire month is valid for the reading of the *Megillah*. What is the reason? 'And the month which was turned...' Rabbi Chelbo said: 'Only until the 15th...' and 'it shall not pass'—meaning it does not return from the *entire month* being valid, etc. (since it derives this from the verses). Rather, it is like a lion crouching over it—the prohibition of 'it shall not pass.' But this is not the place to elaborate.) Additionally, regarding the 16th—when the 15th falls on Shabbos, those in walled cities hold the feast on the 16th (*Shulchan Aruch*, *Orach Chaim* 688:6).

## 9121

B"H, 9 Nissan, 5726
Brooklyn.

Mrs. Miriam
Tichyeh

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter of Friday, 6 Nissan, in which you write regarding accepting a position as a kindergarten teacher in the holy community of Zurich, and the problems associated with it.

It is true that there is a great responsibility in the education of the children of Israel, for regarding each and every one of them it is said, "You are children to Hashem your G-d." However, the Ribono shel Olam desired to create His world such that everyone is in need of education, and all the more so the children of the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, for "a wild ass of a man is born." The Torah was not given to the ministering angels, and this includes the mitzvah of education, which is part of our Torah—the Torah of life. From this it is understood that along with the responsibility, the strength is granted from Above to fulfill this responsible role, provided that a person dedicates themselves to its fulfillment with all their heart. For "he who comes to purify himself is assisted," and especially because the merit of the many—the students—assists her.

Performing this in light of the above, with joy and a glad heart, as every mitzvah must be performed, adds to Hashem’s blessing and success.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

It is the way of the world, and in the life of every person, that from time to time there are problems. In cases of doubt regarding their resolution, one should act according to the verse: "In the multitude of counselors there is salvation," among friends in your surroundings.

## 9122

By the Grace of Hashem
11 Nissan, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

—The year of the centennial of the histalkus hilula of the Rebbe, the Tzemach Tzedek—

To the sons and daughters of Israel, everywhere,
May Hashem protect them and grant them life,

Peace and Blessing!

The Yom Tov of Pesach is named after the **Korban Pesach**, which prepared, brought about, and (it is understood from this) expressed the content of a primary and all-encompassing event in the life of the Jewish people: **Yetzias Mitzrayim** and **Zman Cheiruseinu**—the total exodus from **Mitzrayim** and the attainment of **our** freedom. The Torah specifies the details and the minute particulars of how the Korban Pesach must be prepared, how it must be offered, and how it must be eaten.

I will pause here to discuss one of these details—and what can be learned from it.

***

The Korban Pesach—a lamb, which was the idol of Mitzrayim—the Jews had to make into a **Pesach l’Hashem**, slaughtering it and then roasting it over fire—**rosho al kera’av v’al kirbo**—"its head, its legs, and its innards together."

Everything, from the highest part—the head—down to the lowest-ranking details—the legs of the idol—and even those things that serve only as a means to sustain and "feed" the idol (the head through the legs), must be nullified. It is made into a Pesach l’Hashem, *rosho al kera’av v’al kirbo*, and all of it is roasted with the same fire.

The rejection of avodah zarah must be **complete**, in **all** details. If one truly does not serve the "head" of the avodah zarah—if its wisdom and intellect do not exist for him—but he still bows to its "legs" because ("**Mitzrayim**" claims that) they trample and rule over everything and everyone, he loses himself and bows to the means that the avodah zarah utilizes.

So too with the person himself: there is the avodah zarah of "rosho"—he makes his own head and his limited intellect the highest and final authority; the avodah zarah of the lower things within him, down to his "kera’av"—the desire for power, to rule, to trample, and to crush everything around him; down to bowing and making an idol of his "kirbo"—his food and livelihood, for the sake of which he will stop at nothing.

For all of this, the rule applies: a *mashehu* (a tiny bit) of avodah zarah is an entire avodah zarah.

And just as it is with Yetzias Mitzrayim (and the exodus from the abominations of Mitzrayim), so too with our **cheirus**, our liberation and the concept of liberation, which consists of becoming **avdai**—servants of the Almighty. The mesiras nefesh-filled decision to be a Jew does not allow for measurements or distinctions: more mesiras nefesh when it comes to the "legs," and less when it comes to the "head"—to matters of the head that he insists on understanding with his own intellect. Rather, *Pesach hu l’Hashem*—when *rosho al kera’av v’al kirbo*—everything is encompassed by the same fire, a fire that burns through, through and through.

***

In these days of preparation for Pesach—13 Nissan—this year marks the 100th yahrtzeit of the histalkus hilula of the Rebbe, the Tzemach Tzedek. A model of **shleimus** in the aforementioned concept—the fire of mesiras nefesh that permeates a Jew, *rosho al kera’av v’al kirbo*, **all the days** of the entire year—can be seen in the Rebbe, the Tzemach Tzedek. He united within himself the highest levels of tzaddik, gaon, chocker, mekubal, posek, and leader of Israel. Just as his gaonus reached into every corner of Torah, nigleh and nistar—in peshat, remez, derush, and sod—so too was his leadership of the community and the individual in all matters, both gashmius and ruchnius: from the most vital matters for Klal Yisrael, down to the very "lowly" details of a single individual; from spreading agriculture among Jews and securing the proper concessions from the government, to providing a Jew with a loan; from safeguarding and strengthening Torah education for Klal Yisrael in Russia, to providing a melamed for a single individual.

And all of this he did with a fire of mesiras nefesh, with all his kochos hanefesh and with everything he possessed—doing so both for the collective and for the individual.

And although who can compare himself to the Rebbe, the Tzemach Tzedek, the true tzaddik and leader of Israel has the quality to shine, to illuminate, and to bestow kochos upon everyone who wishes to walk in his ways, just as the massive sun reflects and makes bright and luminous a small drop of water—if only the drop of water is pure and clear and turned toward the sun.

***

May it be the will of the Ribono shel Olam that the hisorerus of the days of Pesach—and following the example of the Baal HaHilula—should influence every man and woman in the spirit of Yetzias Mitzrayim and Zman Cheiruseinu, that we should be freed from all obstacles and limitations (Mitzrayim and gevulim), both internal and external, and be *avdai Hashem*—serving the Almighty in true freedom.

And through this, also hasten the Geulah Amitis v’Hashleima through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, and the fulfillment of the request: "And we will eat there from the sacrifices and from the Pesach offerings."

With the blessing of a kosher and happy Chag HaPesach,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 9123

B"H, 11 Nissan, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Generator Committee, may they live – Attn:
The esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and dedicated to communal needs, R' Meir Tzvi, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter of the 6th of Nissan, and thank you for the good news contained therein.

In anticipation of the festival of Matzos, the time of our freedom, which is approaching for us and for all of Israel for the good, I hereby express my blessing for a kosher and joyous holiday and for true freedom—freedom from material worries and from spiritual worries—from everything that hinders the avodah of Hashem with joy and a good heart.

And may this freedom and joy be continued throughout all the days of the year.

Especially since the avodah of Hashem, as we are commanded in our Torah, the Torah of life, encompasses all of a person’s affairs and extends throughout the entire day and night, as it is said, "In all your ways, know Him."

Enclosed with the letter is [the requested item].

With blessings for great success in your most exalted endeavor, and with holiday blessings to each and every one of you and your families, may they live.

**M. Schneerson**

***

Regarding the above, your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Shemini was received. In response to your questions:

1) The possibility of *simcha shel mitzvah* even in the mitzvah of *teshuvah*—see Tanya, Chapter 31 (and elsewhere) regarding "not to mix or confuse the joy of the soul with the sadness of the body." If so, all mitzvos are **equal** in this regard. The **advantage** of the joy of the mitzvah of *teshuvah* over the joy of other mitzvos is based on what is discussed there: "And there is no joy greater than leaving the exile, etc."—which is the **essence** of the mitzvah of *teshuvah*, unlike other good deeds. The **incomparable advantage** of the joy of other mitzvos—immediately upon contemplating that *teshuvah* is incomparably higher than other mitzvos (for it is a **halachic ruling that a completely wicked person who contemplates teshuvah is immediately rendered a completely righteous person**), and consequently, its joy is as well. And this is not the place to elaborate.

2) It is simple that he should (also) put on *tefillin* of Rabbeinu Tam. See *Shaar HaKollel* (on the *Siddur*), end of Chapter 11, where he discusses this at some length.

3) Regarding the place of their residence after the wedding, may it be in a good and auspicious hour—based on your letters—Bnei Brak takes precedence.

***

Regarding your writing about paying attention (*simas-levav*) to your wife, may she live, that such and such actions were (and are being) taken, etc.—you are certainly correct in your calculation from your own perspective. However, in this matter, an additional and primary point is: this *simas-levav* (with two *beis*s) has a **special** importance for her as a form of medicine (for both the soul and the body together), and therefore it is measured by a medical standard specifically (in addition to the fact that matters of the heart and measurement generally do not align so well). And surely for someone like you, elaborating on this is superfluous.

May the Healer of all flesh, who performs wonders, send a complete and speedy recovery to your wife, may she live.

***

It is simple that your plans are good—and if only you would finally find a listening ear among *anash*, may they live, in the Holy City of Tel Aviv. But it is simple (and even more so) that a lack of activity by others, at least for the time being, **increases** your own responsibility (and your merit), and the *koch* in this must be even greater—the **opposite** of the conclusion in your letter!

The mailing was delayed, and regarding the above, your letter of 11 Nissan and the enclosure (clippings of newspapers—his articles) were received. Thank you for the *nachas*.

## 924

B"H, 13 Nissan, 5726
Brooklyn

To Mrs. [Name], may she live:

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter and the *pidyon nefesh* dated 30/3.

At a *eis ratzon*, it will be read at the *tziyun hakadosh* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach,

On behalf of the Rebbe,
Secretary

P.S.

In response to your question regarding the fact that recent events in your family are incomprehensible, etc.:

As has been discussed on several occasions, it is no wonder at all if a person does not understand the conduct of Hashem Yisborach. On the contrary, it would be a wonder—a very great one—if one *did* understand. As is the well-known analogy: it is like a child still in kindergarten attempting to grasp and comprehend the reasoning behind the laws of the land by which the country is governed, or the rulings issued by the highest court of the land (the tribunal), and so on.

Even if that child were a prodigy, such a thing has never happened in history—even though the current leaders of the country and the highest judges of the land were also once at the age of a child in kindergarten, and in time, that child may perhaps grow and advance in knowledge and experience more than the current elders. How, then, can one make such a comparison when it concerns a human being, versus Hashem Yisborach—that a human intellect should be capable of grasping and comprehending the conduct of the Highest Court over everything and everyone, the Creator of the world? Hopefully, there is no need to add anything further to what has been written above.

There are only certain things that Hashem Yisborach has willed, revealed, and arranged in such a way that the human intellect *is* able to comprehend and grasp His conduct.

It should also be added that the more one relies on pure *emunah* and *bitachon* in Hashem Yisborach, the more one begins to see and understand with one's intellect the events in the world in general, and in one's individual life in particular.

May Hashem Yisborach bless you with everything you need, and among the primary things, true *menuchas hanefesh* (inner tranquility and harmony). May things settle in your life in the best possible way for you in all respects, leading to *tov hanireh vehanigleh* (good that is visible and revealed—good that is also understandable to the human intellect).

And daily conduct in accordance with the instructions of our holy Torah—which is called *Toras Chaim*, a living Torah that shows one how to live—is the path and the vessel to receive the blessings of Hashem Yisborach.

## 925

[Text of the telegram for 13 Nissan, 5726]

Blessings for a Chassidic farbrengen in honor of the centennial hilula of the Tzemach Tzedek, and a kosher and happy Pesach.

**Menachem Schneerson**

[Secretariat Letter - Regarding the Centennial Year]

The Administration of "Keren HaMeah"

The purpose of the fund: To publish the seforim and writings of the Tzemach Tzedek, and to disseminate the study of his Torah in both nigleh and Chassidus.

- Founded in the centennial year of his passing -
(5626 - 5726)

B"H, 8 Nissan, 5726
- The centennial year of the passing of the Tzemach Tzedek -
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the honorable Chabad organizations and institutions everywhere,
May Hashem keep them alive,

Shalom u’vracha!

Following the proposal of the Rebbe shlita — and in continuation of the campaign for "Keren HaMeah" as explained in the sicha of Shabbos Parshas Re’eh, Rosh Chodesh Elul 5725 —

In order to provide the opportunity for every one of the Chabad organizations and institutions, their administration, members, supporters, etc., to merit a special privilege on the very day of the hilula of the Tzemach Tzedek, 13 Nissan 5726, which is the centennial year of his passing:

We hereby grant you authorization to accept, **as our shluchim**, single banknotes (one dollar, one lira, etc.) of your local currency and to designate them for the following purpose:

Each person affiliated with your institution (supporters, administration, etc.) may, **during the twenty-four-hour period of the day of the hilula**, purchase from you (acting as our shluchim) **one** banknote (and no more) from the aforementioned notes, at a price of no less than "double" (i.e., twice the value of the note) as a contribution to **Keren HaMeah**.

Through this, one participates in his activities. And the more one increases this contribution, the more praiseworthy it is, as is obvious and simple.

However, **there is no point** (**and on the contrary — it is the opposite of the intention**) for one person to purchase more than one note.

Students of the institutions Tomchei Temimim, Toras Emes, Achei Temimim, Ohalei Yosef Yitzchak, Beis Rivkah, Beis Chana, Ohalei Torah, and Torah institutions in general — who wish to purchase notes as stated above — shall pay no more than "double." [Those who wish to add to this should do so through the study of the Torah of the baal hilula.]

All those who purchase the aforementioned notes do so **on the condition** that all those involved in Torah study will study, during the twenty-four-hour period of the day of the hilula, from the Torah of the baal hilula — at least one topic in nigleh and one topic in Chassidus. [Women — in topics appropriate according to the instruction of the Alter Rebbe in Hilchos Talmud Torah, Chapter 1, Halacha 13, at the end.]

Anyone who has purchased a note, or for whom a note was purchased, and thus has more than one note in their possession, should certainly return the excess (and receive the value back), for as stated above, **there is no merit** in this surplus. **On the contrary** — if they do not return it, they do not possess even one note that is certainly from Keren HaMeah. And this is understood.

Those who wish to do so should submit their names (including the mother’s name), and they will be mentioned at the Ohel of the Rebbe (Rayatz) (the successor of the baal hilula).

**The entire matter of the aforementioned shlichus is valid only until the end of the twenty-four-hour period of 13 Nissan 5726.**

* * *

The administration of the institution, etc., shall deposit all the money (after deducting expenses) and the lists of names to the administration of Keren HaMeah (in the USA and Canada — send the above to the central Keren HaMeah administration) or to our representative for this matter (as noted in the margin) **during the twenty-four-hour period of the day of the hilula**, and in any event — **before the holiday of Pesach**.

Our Sages have said: One does not divert funds from one charity to another, and the Children of Israel do not commit an injustice even in such a case. In many matters, they also ruled out even temporary loans from charity funds. **And in this case, too, it is the same.** **And with greater force**, because since the entire matter is done as a **shlichus** from the administration of "Keren HaMeah," if one deviates from this (through a loan or similar means), the shlichus is nullified from the outset, and the aforementioned has no validity or substance. And this is understood.

With respect and blessings for success in strengthening and expanding the institutions,
And with blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach,

**The Administration of "Keren HaMeah"**

Regarding the aforementioned proposal of the Rebbe shlita, he emphasized that, of course, this is in addition to each person’s participation in an appropriate farbrengen during the twenty-four-hour period of the day of the hilula.

#### 925

Printed in the Haggadah Shel Pesach with Likutei Taamim, Minhagim, and Beurim (Kehot Publication Society, Vol. 2, p. 851).

**Secretariat Letter**: On Motzaei Shabbos, the eve of 13 Nissan, there was a special farbrengen in which the Rebbe mentioned the letter before us:

"You have surely read the letter sent by 'Keren HaMeah' regarding participation in 'Keren HaMeah.' If it is appropriate throughout the year, it is certainly so on the day of the hilula itself, which is a time of ascent—what is called an ascent according to the teachings of Chassidus, and in general, an incomparable ascent... The details are explained at length in the letter, and I have only come to remark, add, and emphasize that if all mitzvos must be performed with joy and a good heart, how much more so a mitzvah that involves a financial loss—and on the contrary, a significant financial loss, for one must give in a way that 'the more one increases, the more praiseworthy it is.' If so, the joy and good heart must be with greater intensity and strength. And Hashem is certain to fulfill the promise, 'Test Me now in this,' that through this, one will 'become wealthy' in spirituality, and 'in order that you may become wealthy' in materiality... If so, let the beginning be with a joyous nigun, and then the giving should be with joy, and then the giving will also be in a manner that 'breaks through boundaries' (poratz geder)."

**In the sicha of Shabbos Parshas Re’eh, Rosh Chodesh Elul 5725**: Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 7, p. 288 and onwards.

**One does not divert funds from one charity to another**: Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah 259.

## 9131

B"H, 1 Iyar, 5726
Brooklyn.

Mr. Yaakov
Shy'

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 27 Nissan.

It is surprising that you write with questions to overseas, at a time when you could have turned to the Chabad Rabbonim and the heads of Chabad yeshivos in Eretz Yisrael itself, without any extra trouble, and they would have clarified your doubts and questions for you.

In any event, since you have already written, I will answer, at least briefly.

Regarding your question about the text of the davening — we follow the custom as printed in the Siddur Tehillas Hashem, which is also published in Eretz Yisrael. There, in *Emes V'Yatziv*, the word *ve'emunaso* appears without parentheses, meaning that it is recited.

Regarding the word *al* at the end of Hallel — our custom is to omit the word *al*, and we say *yehalelucha... kol ma'asecha*, as per the emendation of the Tzemach Tzedek in his Siddur.

Regarding standing during the reading of the Torah — see the emendation of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe (the Rebbe Rashab), in the Siddur Tehillas Hashem.

Regarding standing during Krias Shema — there are various customs in this regard, and you should clarify this with a Rav who is a *moreh hora'ah* in your community.

Regarding the method of learning Chassidus with your brother, shy' — since this depends on several details, and not every person is the same, you should consult with the *mashpi'im* of Chassidus at Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim regarding this.

Since you have written repeatedly regarding the aforementioned questions and the like, the hope is strong that you are not satisfied with just the study and diligence in *nigleh* and Chassidus as you are accustomed, but that you are conforming to the directive to "ascend in holiness," and there is nothing that can stand before the will.

I trust you are keeping up with the three daily *shiurim* of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya, as is well known.

With blessings for good news in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 9133

4 Iyar, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Shalom Eliezer
Staub

Greetings and blessings!

After a long delay, I acknowledge receipt of your letter from Isru Chag HaPesach, in which you ask about the reasons for the events of recent years.

In general, we have a fundamental instruction in our Torah, which is called *Toras Chaim*—the Torah of life. The meaning of this is as the simple translation suggests: *Toras Chaim* is a Torah that provides guidance for daily life, and especially regarding general occurrences: "You shall be wholehearted with Hashem your G-d."

This means relying on Hashem Yisbarach, knowing for certain that there is a correct explanation for everything that happens in the world, and especially regarding Yisrael, His close people, whom Hashem Yisbarach calls by name many times in His Torah: "You are children to Hashem your G-d."

Actually, the above is understandable. How can a person, who is limited in intellect and limited (meaning not fully exhaustive) in knowledge of events—meaning that not all details are known to him, and certainly not the outcome in the immediate future—how can he grasp and understand the *sechel* (so to speak) of the Ribono shel Olam?

As is well known, the comparison for this is a small child trying to grasp and understand the conduct and actions of an elderly, wise person of great character. The difference between them is only relative; the proof is that the great sage was once the same age as the child, with the same intellect, and the child has the possibility and hope that, in time, he too will be a great sage, perhaps even greater than him. Regarding a human being and the Creator, however, there is no comparison.

On the contrary, in the areas where one *does* understand and grasp, therein lies the novelty and the wonder.

Therefore, one thanks Hashem Yisbarach for the fact that He gives and bestows *da'as*—"He who graciously grants *da'as*."

Recalling our meeting, I am certain that it is unnecessary to elaborate further on what has been written above.

On this occasion, I take the liberty of enclosing a copy of my *Michtav Klali* for Pesach, which I hope you will find of interest.

With respect and blessing,

Let us imagine a person, quite intelligent and possessing good ethical sensibilities and intellect, who was raised on an island and has no inkling of medical healing through surgery. Suddenly, he walks into a hospital, enters an operating room, and sees a person lying on a table, tied down with ropes (as was done before the discovery of anesthesia).

Around him stand several people with knives and various instruments, cutting into the person on the table, while that person cries out in agony. When the islander sees this, he is horrified and asks, "How is it permitted to cut a person and pay no heed to his cries of agony?" This is only because he—the islander—has no inkling of the true intent of the operation. *Vehanamshal muvan* (and the analogy is understood).

## 935

B"H, 13 Iyar, 5726
Brooklyn.

P.S. Among the pieces of advice regarding anger is to contemplate how "the whole earth is full of His glory," the King of kings, the Holy One, blessed be He. This is especially true according to the words of our Alter Rebbe in Chapter 41 of the *Tanya Kaddisha*, that Hashem stands over him, etc., and looks at him and examines his kidneys and heart to see if he is serving Him as is fitting. When one remembers this matter—how one is in the presence of Hashem, may He be blessed and exalted, and that at that very moment Hashem is examining his kidneys and heart—there is surely no room for anger, etc. This is also the advice for success in the battle against the *yetzer* and distracting thoughts, etc., about which you wrote.

## 9239

B"H, Pesach Sheni, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, a man of the people and elevated above the people, who seeks the good of his people, a man of noble character, a scion of a noble lineage, R' Schneur Zalman, shlita,

Shalom u’vracha!

In connection with the information I receive from the members of the village who report to me whenever they speak with you regarding the "second" Kfar Chabad, I wish to clarify here, for you specifically, my hope and objective in this matter with greater clarity—even though, regarding certain points, I have not yet wished to publicize my ideas. By way of introduction:

As is known, it was necessary to establish the first Kfar Chabad urgently, in order to organize the immigrants from our country [the Soviet Union] who had arrived in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. There was no opportunity to plan the village in a full and precise manner. Although it would have been appropriate from the outset to establish two separate villages for reasons that will be explained below, because the number of immigrants at the beginning of the immigration from there was not so large, they were organized in one place.

However, now that their numbers have, B"H, increased, and we hope to Hashem that soon He will proclaim liberty to the captives, and our brothers who are in distress and captivity (and especially spiritual captivity) will ascend with song to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established—and our hope is also that their departure from there will be "as in the days of your coming out of the land of Egypt" (in the language of the verse)—with our young and our old, with our sons and our daughters, it seems clear to me that we must prepare a place and an organization for them in a planned manner. This is not only for the new immigrants who have already arrived, are arriving, and will arrive in the near future, but also in a way that will allow for improvements in the planning of the existing Kfar Chabad, especially in matters that should be in separate locations.

It is understood that one of the main points in this—which I believe I touched upon in one of our conversations when you were here—is that the educational institutions for girls and the educational institutions for boys currently located in Kfar Chabad (and we are not talking about a small number, but several hundred, may they be blessed, and my hope is that their number will continue to grow) should be located in separate places: the boys in the current Kfar Chabad, and the girls in the second Kfar Chabad.

There is another fundamental issue regarding the atmosphere that the new immigrants from there will require. Since they were disconnected from an atmosphere of Torah and mitzvos—having observed them with mesiras nefesh in hidden chambers—they were accustomed not to emphasize their conduct openly. Therefore, it will be difficult for them to change their conduct from one extreme to the other in a single hour and a single moment, or even in a few days or weeks.

On the other hand, those who grew up in a free atmosphere and were accustomed to the life of traditional, Chassidic Jews must be given the opportunity to continue in that atmosphere. Together with this, it is necessary that the two types not be at a great distance from one another, as they require mutual influence.

To enable full planning in accordance with the aforementioned requirements and conditions—this was my aspiration and hope in founding the second Kfar Chabad. First and foremost, as we spoke and as is recorded in my memory, the second Kfar Chabad must be distinct from the first, so that it does not border it. Yet, the aforementioned distance should be such that it only distinguishes and does not separate, so that they can visit one another even on Shabbos.

Secondly, the second Kfar Chabad must be planned from its inception to be primarily for the younger generation who were educated in an environment that openly practices a Chassidic way of life and can continue to do so. As for the educational institutions, those whose students are less fortified against influence from outside the walls of the institution should be there—I refer to the educational institutions for girls and young women. This will be easier to arrange in any case, since the educational institutions for boys are already organized in large buildings in the current Kfar Chabad.

In my thinking and my plan, with the help of Hashem, there will certainly be a shaliach, founder, and assistant in the establishment of the second Kfar Chabad, just as there was for the first Kfar Chabad. The new village will be in a suitable area, distinct but not separated, as mentioned above, and there the buildings for the girls' educational institutions will be established. It is understood that there will also be apartments there, first and foremost for those connected with these institutions, and also for the younger generation who were educated, as mentioned, in a Chassidic environment and do not necessarily need to live in the current Kfar Chabad under the wings of the elders of Anash.

Conversely, it is essential that the new immigrants from our country, who in their living conditions were not at all accustomed to a normal traditional Jewish way of life—let alone a Chassidic one—outside of their homes, and who never saw a Jewish street or a Jewish environment like that in Kfar Chabad, should find themselves for at least a few weeks in the atmosphere and environment of the current Kfar Chabad, whose influence they need the most. This is so that immediately upon arriving in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, they will enter a path of Chassidic life—a path of life that is established and orderly, existing for already eighteen years in the current village. There they will find people of their age, elders and those in their prime, as well as young people. Then, in the style of our Sages, "the earlier, the earlier [the former] nullifies [the latter]," and they will adapt to a Chassidic way of life openly, without difficulties and adventures. Therefore, it is necessary and most beneficial to establish the apartments and the hotel for them in the current Kfar Chabad specifically. This is in contrast to if the aforementioned apartments were in the second Kfar Chabad, where they would constitute a large portion of the quantity; then the aforementioned adaptation would be more difficult and fraught with adventures—adventures that can easily be prevented in the aforementioned manner.

This was also one of my reasons regarding the committee of the second Kfar Chabad. Although in my opinion it is desirable that it be connected with the committee of the first Kfar Chabad—and presumably this can be adapted within the framework of the law—in this committee itself, which will manage the second village, it is desirable that the majority of its members be from those who belong to the girls' education [sector] and from among those born in Eretz Yisrael, for whom there is no necessity to live specifically in the environment of the mashpi'im of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, etc.

There is much more to elaborate upon regarding what has been said, but I have come only to the main points, in addition to the essential fact that surely for one of your stature, there is no need for elaboration on the aforementioned matters, as you have contemplated and delved into them, and have also lived them (eingelebt un ibergelebt un durchgelelebt) for many years.

With appreciation, honor, and a blessing for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9137

By the Grace of Hashem, Sunday, the week of *Parshas Veshavtah Haaretz Shabbos LaHashem*, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Eleventh Annual Convention of N'shei U’Bnos Chabad, may they live and be well,

Greetings and Blessings!

The leitmotif of this year’s convention is **Shabbos**, and the theme is specifically tailored to this year of **Shemitah**. Furthermore, the convention takes place during *Parshas Behar*, which begins with the subject of Shemitah and unites the concept of Shemitah with Shabbos, as the Torah states: **"And in the seventh year... a Shabbos to Hashem"** (in the seventh year there shall be a Shabbos to Hashem), and as our Sages note: **"For the sake of Hashem, just as it is said regarding the Shabbos of Creation."**

This means to say:

Just as Shabbos—the seventh day—is set apart from all the days of the week and is sanctified to Hashem, so too is Shemitah—the seventh year—set apart from all other years and is sanctified to Hashem.

And just as Shabbos bears witness that Hashem is the **Creator** of the world, who created the world in six days and rested on the seventh day—Shabbos Kodesh—and this repeats itself every week, for the Divine creation of the world is **constant**, as explained in many places and specifically in Chassidus—so too was Shemitah set apart from all years and sanctified as a witness that Hashem is the **Master** of the world.

***

In daily life, this means:

In the private life of a Jew, there are times when spiritual life is explicit and prominent—when a Jew lives in shul and the beis medrash, in yeshiva and educational institutions, a life permeated with Torah and yiras shamayim—a "Shabbos LaHashem."

One might therefore think that at other times—at home, in domestic matters, in the street, and in business—it is not as important to emphasize the **"LaHashem"** (for Hashem).

Just as the not-working of the fields, letting the earth rest during the Shemitah year, is a "weekday" natural means for the earth to be richer and more fertile, to produce more and better grain—the Torah instructs that this resting must be only *LaHashem*—**for the sake of Hashem.**

The *Shnas Hashemitah* reminds and emphasizes—like *Shabbos Bereishis*—that for Jews, **all** details and events in daily life, even the "weekday" and "earthly" matters—such as eating, drinking, and matters of livelihood—must be **LaHashem**: eating *LaHashem*, drinking *LaHashem*, working and trading—*LaHashem*. All, every detail of the daily life of a Jew must be permeated with holiness and light that connect the Jew with Hashem Yisbarach.

***

Such a life depends—as has been discussed many times—to a very great extent upon Jewish women and girls: those who already manage Jewish homes as the *akeres habayis*, the mother and grandmother; and those who are preparing themselves for this most important role, the Jewish daughters.

May Hashem grant success to your multifaceted activities to strengthen Yiddishkeit—Torah of **Hashem** and mitzvos of **Hashem**, permeated and illuminated with the light and warmth of Chassidus—both in the close circles of your own family and in the wider circles of your surroundings. And may the Divine blessing in this week’s *sedra* be fulfilled: **"And I will command My blessing to you"**—you and all your loved ones should be blessed with Hashem’s blessing, even in a supernatural way and in all so-called natural events and necessities, from His full, open, holy, and generous hand.

With blessings for success and good tidings,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 9138

B"H, 20 Iyar, 5726
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Sunday, in which you write regarding the issue of adopting children from Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established), and whether you should travel there in this connection to clarify the details and conduct the negotiations, etc.

Regarding adoption in general, one must anticipate from the outset the difficulties associated with this according to our holy Torah, as explained in the Shulchan Aruch. This is based on the premise that an adopted child’s status is, of course, not the same as a son or daughter born to one. Therefore, matters of hugging, kissing, and *yichud*—which are permitted between a father and daughter or a mother and son—have no basis for leniency regarding an adopted child. It is understood how difficult it is to be careful about the aforementioned when raising and educating a child in such a way that they do not feel they are not a child born to you.

Therefore, one should only consider adopting a child **after** taking the aforementioned into account, and after reaching a firm decision to conduct oneself with the child according to the instruction of our holy Torah, the Torah of life. If you and your husband (may he live and be well) decide to proceed, and it appears to you that there are prospects that if one of you visits Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established) you will succeed in receiving the boy or girl, then you should travel in a good and auspicious hour.

As you requested, the letter is being sent without waiting for the turn.

#### ***9138***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 37, p. 197, and completed according to a copy.

**Regarding adoption**: See also above, Vol. 23, Letter 8,400, and the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 9,339

B.H., 22 Iyar, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Blessings and Peace!

I acknowledge receipt of the book by your husband, a.h., and I thank you for your thoughtfulness.

Along with this acknowledgment, I feel it is my duty, however difficult it may be, to express my negative stance regarding the use of the figures and events of our holy scriptures in allegorical interpretations—especially in a direction that obscures their luminosity and chosenness, even when that was not the author’s intent.

It is true that one is accustomed to the idea that in poetry, various liberties are permitted.

In my opinion, however, this should not be applied to the figures and episodes of the Tanach, whose lives and works still have an influence to this very day on Jews of all ages, and even on non-Jews. This demands that one refrain from utilizing poetic license even to portray them as greater than they are described in the Tanach, as this can lead the reader to the conclusion that since part of the description is an exaggeration, perhaps the whole thing is embellished; this is certainly the case if one utilizes the aforementioned license in the opposite direction.

As mentioned above, it is difficult for me to elaborate on this, especially since one can see from the book that the author’s intent was good. Furthermore, it is generally unethical and contrary to the ethics of Judaism to engage in criticism of someone who is already in the Olam HaEmes. However, one also has no right to remain silent regarding a general "protest."

By the way—and perhaps this is not by the way—it was especially pleasant to see in the poem you enclosed in the "Kinder Journal" an expression of the spirit of mesorah, which influences young readers to draw them closer to the luminosity of Shabbos and its holiness.

With respect and blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary
