## 941

941

B.H., 22 Iyar, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of "Beis Chana," New Haven, Conn.
May Hashem grant them life.

Blessings and peace!

I received the first issue of your publication with pleasure. May it be a good beginning, and may this endeavor, like all matters of Torah and holiness, be one of constant ascent and progress, "from strength to strength."

This issue was prepared and appeared at the appropriate time between Pesach and Atzeres. In both of these festivals, the women and daughters of Yisrael played a primary role. As Chazal relate, it was in the merit of the righteous women that our forefathers were redeemed from Mitzrayim, in order to receive the Torah from Sinai. Furthermore, before the Torah was given, Moshe Rabbeinu was commanded to speak first to "Beis Yaakov"—these are the women—and only afterwards to "Bnei Yisrael"—these are the men.

The days of Sefirah between these two Yomim Tovim are days of connection between the "time of our freedom" and the "time of the giving of our Torah," days of ascent and progress from strength to strength, as mentioned above. This is also hinted at in the manner of counting: as is known, the counting is not done with ordinal numbers (the first day, the second day, etc.), but with cardinal numbers—"today is two days," "three days," and so on. An ordinal number does not emphasize the concept of addition and completion, but rather the sequence in time. This is not the case when we say "today is two days" and "three days," etc., which emphasizes that the day upon which one stands completes, elevates, and adds to the previous days, leading toward the ultimate perfection. This is also hinted at in the parsha of the week: "And you shall count for yourself seven weeks of years, seven years seven times," etc. Just as it is with years, so it is with the days of every year during the days of Sefirah between Pesach and Shavuos. The number **seven** in general is a sign of perfection, as hinted at in the Song of Chanah: "The barren one has given birth to seven" (in negation of the opposite, as emphasized by the verse "she who had many children").

May it be the will of Hashem that just as it was at the time of the exodus from Mitzrayim—in the merit of the righteous women, as mentioned above—so too shall it be now, in these days of preparation for the fulfillment of the promise, "As in the days of your exodus from the land of Mitzrayim, I will show you wonders." And as the conclusion of the Song of Chanah states: "Hashem shall shatter those who contend with Him... and He shall raise the horn of His Mashiach," very soon.

With blessings for success and for good tidings.

## 9142

B"H, 22 Iyar, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 19th of Iyar, in which you write the main points of what you have recently been through and your current state of mind, and you quote verses from Psalm 22.

It is very surprising that you stopped the quotation at a place where one should not stop, for immediately following the verses you cite comes their resolution, a faithful piece of advice: "Commit [your way] to Hashem; **He will deliver him, He will rescue him**, for He delights in him."

This is especially true since in this very letter you write that you have already settled a significant portion of your debts, and surely you will succeed in easing the payment terms that were set, in a way that will allow you to continue paying and clearing your debts.

Adding to your trust in Hashem, who watches over each and every person with *hashgachah pratis*, increases Hashem's blessing; however, the conduit and vessel for receiving this blessing are Torah and its *mitzvos*. These days are indeed days of *segulah* for this, days of preparation for receiving the Torah. Surely, for someone like you, further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

I was honored by a visit from your father, the venerable Rabbi, etc., *shlita*, last night, and it was a pleasure to speak with him, to clarify and hear about general and personal matters. May Hashem lengthen his days and years in goodness and pleasantness, including true *nachas* from all his descendants, may they live, and may he succeed in spreading Yiddishkeit with abundance.

With respect and blessing in the customary manner for receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness, and for good tidings regarding the contents of your letter, with joy and a glad heart.

## 9143

9143

B”H, 1st of Sivan, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the annual dinner for the educational institution "Oholei Torah," may Hashem grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

The dinner is taking place this year on the day after Shabbos Parshas Bamidbar, a few days before Shavuos, *zman matan toraseinu*. This lends a special significance and importance to this annual undertaking for the benefit of the "Oholei Torah" educational institution.

According to the Geonim, we always read Parshas Bamidbar before Shavuos. The parsha begins with the counting of the Jews in the Sinai Desert, which is why the entire Chumash Bamidbar is called **Chumash HaPekudim** (The Book of Countings).

One of the implications of this is that when it comes to **Matan Torah**, all Jews must be counted and included in the *Klal Yisrael*, because every Jew has a portion in the Torah, and every Jewish neshamah is connected to the holy Torah.

Every Jew, from Moshe Rabbeinu down to the simplest of the simple, must be counted as "one"—no more and no less—because in terms of the *penimiyus* of the soul, all Jews are equal and precious to the Ribono shel Olam as children to the Makom, as it is explained in Tanya (Chapter 32): **"All are equal, and one Father for all of them"**—all are equal, and all have one Father.

From this, it is also understood that one must never, G-d forbid, "dismiss" a Jew, regardless of what his standing and state may be in Torah and mitzvos.

The recognition of the loftiness of the Jewish neshamah, and that every neshamah is a part of *Klal Yisrael*, and that the Ribono shel Olam is "one Father for all of them"—this is a preparation for *Kabbalas HaTorah* with joy and *penimiyus*.

Taking into account that the Torah was given only when we presented the children as a guarantee that the Torah would be studied and guarded—**"our children are our guarantors"**—it is clear how vital true, Torah-true education is, and what the approach to this education must be: On the part of the educators—to plant in the young hearts of the students a love of Torah and *yiras shamayim*, together with *ahavas Hashem* and *ahavas Yisrael*, in the spirit of **"all are equal, and one Father for all of them."** And on the part of the *baalei-batim*—to recognize their responsibility and privilege to create all the possibilities for this education *al taharas hakodesh*, and to ensure that not a single child, G-d forbid, should have to be left outside.

It is to be hoped with certainty that all participants in the annual undertaking for the educational institution **Oholei Torah** will correctly appreciate their responsibility and privilege regarding this educational institution, to ensure that the undertaking will fulfill all expectations, in all respects and to the fullest measure, and that its success will be felt throughout the entire year.

With respect and blessings for success,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9144

B"H, 26 Iyar, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Rabbi, G-d-fearing, distinguished scholar, involved in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Asher Abramson, shlita

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 12 Iyar, along with the enclosed material, in which you ask my opinion regarding the study program called "general religious and moral education" that the government has instituted. You raise two questions:

a. Is this study harmful to the souls of Jewish children?

b. Are we obligated according to halacha to take legal action regarding this?

a. It is understood that this study (as explained in the enclosed booklet) is prohibited, generally speaking, according to the words of the great teacher, the Rambam, in his Yad HaChazakah, Hilchos Avodah Zarah, Chapter Two, and its prohibition is a prohibition from the Torah, based on the well-known halachic ruling that Christians are idolaters.

From this, it is understood that not only is this study harmful to Jewish children, but it is actually a matter involving the laws of Avodah Zarah, where even the secondary aspects (*avizaryehu*) are extremely severe, and all the more so an actual prohibition.

b. From the above, the immediate conclusion is that we are obligated according to halacha to take legal action regarding this, and to do everything possible, through all legal channels, to annul the aforementioned decree. Certainly, when the situation is explained truthfully and with the necessary firmness, the argument will be accepted, since the matter touches upon the religious sentiment and the steadfast faith of our people, the Children of Israel—for which they have demonstrated mesiras nefesh throughout all the generations, to the point that all the nations of the world, and especially the enlightened nations in democratic countries, have recognized that one must not force the Jewish people to transgress their religion, G-d forbid, and certainly not to pressure them, restrict them, or make it difficult for them to observe their religion.

Given the simplicity of the matter and the urgency of the issue, I will suffice with these few lines, which are small in quantity relative to the magnitude of the subject.

With respect and blessing for good tidings regarding all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

Regarding your writing about the fact that in printed *Tehillim* books, the content of each chapter is printed before every *mizmor*:

- This is already found in very old printed *Tehillim* books and in many editions, and this is not news from recent times.

Regarding chapter 86, it states that it contains various prayers, etc., and many descriptions of praise to Hashem. It is not understandable what is not smooth here; this is simply the straightforward, literal interpretation of the verses of this *mizmor*, in which are mentioned "the arrogant," "a congregation of violent men," "those who hate me"—which refers to people—and because of this, "poor and needy," "the day of my distress," "the lowest *Sheol*," etc., and likewise regarding the praises to Hashem.

It is surely understandable that every painful or unfavorable human situation requires a specific prayer, similar to the matter from which one needs to be redeemed.

To the extent that this *mizmor* is considered to be composed of very serious requests, this is also clear from the fact that in the *seder* of *tefillah*, it is not recited on Shabbos and Yom Tov, nor on days when *Tachanun* is not recited.

The translation and commentary you mention in your letter are not with me at the moment; in any case, this does not change what was written above—the straightforward, literal interpretation of this *mizmor*.

***

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated the 21st of Iyar. The *pidyon nefesh* included therein will be read at the holy gravesite.

Regarding school matters—follow the instruction of the administration of the *Reshet*.

Regarding the leather that has a different color in some places—follow the instruction of an expert doctor.

Surely you are keeping the three *shiurim* that are equal for every soul—in *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*—and in any case, you should do so from now on.

## 5151

[Erev Chag HaShavuos 5726]

Ashkenazi

Further to the previous telegram, surely the actions that were written about will be stopped immediately, and it will be publicized that they were done without my knowledge, and it is obvious that this is the opposite of my will.

And the receipt books that you mention—send all of them, literally, here.

## 952

[Erev Chag HaShavuos, 5726]

Regarding what you wrote, that your son—may he live—has not been successful in his studies at the yeshiva: It is understood that it is worthwhile for him to learn a trade (craft). It would be best to do so at a vocational school where they also study Torah. (Studying at a public school is, of course, out of the question, as he would be mixing with non-Jews, etc., in addition to the issue of boys and girls being mixed together.)

If such a school can be found in Toronto, or at the very least in New York, it is better than being at a great distance—so that you can see him frequently and be able to advise him on how to adjust more easily, and the like.

If one cannot be found, then [he should go] to Eretz Yisrael. You should clarify with R' Chefer—may he live—whether the program at Kfar Chabad is suitable for his capabilities (where they also study Chassidus), or if there is another **religious** vocational school in Eretz Yisrael.

## 9,153

B"H, Isru Chag of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah, 5726. Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants in the annual luncheon of the N.Y. Committee for the Seminary for Teachers and Schools for Girls in Kfar Chabad in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily,
May Hashem grant you life,

Blessings and peace!

On the occasion of the annual luncheon taking place on Sunday, Parshas Shelach, I send my heartfelt wish that Hashem bless this endeavor with great success, and that this success be felt and evident throughout the entire year.

In this week’s parsha — Shelach — we are told of a matter in which the women once again distinguished themselves with their devotion to Hashem, serving as a model for the men.

This concerned Hashem’s promise, through Moshe Rabbeinu, to give Eretz Yisrael to the Jewish people, a promise which the spies, with their negative report, weakened in the hearts of the men. The women, by contrast, remained firm in their belief in Hashem’s promise. This was expressed especially when the daughters of Tzelofchad demanded an inheritance in Eretz Yisrael, as is recounted in a later parsha. This courageous action of the loyal Jewish daughters is highly praised by our Sages, of blessed memory.

From this we see that there are matters — often very important affairs that concern the entire Jewish people — where women must take an active role and serve as a living model, even for the men.

Especially important is the role that women must take in the field of **chinuch**. The Jewish woman is endowed with special qualities and sensitivities, with a unique perceptiveness and maternal devotion to a Jewish child, particularly a child in need. Beyond the fact that they can contribute so much through their direct assistance, both regarding material and spiritual needs, no less important is the indirect help that women provide, serving as a living example and inspiring enthusiasm among the men.

The merit of your activity on behalf of the educational institutions in Kfar Chabad, which were founded by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory — an activity which you will surely strengthen and expand, as is required in all matters of Torah and holiness — will stand by you. May you, with Hashem’s help, be successful in your work, and through this, be blessed, together with your families, in all that you need, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for success and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

954

B"H, 14 Sivan, 5726
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Sivan, in which you outline the events of your life and what you have recently experienced, concluding with what occurred when you served as the shaliach tzibur on Rosh Chodesh, etc.

Since, as you write, this is the custom of the congregation in the beis medrash where you davened (and indeed the custom of the entire city), according to many poskim, you were obligated to follow the custom of the congregation, even in a matter more stringent than the one you describe.

In any event, from here on, you should divert your thoughts from this matter. On the contrary, you should strengthen your bitachon in Hashem, who oversees each and every person with hashgacha pratis, for "everything the Merciful One does is for the good." Increasing your bitachon in Hashem and in matters of Torah and mitzvos in general will bring about the fulfillment of the promise of Chazal: "Whoever adds, they add to him."

At an opportune time, I will mention you at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in accordance with the content of your letter. May it be His will that just as you brought the request, you will also bring good news regarding the aforementioned.

With blessings,
On behalf of the Rebbe,
Secretary

P.S. Regarding an avel serving as shaliach tzibur: The custom of Chassidei Chabad, according to the instructions of our Rebbes, is not to serve as shaliach tzibur, even for Maariv on a day when there is a Musaf prayer. However, as mentioned above regarding your specific incident, you davened as a member of a congregation that follows a different custom, and this is understood.

**And what you have recently experienced, and you conclude:** In your letter: My father, of blessed memory, passed away on Shabbos, the 9th of Adar II, 5725. As an avel, I davened before the congregation and recited Kaddish according to the halacha.

Rosh Chodesh Nissan of 5725 fell on Shabbos, a day when an avel does not serve as shaliach tzibur.

On Rosh Chodesh Iyar, I followed the custom of the people of Jerusalem, where the shaliach tzibur davens until the blessing of Hallel, and after someone else finishes Hallel, I recited Kaddish Tiskabel. In the middle of the repetition of the Amidah, I began to feel unwell and barely finished the repetition. Because it was Rosh Chodesh, I did not continue, and afterwards it passed and I felt normal, as if nothing had happened. Exactly one month later, on Rosh Chodesh Sivan, I again began to feel unwell in the middle of the repetition of the Amidah, and during the prayer of "Chanun Hamarbeh Lisloach," I was forced to stop, and another member of the congregation finished the prayer.

As I lay ill on my sickbed in the hospital, it occurred to me that I had conducted myself during my year of mourning in opposition to the halacha of the Gaon of Vilna, zt"l, that an avel does not serve as shaliach tzibur on Rosh Chodesh, even for Mincha. Furthermore, my father, of blessed memory, who was of Vilna descent, named me Eliyahu after the Gaon, and perhaps because of this I was punished by Hashem.

**Everything the Merciful One does is for the good:** Berachos 60b.

**The promise of Chazal:** See Taanis 31a and Rashi there.

**Not upon us and not now:** [A common expression used when mentioning unfortunate events].

**The custom of Chassidei Chabad:** Sefer HaMinhagim-Chabad, p. 36. See also above, Vol. 2, Letter 349; Vol. 11, Letter 3882.

## 9055

By the Grace of G-d
15 Sivan, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Brownsville and East New York Women’s League
May they be kept alive by Hashem

Blessings and peace!

On the occasion of your annual luncheon, to be held on Monday, the 18th of Sivan, may the Ribono shel Olam grant that the event be a great success in every respect.

This year is a **Shmittah year**, the seventh year, which is sanctified among the years just as the seventh day, Shabbos, is sanctified among the days. The difference is that on Shabbos all forms of work are forbidden, whereas in a Shmittah year, one is only forbidden from working the fields and gardens, while all other household work and the like is permitted.

The purpose of the Shmittah year, as with the day of Shabbos, is — **"to Hashem"** — sanctified to G-d.

This means, first and foremost, that the time freed from agriculture — which was one of the primary occupations of Jews before the Golus — should be utilized for matters of Elokus and holiness.

Furthermore, another primary lesson of Shmittah emerges: that even in the ordinary "weekday" daily life, one should increase in matters of Elokus, until the entire year is justifiably called "to Hashem," similar to Shabbos, which is called "holy to Hashem."

And just as the spirit and holiness of Shabbos must influence all the days of the week, and Shabbos is the "source of blessing" (the fountainhead of Divine blessings) for all the days of the week, so too must the spirit and holiness of Shmittah be reflected in all the remaining years, and this creates the channels to receive Divine blessings even in material necessities.

For the Jewish woman, this means: although she is not occupied with the study of Torah, she can, and must, increase in all matters of holiness in the home, where she is the "pillar of the home," as well as in activities to support the institutions of Torah, which is the mission of your Women’s League. Especially since you have the great merit to support the holy institutions of the Lubavitcher Yeshivos, founded by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which are an inexhaustible source of Torah and holiness, including Pnimiyus HaTorah, Toras HaChassidus, and serve as a model and encouragement for other institutions of Torah and education as well.

May Hashem Yisbarach grant success to your work, which you will surely continue in an intensified and growing measure, and may He bless you and your families, may they live, with all that you need, with revealed and manifest good, in both Gashmius and Ruchnius together.

With blessings for success and good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9559

9559

B”H, 18 Sivan, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. Nechama
Tichye

Blessings and Peace!

Our dear friend, Rabbi Shlomo Aharon Kazarnovsky, showed me a copy of the letter you sent to Eretz Yisrael regarding the "Beis Nechama" project.

I would like to take this opportunity to express my great satisfaction upon reading the letter and seeing the warm Yiddishe feelings expressed within it, as well as your firm stance regarding the strict kashrus that must be maintained at "Beis Nechama."

I am certain that your appeal will have the appropriate resonance, and that all your good resolutions will be crowned with the fullest measure of success, serving as a living model for other similar projects. This is especially important, considering that these are conditions connected to the chinuch of the growing generation in Eretz Yisrael, upon whom rests the serious hope that they will not only fulfill all expectations as builders of the new generation, but will also fill the empty void that was, unfortunately, left after so many millions of the best sons and daughters of the Yiddishe people were torn from us. These cut-short lives of the kedoshim, Hashem yinkom damam, of each of whom it is said, **"The candle of Hashem is the soul of man"** (a Yiddishe neshamah is a Divine light), must not be extinguished, chas v’shalom. The light that they spread around them must be continued by the new generation—their spiritual heirs.

This also demands an additional measure of mesiras nefesh from each and every one of us, to whom Hashgacha Elyona has given the great zechus to take a part in the upbringing of the young generation, so that this chinuch should be permeated with the proper spirit and with full recognition and awareness of what their mission in life is, so that they may carry out their Divine shlichus to the fullest extent.

May Hashem Yisbarach bless your good work; may you see good fruits, and fruits of fruits, from your efforts, and derive much nachas from them, in good health, joy, and pleasure.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 9558

B"H, 25 Sivan, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch
For the Chag HaSiyum, Montreal, may they live

Greetings and Blessings!

For the upcoming Chag HaSiyum on Wednesday, 4 Tammuz, I send my greetings and blessing to those completing their studies, as well as to the Roshei Yeshiva, administrators, educators, and all the students, may they live. May Hashem grant that this celebration evoke the appropriate encouragement and *kochos hanefesh* to ascend in all matters of Torah and *mitzvos*.

If this is the purpose of a Chag HaSiyum every year, then *kal v’chomer* when the Chag HaSiyum—as in this year—takes place in the **Shnas HaSheva, the year of Shmittah**, which is called "a Shabbos to Hashem" and has been likened to Shabbos Kodesh.

For on Shabbos—even sleep on Shabbos is a *taanug*—even though during the time of sleep, the intellect, which is the highest faculty in man, is also dormant. This shows that **all** human affairs, even the most mundane—like sleeping—must be sanctified to Hashem.

In this same vein is the concept of Shmittah. In the year of Shmittah, only the various labors connected to working the land were forbidden, while all other labors were not restricted. Yet, the Torah demanded that even in all those other daily occupations throughout the entire year, the "Shabbos to Hashem" should be evident—in addition to the fact that the time freed from working the land should be dedicated to the study of Torah and the fulfillment of *mitzvos* with greater depth and inwardness.

It is therefore to be hoped that the Chag HaSiyum will be conducted under the impression and in the spirit of Shmittah, for the influence of the year of *Shevi'is* should be felt in all the remaining years as well, just as the influence of Shabbos must be felt in all the days of the week.

May Hashem grant success to every one of the *mesaymim*, together with all the students of the Yeshiva, may they live, to fulfill the task and *shlichus* that the founder of the Yeshiva, *ztzukulleh"h nbg"m zi"e*, placed upon the *Temimim*: to be **neros leha'ir** (lamps to illuminate) with the light of *Toras HaNigleh* and the light of *Toras HaChassidus*, in the fullest measure, with joy and a good heart.

With blessings for outstanding success in both material and spiritual matters, and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 859

B”H, 25 Sivan, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Students of the Lubavitch Seminary, Casablanca,
May Hashem grant you life.

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter of 15 Sivan regarding your examinations: as you requested, I will mention you [at the Ohel] for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires for good and for blessing, and for proper organization so that from here on you may increase in diligence and dedication (to holy studies, study that leads to action) and in good conduct in yiras shamayim, as is fitting for daughters of Yisrael, daughters of our matriarchs Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah.

The statement of our Rebbe, the Baal Shem Tov, is well known: that from every matter one must learn (a lesson in good conduct) in the avodah of Hashem, may He be blessed and exalted. From this comes a directive for every Jewish man and woman: that if there is an examination in any matter, first and foremost one must contemplate and perform a self-examination in matters of holiness—that is, in one’s conduct regarding Torah and mitzvos. For in these, every person is examined every day. In the words of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya: “And behold, Hashem stands over him, and the whole world is full of His glory, and He looks upon him and **examines** the kidneys and the heart [to see] if he is serving Him as is fitting” (beginning of Chapter 41, see there).

With blessings for success and for good tidings.

P.S. I was very distressed (a) by the rumor that you suspected me of intending to visit Eretz Yisrael without notifying you beforehand. This is the absolute opposite of the relationship between us—had I not notified you?

On the contrary, the lack of notification is proof that the aforementioned had no basis.

(b) Just now, a second rumor reached me, that you fear that the content of the report regarding the conversation with Mr. S. Ratberg, shlita, and his support for Chabad affairs, has some connection to the support mentioned previously by the Joint (for the project of building the hotel in Kfar Chabad for the new immigrants from our country, in the past).

Beyond the clear law that one does not divert funds from one tzedakah to another, and beyond the fact that it is understood that in a matter in which you invested effort and toil, I would not do anything without clarifying your opinion beforehand, it seems to me that it was highlighted in my letter to you in the aforementioned report—that the conversation with the aforementioned was because of the matter that they (S.R.) walk among the philanthropists of the United States, and this has no connection whatsoever to the Joint. Furthermore, even when I mentioned in the conversation about the activities of the aforementioned, it was mentioned only and precisely regarding the UJA and the Bonds.

(c) Regarding the location of the hotel building for the aforementioned immigrants: It is true that I had—and still have—an opinion, as explained in the letter attached hereto. But it is understood that the decision is in your hands—you are the initiator of the idea, and you even brought it to a practical stage in your conversation with Mr. D. H. Jordan, shlita. Furthermore, although the letter attached hereto was written many weeks ago, I delayed sending it until further details regarding the aforementioned were clarified (clearer information regarding the immigration from there, the prospects for the start of the construction of the second Kfar Chabad, and the estimation regarding its completion, etc.). But since the rumor regarding my general opinion concerning the location of the hotel building has already reached you, I am sending the aforementioned letter with the addition—that to the extent that the aforementioned details have been clarified, this strengthens my opinion even more—that it is worthwhile to build the aforementioned hotel as soon as possible, which is to say—in the village that already exists, in addition to the reasons explained in the attached letter. And with the addition, once again, that the final decision in this is in your hands, for ultimately, the intention of both of us is only and exclusively for the benefit of the immigrants and their families, may they live, and may they increase, very soon, and may they come with singing and everlasting joy upon their heads.

## 962

B"H, 2 Tammuz, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Tzvi Slonim, 10 Yehuda Halevi, Bnei Brak

Shalom u’Bracha,

After a long interval, your letter of 17 Sivan from the Holy Land (may it be rebuilt and established) was received.

With respect and blessing for good tidings regarding all the aforementioned, and with a request to convey my regards to your father (may he live and be well), along with my surprise that it has been quite a few months since I have heard from him.

Regarding the note from the Ramban in *Bamidbar* (1:45)—it is more relevant to the matter of a *pidyon nefesh* than to the status of *maamad*, etc. However, see *Kesuvos* (105b)—and based on what is explained there, one can also understand why this has been accepted with favor by our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, despite the ruling in *Shulchan Aruch Choshen Mishpat* (end of section 249) (and it is even more difficult according to what is written in the *Sma* there: "and he does not rebuke them," etc.). Rather, our Sages were precise there: "He who brings" (and not "he who gives" generally—which includes even that which was pressured), a "gift" (according to what is explained in the *Rema*, *Shulchan Aruch Yoreh Deah*, end of section 251), "first fruits" (see tractate *Bikkurim*. And a word to the wise is sufficient). And this is not the place to elaborate.

## 966

B"H, Days of Redemption, Tammuz 5726

To "Gan Yisroel," may Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

May the opening of "Gan Yisroel" and the entire duration of your stay there be successful in every respect.

Especially as this year is the year of Shemitah, which is a Shabbos to Hashem and is auspicious for increasing in Torah and mitzvos, and for drawing down *shuvah* and *nachas*—the true *taanug*—in matters of both body and soul alike, and for hastening the fulfillment of the prophecy in our parsha, "A staff shall arise from Yisroel," which refers to Melech HaMoshiach, "and Yisroel shall perform valor." 

With the blessing of the Chag HaGeulah,

**M. Schneerson**

**For increasing in Torah:** See Berachos 35b, "Is it possible that a person plows..." etc., [and yet engages in] Torah, etc.

**And mitzvos:** (Through the increase in) learning that leads to (the increase in) action. 

**Shuvah... the true:** See the Reshimus of the Admur the Tzemach Tzedek on Tehillim (92:1 and in the supplements there). 

**Body and soul:** Which in spirituality are mitzvos (the limbs, *garmohi*) and Torah (the blood is the soul, *chivohi*)—see Tanya, Chapter 23 (and the glosses of the Tzemach Tzedek there). Likutei Torah, Bamidbar 13a. 

**This refers to Melech HaMoshiach:** Rambam, Hilchos Melachim, beginning of Chapter 11. 

**And Yisroel shall perform valor:** See Zohar, end of this parsha. 

---

See also below, Letter 951.

**Shabbos to Hashem:** Behar 25:2-4.

**Learning that leads to... action:** See Kiddushin 40b and the sources cited there.

**Reshimus of the Admur the Tzemach Tzedek on Tehillim:** Yahel Or, p. 328 and onwards. Ibid., p. 627 and onwards.

**The blood is the soul:** Re'eh 12:23.

**And the glosses of the Tzemach Tzedek there:** Kitzurim VeHe'aros LeTanya, p. 104 and onwards.

**In our parsha:** Balak 24:17.

**Zohar:** Vol. III, 212b.

## 9667

B"H, 16 Tammuz, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from Rosh Chodesh Tammuz and the one preceding it (along with the enclosures).

At an auspicious time, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires for the good, regarding all the matters about which you write.

As we have just passed the days of redemption, 12 and 13 Tammuz—days whose history you surely know, and more importantly, the lessons we must derive from them—this will certainly add to your trust in Hashem, who oversees each and every person with *hashgacha pratis*. As the Sweet Singer of Israel expressed, "Hashem is with me, I will not fear," and "Hashem is my shepherd, I shall not lack." This refers not only to matters that are called "great" in human terms, but even to small and minute details. This is in accordance with the well-known style of the Baal Shem Tov regarding *hashgacha pratis*: that it is not merely the rolling of a leaf in the street that is overseen from Above, but even the manner and cause of that rolling.

From this, we learn the magnitude and inwardness of the supervision of Hashem, may He be blessed, regarding the affairs of the sons and daughters of Israel, "His close people."

With blessings for good tidings regarding the content of your letter—and it is understood and simple that what is written above is directed to each one of you, and especially to the content of your letter regarding the state of your health, etc.

The intention is not to offer a defense, Heaven forbid, for the aforementioned situation, but rather, on the contrary, to suggest that perhaps its interpretation is merely a matter of a *nisayon* (which is relevant specifically through something difficult and incomprehensible). And then, as is customary with matters of *nisayon*, once it is recognized that "Hashem your G-d is testing you to know whether you love Hashem your G-d with all [your heart]," and one stands the "test," the situation is nullified (for it has already fulfilled its "role") and one returns to one's strength.

With blessings for a complete and speedy recovery, for the expansion of your livelihood, and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S.
The suggestion of the honorable ones regarding their daughter, may she live (with the *avreich*... may he live)—is generally correct. However, since you mention that (at first) she was somewhat hesitant, etc., it is not advisable for you to intervene further in this. Let your daughter continue as she sees fit, according to the inclination of her heart, etc., and—as mentioned above—Hashem oversees with *hashgacha pratis*.

## 9168

In response to your letter of 12 Tammuz, in which you write that it has been some years since your wedding, and you have not yet been blessed with children.

It is surprising that you do not mention whether you have consulted with expert physicians, for a person must do what is within their power through the natural path; in any case, you should do so now.

Furthermore, and most importantly, since the delay in Hashem’s blessing for living and enduring offspring often stems from a lack of precision in observing the laws and statutes of Taharas Hamishpacha (Niddah, Hefsek Taharah, immersion in a kosher mikveh, etc.), or from a lack of full knowledge regarding all the details thereof, you must clarify all these details with a Rav who is a teacher of Halacha, with the intent to observe them from here on in as is required.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## Text

B"H, 19 Tammuz, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Schneur Zalman Maschari

Greetings and Blessings,

I was pleased to receive your letter from the auspicious day of 13 Tammuz (and the one preceding it), in which you provide a report of the recent meeting and a summary of the resolutions. May it be the will of Hashem that your resolutions be fulfilled for the good, and may the statement of our Sages be fulfilled: "He who has one hundred wants two hundred; he has two hundred and wants four hundred" (and he is not satisfied with the addition of a mere hundred as before). The success in these matters will, as you write, lead to a second list, and the hope is that it will surpass the first in number, weight, and so on. Just as you have brought good news until now, so too may you bring good news in the future, in good health and with successful activity, as you write at the conclusion of your letter.

This is especially pertinent as your letter was written on the day of the redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and as we spoke when you were here, the lesson of 12-13 Tammuz for each and every one of us is that when a person stands firm, he overcomes the greatest obstacles. And although "who can compare to him," the obstacles in our time are incomparably smaller, and furthermore, the path has already been paved and cleared before us by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the Nasi of our generation.

May it be the will of Hashem that these days of "between the straits" be transformed into joy and gladness, as the prophet foretold, and may we merit to see, speedily in our days, the true and complete Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With respect and with blessings for a speedy recovery and for good tidings.

***

**Mr. Schneur Zalman Maschari**: See additional letters to him in the previous volume, and the references noted there.

**Statement of our Sages**: See Koheles Rabbah 1:13. Referenced in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 21, p. 450.

**The lesson of 12-13 Tammuz**: See also the previous letter.

**Immediately**: Note the statement of our Sages that there are "three immediacies" (discussed in the Maamar *Se'u Yedeichem*, Shabbos Parshas Pinchas, Ch. 7 [in Sefer HaKunteresim, Vol. 1, p. 188]).

**Pinchas**: See Berachos (56b): "Pinchas... a wonder" (and Rashi there: as was done for Pinchas, as we say in Sanhedrin (82b). It is puzzling, for if so, it should say "wonders," as many miracles were performed for Pinchas then. Note that the letter *nun* is interchangeable with *lamed* (from the same source—the letters *daled, tes, lamed, nun, tav* in the language), and *Pinchas* contains the letters *pe-ches-nun-samech* (though according to this, it should say "a miracle was performed"). However, for the time being, I have not found this in a sefer).

**The letters daled, tes, lamed, nun, tav in the language... however**: In another copy, it is with a variation and addition: "the letters *daled, tes, lamed, nun, tav* in the language (see Nechemiah 3:30) and *ches*—a level of *Chesed* (Zohar Vol. 3, 238a); also in *Pinchas* there are the letters *nun-samech* (however..."

**The four types**: Note the *Yahel Ohr* of the Tzemach Tzedek on Tehillim 107.

**As the prophet foretold**: Zechariah 8:19. See Rambam, end of Hilchos Taanis.

## 9105

9105

B"H, Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Pinchas, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter...

These days are days of *segulah*, immediately following Shabbos Parshas Pinchas, the day of the *Birchas HaGomel* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *Nasi Yisrael*, in connection with his redemption.

And as has been discussed many times: "The body follows the head."

Especially for those who are in need of Hashem bestowing goodness upon them, they are the four types—and your mnemonic is the word *Chayim* (Life): *Choleh* (sick person), *Yisurim* (those who suffer), *Yam* (sea), *Midbar* (desert)—who shall give thanks to Him forever, *Chayim*.

This is meant both literally,

And also regarding these four types in *avodah ruchanis* (as explained in the *maamar* beginning "Baruch HaGomel" [Blessed is He who bestows good upon the guilty, for He has bestowed good upon me], by the author of the redemption):

*Choleh* (sick person) — *timtum* of the mind and heart.

*Chavush b'veis ha'asurim* (imprisoned) — "The wicked surrounds the righteous" (*tzaddik*).

*Yored b'yam* (descending into the sea) — in the multitude of distractions (*mayim rabim*) of worldly matters.

*Holech bamidbar* (walking in the desert) — one who is surrendered only to the physicality and materiality of the world (the opposite of a place of human habitation; "You are called *Adam* [man]," [meaning] *adameh l'elyon* [I will be like the Most High]).

For, as the conclusion of the *maamar* (ibid.) states: Through the kindness of the Most High, a spirit from above is awakened, etc., until "the righteous is delivered from trouble" (which includes every single Jew), as it is written, "And your people are all righteous."

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

Secretary

P.S.
It is appropriate that you have your *tefillin* checked, and every weekday, before putting on *tefillin*, set aside a few coins for *tzedakah*.

Regarding what you wrote concerning your stuttering: Since a person must do what is within his power according to the natural order, you should consult with a doctor and act according to his advice.

However, the main thing is that you must increase your diligence and perseverance in the study of Torah—both *nigleh* and *Chassidus*. This study should be, as our Sages taught, something that leads to action—the performance of *mitzvos* with *hiddur*. Beyond the essential fact that this is the command of the *Ribono shel Olam*, it is also the path to receiving the blessing, for He is the "Healer of all flesh and performs wonders," and a human doctor is merely His agent.

We see tangibly that regarding stuttering, it is particularly helpful to strengthen one's trait of *bitachon* in Hashem Yisbarach, who oversees every individual with *hashgacha pratis*, since a significant cause of the aforementioned ailment is a lack of inner tranquility and the necessary self-confidence.

## 9. Tiku

B"H, 25 Tammuz, 5726
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter—which was received after a long delay—in which you ask regarding your plan to study medicine, but note that there are several obstacles involved, and you begin to list them, etc.

Now, generally speaking, regarding any question that pertains to the Shulchan Aruch, you must turn to a Rav who is a *moreh hora'ah* (an authority on halachic ruling) in your vicinity. This is because a clear halachic ruling is tied to many details and sub-details that cannot always be put into writing, and in such a case, there is also no need to do so, since you can find a Rav in your area to clarify the matter and speak with him face-to-face.

The essential point is that something which is forbidden according to the Shulchan Aruch is indeed forbidden. What benefit is there for a person to deceive himself, as if one could invent some sort of permit in this matter, when a Rav who is a *moreh hora'ah* with authority in this field explicitly states that there is no permit? In the phrasing of our Sages regarding a mitzvah that comes through a transgression, it is "a robber who blesses, he blasphemes Hashem".

It is my hope that you have fixed times for the study of Torah, which is our life and the length of our days, and that the study is in accordance with the instruction of our Sages, of blessed memory: study that leads to action, the fulfillment of the mitzvos.

And since "Love your fellow as yourself" is a great principle in the Torah, you surely influence those in your environment to conduct themselves in this way as well, and we are promised that words which come from the heart enter the heart of the listener and accomplish their effect.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 9257

B"H, 25 Tammuz, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter of 7/11, in which you write regarding the relationships in your home, etc.

In general, in such matters, one can accomplish more through friends and acquaintances than through direct conversation with those closest to the situation.

Regarding your writing, at the conclusion of your letter, about where to invest money:

One should speak about this with reliable business people and good friends who are knowledgeable in this area, or who are able to find out about it.

And may Hashem Yisbarach, who watches over everyone—man and woman—guide you in all that was written above, in a good way, good in all respects.

I hope it is unnecessary to point out that one’s daily conduct must be in accordance with all the instructions of our holy Torah, Toras Chaim, and that one must observe the mitzvos, regarding which it is written, "and he shall live by them." Beyond the primary point—that this is the command of Hashem Yisbarach—this is also the way to receive His blessings in the things one needs.

Surely you observe the good custom of Jewish women to give to tzedakah each time before lighting candles, Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov. And it would be good to have the mezuzos in your home checked (optzhekin) to ensure they are all kosher according to the law—if this has not been done in the last 12 months.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 9178

B"H, 25 Tammuz, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Blessings and peace!

In response to your two letters, in which you write the main points of your life, your state of mind, and your situation in general of late, etc.

It is not at all surprising that a Jewish man or woman lacks inner tranquility if their daily conduct does not align with their inner, essential nature—that is to say, if it does not align with what is stated in our holy Torah regarding every single one of our people: "You are children to Hashem your G-d." If a regular child must behave in a manner appropriate to their parents, then how much more so—to an infinite degree—is this true for the children of the Omnipresent, the sons and daughters of Israel. Their Father in Heaven has provided them with a path in life through His Torah (the word *Torah* implying *hora'ah*, instruction), which is called "the Torah of life." He is also the Creator who fashioned them in a way that is suited for this life. Therefore, a disruption in this conduct brings about a disruption in one's inner tranquility, etc.

From what has been said, the primary advice for rectifying the situation is also understood: first and foremost, you must conduct yourself from here on in a manner that aligns with the will of Hashem, the Creator and Guide of man, as detailed in the Shulchan Aruch.

I assume, of course, that some might raise an objection to this premise based on the reality that many who do not observe the mitzvos seem to lack nothing, including peace of mind, etc. The answer to this difficulty is also simple: 1) In the style of our Sages—no person knows what is in the heart of another, especially in areas that, for various understandable reasons, the other person does not wish to reveal to others. 2) It is like a physical illness, G-d forbid; when a sick person does not feel that they are ill, this is not a sign of health, but on the contrary, a sign that the illness has taken a heavy toll. This is the case, and even more so, regarding the state of mental and spiritual health.

Regarding your question about practical advice, etc., based on the description in your letter, you should begin to organize your life so that you become accustomed to a structured daily routine. This will make it easier for you to enter a steady course of life, self-discipline, and the rule of the mind and intellect over the heart and emotions, etc.

It is understood that the above does not negate what was written at the beginning of the letter. Rather, within this very framework, a person must act according to the way of nature. It appears that the primary factors in your situation are the lack of order and the instability in the external aspects of your life, which result in a similar state in your soul, emotions, etc.

Since it is difficult to become accustomed to an orderly and stable life after a long period of living without structure, one of the ways to facilitate this transition is through an external factor. I refer to accepting a position or something similar, so that you will know you have obligations toward others, with fixed work and set hours, etc.

It seems to me, reading between the lines of your letter, that you assess your situation as having hidden and serious causes, etc. But in my opinion, the main point and the primary factor are the two matters mentioned above: conduct according to the Torah and living an orderly life. When you rectify these (slowly, at least), your situation will improve to a significant degree, and perhaps even to the point of complete resolution.

Another point in the above, which is also essential, is a suitable *shidduch*. But it is clear that the approach to this important issue—and certainly any decision regarding it—must come from a place of peace of mind and without confusion. Therefore, the priority is to settle the first two matters, and only afterward to approach and look into the latter point.

It is difficult to estimate in advance how much time will be required to rectify the above, but it is clear to me that it depends solely on your desire and firm decision to proceed in this direction, and subsequently to fulfill this decision without hesitation or doubt, etc.

May it be the will of Hashem, who watches over every individual with *hashgachah pratis*, to illuminate your path in life and grant you success in all that you need, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for mental and physical health and for good tidings.

On behalf of the Rebbe,
Secretary

P.S.
Regarding what you wrote concerning health matters: instead of the differences of opinion you describe, you should consult with three doctors and decide according to the majority. May it be His will that the verse, "And Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you do," be fulfilled in this.

This is also an opportunity for me to express once again the pleasure I derived from reading and studying, when the opportunity arose, your book, *Klei HaCheres b'Sifrus HaTalmud*. May Hashem fulfill your heart's desires for the good regarding the book you are currently working on (concerning glassware).

This is also an appropriate place for me to fulfill the obligation (and privilege) of urging you on the necessity of having fixed times for studying *Pnimiyus HaTorah*—which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus—in addition to your studies in the *nigleh* of Torah. Surely, for someone like you, elaborating on the magnitude of this matter is unnecessary.

***

**R' Yehoshua**: Brand, Jerusalem.

**"And Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you do"**: *Devarim* 15:18.

## 990

B"H, 15 Menachem Av, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, a man of stature and high standing, who seeks the good of his people, a man of noble character, scion of a noble lineage, R' Schneur Zalman, shlita,

Shalom u’vracha!

Following up on our verbal conversation, I wish to also express in writing, first and foremost, my warm welcome upon your return to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. I offer my heartfelt wishes that the great effort you invested in your travels and the like will yield fruits in a measure far exceeding expectations. To use the phrasing of our Sages—whose every word is precise in all its details—"You have labored and you have found" (*Megillah 6b*). This means that when there is labor, the results are not merely commensurate with that labor, but come in the manner of "finding"—that is, like a windfall that is disproportionate to the effort invested. And the merit of the many will assist you.

I would like to express once again my heartfelt gratitude and the great satisfaction and *nachas ruach* I derived from the precious gift of the original manuscripts in the holy handwriting of the Rebbe (Rashab), *nuch nafshei*. Beyond the matter of *pidyon shvuyim* involved in this—as we discussed—which is a singular act, the *taanug* derived from this, and the content of the letters, are matters that continue and persist, renewing themselves and recurring each time one studies them.

It is understood that I hold you in deep, heartfelt appreciation for the pleasure of the opportunity to meet once again face-to-face, and for the possibility of our private conversation, even though the time at our disposal was not at all sufficient for the scope of the matters we discussed, and certainly not for those we did not discuss, which we will address in writing at the appropriate opportunity.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all of the above, including (my hope) that you will be given the opportunity to rest from your travels and visits. For although there were certainly many matters of personal satisfaction and *nachas ruach*, even matters of *taanug* sometimes leave one in need of rest.

With respect and appreciation,

## 191

By the grace of Hashem, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Eikev,
Brooklyn, N.Y.
20 Menachem Av, 5726

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

May it be the will of Hashem that you bring good tidings in your content,

As it is at the beginning of this week’s parsha: "And Hashem your G-d will keep for you... and He will bless you... you shall be blessed above all peoples... and you shall eat and be satisfied and bless Hashem your G-d..."

Where "and you shall eat and be satisfied" also (alludes to and) includes everything detailed afterward (in the warning "Take heed to yourself"): "you shall eat and be satisfied, and you shall build good houses and dwell... and all that you have shall multiply."

As explained in the Zohar on our parsha regarding the nature of the blessing: "'Blessed' — this is the mystery of the supernal source, to pour out, to draw down, and to illuminate all the lights."

My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, explained: The three expressions — "to pour out, to draw down, and to illuminate" — can be understood because "Blessed," which is the mystery of the supernal source, namely *Yesod* of *Abba*, corresponds to *Chochma*, which is the *Yud* in the Name. This contains three aspects, which are the three letters of the *Yud*: the *Yud* (a point), the *Vav* (a line), and the *Dalet* (a surface). These also allude to *Chabad*, for *Chochma* includes *Binah* and *Da’as* as well: *Yud* is *Chochma*, *Vav* is *Da’as*, and *Dalet* is *Binah*. This is "to pour out" from the *Yud*, "to draw down" from the *Vav*, and "to illuminate" from the *Dalet*, for the illumination of light is in expansion, which is a surface. End quote.

The simple meaning of this is that there should be a "pouring out," and the very essence of the blessing (not merely an illumination) should be revealed from the supernal source of the blessing and drawn down below, and the supernal blessing should illuminate all matters in their details,

(As stated in the verse) until — "and you shall be satisfied."

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

***

I have not found that this Zohar is cited in the *Talmudic Encyclopedia*. In my opinion, it would be worthwhile to complete this in a future edition.

***

In response to your questions: It is found in many places in *Chassidus* that there are explanations for the words of our Sages and customs, even though we do not practice them in Chabad, and even more than that — even when the **halachic ruling** is not so. The reason is that both these and those are the words of the living G-d (*Chassidus*).

Regarding the "etc." (*ko*) in *Iggeres HaKodesh* where it seemingly should be "etc." (*go*): I noted this in the introduction to the "Indices" at the end. It should be added that, as is apparent from the approbation of "the Rabbis, the sons of the Gaon, etc.," most of *Iggeres HaKodesh* was printed from the students' transcripts; see the approbation there.

***

Regarding the health, sleep, etc., of your wife, *tichyeh*: You must ask a doctor again now and act according to his advice — for the sake of *refuah*.

***

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 16th of Menachem Av. May it be the will of Hashem that you continue in your good work in your notes, going from strength to strength — "and all that you have shall multiply," a true satisfaction.

***

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from the 15th of Menachem Av and the one preceding it. May it be the will of Hashem that you bring good tidings in their content.

I was **greatly disappointed by the "actions" regarding the generator. I hoped that as I wrote, it would be set up one week earlier**, and since then many **months** have passed! And finally — they come with a question... whether to buy a generator!! Nevertheless (and despite all this, etc.), I am writing once again (and may it be the will of Hashem that at least now there will be no bad tidings) the answer to your question — per Rashi in *Balak* (22:7):

If **they buy it at this time** (**immediately** upon receiving this letter), there is substance to it, and if...

***

The delivery was delayed, and your letter from the 3rd of Elul was received. Regarding the organization, etc. — if it is as you wrote: the religious *moshav* is as it should be, and they want to accept him (as a trial — meaning, to see if he will fulfill what he takes upon himself), then (if your wife, *tichyeh*, agrees to this of her own good will) you should enter the *moshav* and he should fulfill (as he promised) the conditions of work there as required, and Hashem will grant success.

And furthermore (and this is the main thing, and it concerns *parnassah*), it is essential that peace dwell between you (him and his wife, *tichyeh*). For this, it is necessary that each one yields a little of their own and does not enter into contentiousness and the like. And after that, a man and a woman who have merited, the *Shechinah* dwells between them. And may you bring good tidings.

## 9,193

B"H, 24 Menachem Av, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 18 Menachem Av, in which you write regarding Mrs. ...

Generally speaking, it is not appropriate to answer one person regarding the affairs of another, as is understood.

Nevertheless, as an exception to the rule, I am providing a response in this letter, provided, of course, that the phrasing and style of the question are consistent with the opinion of the aforementioned individual.

1) The surprise regarding the notification that the necessary improvement in her spiritual state has not yet been fulfilled—but that she hopes to improve the situation in the near future—is understandable. If in material matters, "the sooner the better," then all the more so regarding spiritual matters, where every moment and every action is a "whole world." This is especially true when one is in need of Hashem’s blessing, which includes making the proper decisions (in the present, not just in the future) regarding important matters.

2) Regarding the proposal of honorable individuals, as to whether there is a place for disclosing one’s age, she should turn to a Rav or a *moreh hora’ah* in her vicinity, who will instruct her in the *da’as Torah* regarding this.

3) Her traveling abroad does not seem right to me. Regarding *Eretz Yisrael*, it is said, "The eyes of Hashem your G-d are upon it from the beginning of the year to the end of the year." The conduit and vessel for receiving this blessing is conduct in daily life that is consistent with the instructions of our Torah—*Toras Chaim*—and the fulfillment of its *mitzvos*, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them."

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

***

**The eyes of Hashem your G-d are upon it from the beginning of the year to the end of the year**: *Eikev* 11:12.

**Regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them"**: *Acharei* 18:5.

## 996

996

B"H, Erev Shabbos Mevarchim Chodesh Elul, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Convention of N'shei U’Bnos Chabad, Kfar Chabad, may Hashem grant them life,

Blessings and peace!

It was with pleasure that I received the news regarding the scheduling of the convention for Monday, the first day of Rosh Chodesh Elul, the coming year.

Generally, when the sons or daughters of Yisrael gather, it is said of them, "And Your people are all righteous," which is good for them and good for the world. This is especially true when the purpose of the gathering is, from the outset, to strengthen the activities of establishing and disseminating traditional Judaism, illuminated by the light and vitality of Chassidus. Furthermore, there is present here the merit of a *mitzvah* performed by the many, and the merit of the many.

There is an additional, special quality to this convention, as both the place and the time are conducive: it is taking place in Kfar Chabad, may it be rebuilt and established, on Rosh Chodesh of the month of mercy, the month of Elul—the acronym for *Ani L’Dodi V’Dodi Li* ("I am to my Beloved and my Beloved is to me"), as emphasized in the teachings of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe. As explained there, it is based on the parable of a king who, before arriving in the city, is met by the townspeople who go out to greet him in the field, at which point they are permitted—

—and my father-in-law, the Rebbe, adds: **"and are able"**

**"for anyone who wishes to go out to greet him, and he receives them all with a pleasant countenance," etc. This is explained at length by the Tzemach Tzedek—this year being the centennial of his *hillula*—in his sefer *Ohr HaTorah*. **

**May it be Hashem's will that the convention yield the hoped-for results, and even more than anticipated, beginning immediately at the convention itself and continuing to increase in the days that follow. May each and every one of the participants, and all N'shei U’Bnos Chabad in general, and all those who will join them—may they live—see blessing and success in their activities, as mentioned above: activities permeated with the light and vitality of Chassidus, and in a manner of "adding and increasing."**

**Since the convention is on Rosh Chodesh Elul, which is the time for wishing one another a *ksiva v’chasima tova*, may Hashem bless each and every one of them, together with all their family members—may they live—with a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.**

**With blessings for success, for good tidings, and for a *ksiva v’chasima tova*,**

**M. Schneerson**

---

 Yeshayahu 60:21. See Sanhedrin, beginning of Perek Chelek.
 See Sanhedrin 71a, end of side b (in the Mishnah).
 Shir HaShirim 6:3; see Shaar HaPesukim of the Arizal on this verse. Referenced in Sefer HaMaamarim Melukat, Vol. 2, p. 82, note 67.
 See *Likutei Torah*, Parshas Re'eh, p. 32; for the addition by the Rebbe, see the *maamar* "Lecha Amar Libi," 5710, p. 285. *Ohr HaTorah*, Parshas Re'eh, "Anochi Nosein Lifneichem Hayom Bracha," Vol. 2, p. 802 and onwards. Regarding the time for wishing *ksiva v’chasima tova*, see *Mateh Efraim*, Orach Chaim 581:9.

## 9197

B"H, 28 Menachem Av, 5726
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 21 Menachem Av, in which you write that lately you do not see much success in your situation and affairs.

In general, regarding the matters of the sons and daughters of Yisroel, an increase in fulfilling the will of Hashem—by increasing in the study of Torah and the performance of His mitzvos in daily life—adds to the blessing of Hashem in all that a person and his household require, in livelihood, in nachas from children, and in all his affairs. And regarding matters of goodness, holiness, Torah, and mitzvos, even if the situation is already good, there is always room to increase, since these are connected to Hashem, Who is Ein Sof.

It is understood that what has been said also includes strengthening one’s trust in Hashem Yisbarach, Who oversees every single person with hashgacha pratis. Indeed, regarding this it is said, "Hashem is my shepherd" (when one contemplates this and conducts himself accordingly, then) "I shall not lack."

It is appropriate that you have your tefillin checked, as well as the mezuzos in your home, to ensure they are all kosher according to the law—if they have not been checked in the last twelve months—and that every weekday, before putting on tefillin, you set aside a few coins for tzedakah.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 998

B"H, 28 Menachem Av, 5726
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 23 Menachem Av, in which you write regarding the delays thus far concerning shidduchim.

The instruction in such matters is well-known: to focus primarily on ensuring that the prospective partner is consistent with the verse, "A woman who fears Hashem, she shall be praised" — meaning, one who observes the mitzvos in her daily life.

It is understood that the aforementioned is [to be achieved] through increasing one’s conduct in daily life so that it aligns with the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of life, and in the fulfillment of its mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "And he shall live by them". Indeed, in matters of goodness and holiness, no matter how good the situation may be, there is always room to add, since we are connected to Hashem, who is Ein Sof.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

Regarding influencing children: We see tangibly that often, one can exert more influence through friends than through direct influence, even from those closest to them. This is on the condition that they speak about it once, twice, or more, with words that come from the heart, and that it is not obvious that the awakening and the action originated with them.

Furthermore (and this is the main point): If at all times we are commanded to "ascend in holiness," how much more so when one is in need of a special blessing, particularly regarding a matter of such great importance as one’s child. *V’k”l*.

## 9100

9100

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Elul, 5726
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 26th of Menachem Av, in which you write regarding the housing issue in Kfar Chabad and the difficulties involved therein.

It would be well for you to speak once more with the Vaad of Kfar Chabad, and naturally, you may say that you are doing so in accordance with my advice.

May Hashem Yisbarach assist you with a good arrangement, good both in ruchnius and in gashmius—for among Yidden, gashmius depends upon ruchnius, as one sees when one reflects upon it, and it is surely unnecessary to elaborate on this matter.

From this, my attitude toward the second part of your letter is understandable, in which you write regarding the plan of your son, may he live, concerning his studies in the future. It is astonishing that one would even think in such a way.

Hashem Yisbarach led you and your family, may they live, with miracles and double miracles, rescuing you from that country intact—not only in gashmius, but also regarding Yiddishkeit. This miracle succeeded in actual fact, and you ascended to Eretz Yisrael, Eretz HaKodesh. And now, one wishes to give away the best time of life, the years of youth, to study such things that one could have attained in that country as well—and perhaps learned even better than in other places—and to do all this instead of thanking Hashem Yisbarach in a **fitting** way, which is meant by strengthening oneself in following the will of Hashem Yisbarach as indicated in the Torah, up to the Shulchan Aruch, and to pursue that which was not possible in that country, and to do so with simcha and a good heart.

All the more so, and *kal v'chomer*, when it was connected with mesiras nefesh, one did whatever was possible and did not take anything else into account, in order to conduct oneself according to the will of Hashem Yisbarach. And now that you have come to freedom, to conduct yourself as you wish and as **you ought**, someone comes and argues that although **Hashem Yisbarach** is the One who sustains and provides for all with His goodness, with grace, kindness, and mercy, He will, chas v'shalom, be unable to provide for one unless one has a piece of paper stating that one studied in this or that place. Therefore, one must give away so many hours, days, weeks, months, and years for all those things in which **that** country distinguishes itself.

I do not wish to elaborate on such a painful matter, especially since I am certain that what is written above will be sufficient to see the matter as it is in truth.

And especially as we stand in this month of Elul, when every Yid says twice a day, "Hashem is my light and my salvation"—that Hashem Yisbarach, and **only** Hashem Yisbarach, illuminates his life and helps him.

According to your writing, the letter was sent via airmail express.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

***

**9100**

**Twice a day**: See Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 9, p. 170, and the sources noted there.

## 9101

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. According to the teaching and emphasis of the Baal Shem Tov that every matter is by Divine Providence, my hope is strong that you are utilizing the strengths and opportunities granted to you in your capacity as Chairman of the Regional Council to establish the region in both the material and the spiritual, in the manner and tradition of our people, the Children of Israel, in all their settlements, and all the more so in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established—in a manner where the spirit prevails over the material, and the form over the substance. And surely, for someone of your standing, further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

I recall that we met in our youth in the home of my father, of blessed memory, in Yekaterinoslav. Surely, at the next opportunity, you will inform me of your name at that time, as I do not recall the name "Guber" from those days, though you surely changed your family name as is customary in the Holy Land.

#### ***9101***

**A meritorious matter is brought about on a meritorious day**: Ta'anis 29a, and elsewhere.

**When we begin to wish**: See Mateh Ephraim, Orach Chaim 581:9.

**The teaching and emphasis of the Baal Shem Tov that every matter is by Divine Providence**: See Kesser Shem Tov, Additions, section 19 and onwards, and elsewhere.

## 903

B"H, 2 Elul, 5726
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished R' Aharon, may he live.

Shalom and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 25 Menachem Av.

Regarding your question: If one who sustains **one** Jewish soul is considered by the clear ruling of Chazal as having sustained an entire world, how much more so is this true for tens of souls, and even an entire community. For when Bnei Yisrael study the Torah—which is our very life—in a manner that influences the life of the student (in the style of Chazal: "study that leads to action") to the point where there is a strong hope that it will shape his life, one is thereby sustaining him, giving him life, and bringing him to the life of the World to Come, as well as to the life of This World (the kind that is truly worthy of the name "life").

Based on this, it is understood that your path for the future is clear: to fulfill the request of the community and continue your activities there for a further period of time. Through this, may Hashem’s blessing be added to your personal affairs as well, and in the most essential point—much true nachas from all your offspring, may they live.

With blessings for good tidings and to be inscribed and sealed for good.
