## 9105

B"H, 8 Elul, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. Esther Berman, may she live and be well,

Blessings and peace!

I have received the happy news that you have been privileged to preserve in your possession manuscripts (*bichlech*) of Chassidic maamarim that were originally delivered by our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, and transcribed by those who heard them and by scribes.

As a rule, these *bichlech* exist in several copies, and the vast majority were once part of the collection of *bichlech* and the library at the Rebbe’s house, but during the years of upheaval and war, many of them were lost and scattered. It is understood that in order to clarify and refine the text and wording as much as possible—and especially to prepare them for publication—it is necessary to compare all the versions. For anyone who possesses a *bichl* or *bichlech*, it will be considered a great merit to send them here, for this is the rectification and the purpose of the Chassidic *bichlech*: the dissemination of the wellsprings of Chassidus, the Torah of our Rebbe, the Baal Shem Tov, may his merit protect us.

The magnitude of the merit in this—the merit of disseminating the wellsprings and the merit of the many who study the books of Chassidic Torah published by us—is beyond description, and it is certainly unnecessary to elaborate on this to one such as yourself, given my knowledge of your family and the rock from which you were hewn.

"Merit is brought about through the meritorious," and for the sake of the meritorious, the esteemed Chassid, a man of action and many accomplishments, Rabbi Moshe Pinchas HaKohen Katz, may he live, is currently visiting the Holy Land (may it be rebuilt and established). He holds the authority to act as a representative to receive them. You will surely be happy to entrust the *bichlech* to his hand so that they may be brought here even before the upcoming Rosh Hashanah, during these days of favor, to increase your merit in anticipation of the new year that is approaching us and all of Israel for good and for blessing.

With blessings for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both body and soul,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 9156

B"H, 12 Elul, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the day on which "it was doubled for the good" [Tuesday], in which you write that it has been several years since your wedding and you have not yet been blessed with children.

At a time of favor, I will mention you at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Since the delay in receiving Hashem’s blessing for children often stems from a lack of precision in observing the laws and statutes of *taharas hamishpachah* (the laws of *niddah*, *hefsek taharah*, immersion in a *mikveh* that is *kasher*, etc.) due to a lack of knowledge regarding all the details involved, you must clarify all these details with a *rav* who is a *moreh hora'ah*, and resolve to observe them as required from this point forward.

It is understood that the above is within the context of your general daily conduct, which should be in accordance with the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of life, and in the fulfillment of its *mitzvos*, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them," with an increase in this from time to time.

After strengthening yourselves in the aforementioned conduct, you should once again consult with an expert physician and follow his instructions.

Regarding the specific details of the treatment you mention in your letter (surgery, etc.), first and foremost, you must clarify with a *rav* who is a *moreh hora'ah* whether it is permitted according to our Torah, the Torah of life.

It is appropriate that you have your *tefillin* checked, and every weekday, before putting on *tefillin*, you should set aside money for *tzedakah*—it goes without saying that the setting aside of *tzedakah* should be without a vow.

With blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*.

## 9007

9007

B"H, 12 Elul, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, distinguished, and prominent individual, a man of the people who is elevated above the people, who seeks the good of his nation, a man of noble character, a scion of a noble lineage, R' Shneur Zalman, shlita,

Greetings and blessings!

Sent to you in a separate package are the kuntresim of the maamar "Nachamu" from the year 5716, delivered by the Rebbe (Rashab), n'e, which was said on that Shabbos. It is based on the kuntres "Nachamu" of 5626, which was printed in honor of your visit and presented to you personally. That kuntres contained only a list of points, and the Rebbe, n'e, expanded upon it in his discourse (though he did not write it down himself, relying on the recording in the kuntres from the year 5626). It was recorded by one of the listeners present at that time, who was among the primary chozrim and those who grasped the content, Rabbi R' Eliyahu, shlita, Simpson, whom I requested to visit you and farbreng with you on the fifteenth of Av at your hotel in New York.

This is analogous to what the Rebbe, my father-in-law, wrote in several of his reshimos: how the history of the Chassidic movement parallels the history of our people in general, and specifically in relation to our Torah, "Toras Chaim"—which means, even in its literal sense, a directive for daily life, since the Torah is eternal and transcends the constraints of time and space. Examine this and you will find that the core of the maamar "Nachamu" was already stated (apparently) by the Tzemach Tzedek, and is based on the words of our Alter Rebbe spoken about two hundred years ago. Subsequently, they were repeated with additional explanation by the Rebbe Maharash on Shabbos Nachamu 5626. On Shabbos Nachamu of this year—the day of our meeting on the evening following that Shabbos—it was exactly one hundred years to the day. Afterward, they were repeated in a slightly different manner by the grandson of the Tzemach Tzedek, and later became the subject of conversation between one who was named after our Alter Rebbe and one who heard the maamar himself and recorded it in the year 5716, who happened to meet and farbreng together in a hotel in New York. And now, these Chassidic discourses will not depart from the mouths of those who study them in our Holy Land, both in Jerusalem, the capital city, and in Kfar Chabad, the place of settlement for the descendants of the chassidim of our Alter Rebbe. This is characteristic and full of significance.

We were delayed somewhat in sending the kuntresim to you, as they were only brought from the bindery these past few days, even though the initial plan was for them to be ready by the approach of Friday, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, 20 Menachem Av, the day of your departure for the Holy Land, t'u. For this reason, the sending of the check we discussed during your visit here was also delayed; it is in the amount of ten thousand dollars, in connection with the founding, construction, and establishment of the second Kfar Chabad, in the vicinity of the first Kfar Chabad ("double comfort"), and it is enclosed herewith.

With respect and blessings—though it is my hope that we will correspond again before the onset of the year—in the traditional and accepted style, dedicated from generation to generation, for a good and sweet year, inscribed and sealed for good.

## 9108

B"H, 12 Elul, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter of August 18—which was received only now—in which you write regarding your daughter, may she live, who has known this young man for some years and met with him several times, and who recently stated that she is not interested in him because he is a "fanatic" (kanai), and you ask for my opinion on this.

Since regarding fear of Hashem, the verse explicitly states, "Fear Hashem and keep His mitzvos, for this is the whole of man", it is worthwhile (in an appropriate manner) to endeavor that your daughter, may she live, again take an interest in the aforementioned honorable proposal, until it reaches a successful conclusion in a good and auspicious hour.

Of course, if the aforementioned is indeed the only reason—and while there is no point in forcing a daughter or son of Israel regarding a shidduch—you must explain to your daughter, may she live, the great happiness and importance of a life lived according to our Torah, the Torah of life, and the fulfillment of its mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them". And regarding anyone who adds to this, our Sages of blessed memory have informed us that Hashem adds to his blessings. Even though people sometimes label this addition as "fanaticism," there is also a type of fanaticism regarding which it is said, "in his zeal for My zeal" —the zeal of Hashem, which is the source of blessing, success, and happiness.

At a time of favor, please mention your daughter and all that you write about on the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Based on the tone of your letter, it is surely unnecessary to emphasize that an increase in matters of Torah and mitzvos adds to Hashem’s blessings in all that is needed. This refers to one’s conduct in daily life, as the wisest of all men said, as written above: "Fear Hashem, etc."

It would be proper to have his tefillin checked, as well as the mezuzos in your home, to ensure they are all kosher according to law—if this has not been done within the last twelve months. And she should maintain the good custom of kosher daughters of Israel: to set aside money for tzedakah before lighting candles every Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov.

With blessings for a *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 919

B"H, 15 Elul, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

...And as we stand in the *yimei ratzon*, the days of the month of Elul, the month of mercy—

During these days, as the Alter Rebbe states, Hashem is like a king whose "countenance is received in the field, and then everyone is permitted"

(And my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, adds and explains: "and is able")

"to go out and greet him, and he receives them all with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to all"—

May the King, the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He, fulfill—while still in the field—all the requests and desires of the hearts of all who greet Him, for the good, within the totality of *Klal Yisrael*, and may He fulfill them (as above) with a pleasant countenance.

And may each and every one be inscribed and sealed for a good and sweet year, in revealed and manifest goodness.

And today is the day when the moon (of this entire month) stands in its fullness.

With the blessing of *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah*,

**Menachem Schneerson**

 **In the days of favor (yimei ratzon):** See Rashi on Shemos 33:11; Tur, etc., Orach Chaim 581.
 **Month of mercy:** See also *Dah Ani L'dodi*, 5710.
 **Alter Rebbe:** In *Likutei Torah*, Parshas Re'eh, p. 32.
 **Adds and explains:** In the *maamar* beginning "Lecha Amar Libi," 5718.
 **With a pleasant countenance:** See the Commentary on the Mishnah to Avos 1:15. Note the comment in the Commentary on the Mishnah there (3:12): "with joy, and this is greater, etc." It could be said that this refers to *Chag HaSukkos*, "the time of our rejoicing," which follows Elul and the *Aseres Yemei Teshuvah*, the days of *Shammai*—his ways (see *Likutei Torah*, Shir HaShirim 48:3), but this is not the place to elaborate.

 **919:** General-specific. Printed in *Sefer HaMinhagim-Chabad* at the beginning (and see letter 929 below) and in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 7, p. 312.
 ***Dah Ani L'dodi*, 5710:** *Sefer HaMaamarim 5710*, p. 150 and onward.
 ***Sdah Lecha Amar Libi*, 5718:** *Sefer HaMaamarim 5718*, p. 167; 5710, p. 285.
 **All requests:** See *Ohr HaTorah* by the Tzemach Tzedek (this year being the centennial of his *histalkus* and *hillula*), Parshas Re'eh, glosses to the aforementioned *Likutei Torah* (p. 808): It may be said that then, in Elul, the illumination of the aspect of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy shines also upon the outer *shoshana* (rose). See there.
 **The moon stands:** That Yisrael count by the moon (Sukkah 29a) and are likened to the moon, corresponding to its changes (see *Shulchan Aruch*, Yoreh Deah 179:2; *Zohar* Vol. I, 181a; *Sefer HaMitzvos* by the Tzemach Tzedek, 31a).
 **The moon stands... in its fullness:** *Zohar* Vol. III, 215a, and elsewhere.

## 911

B”H, 16 Elul, 5726.

To my dear relative, Mrs. Devorah Leah, may she live, and Mr. [Yosef], may he live,

It is with great sorrow that I express my participation in your mourning over the passing of your relative, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing man, and man of integrity, R’ Shlomo HaKohen, of blessed memory. I offer the traditional blessing: May the Omnipresent comfort you among the other mourners of Tzion and Yerushalayim.

From now on, may you know no more sorrow or sighing, and may only goodness and kindness pursue you always, all the days of your life.

With blessings for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, with revealed and manifest goodness.

On the face of it, the phrasing of the blessing of consolation, which links the matter of comfort with the mourning for Tzion and Yerushalayim, is difficult to understand. However, in this very point lies the essence of the consolation, and it consists of two aspects—though time does not permit an elaboration: 1) The mourning of the individual is, in truth, the mourning of the collective, and this is emphasized by joining the mourner with the mourners of Tzion and Yerushalayim—that is, the entire **collective** of Israel. 2) The comfort of the individual is a true and **guaranteed** comfort, exactly like the comfort of Tzion and Yerushalayim, which is a foundation of our faith—a faith of life. **And in the manner of** the comfort of Tzion and Yerushalayim, regarding which it is said, “I will thank You, Hashem, for You were angry with me; let Your anger turn away and You will comfort me” (Yeshayahu 12:1)—where the “thanking” applies also to the “anger”—so too is the promise regarding the comfort of the individual, and even more than what is written is found here.

## 914

B"H, 20 Elul, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 17 Elul, in which you write regarding the questions and answers you received from some individuals in Kfar Chabad.

May Hashem Yisbarach, who watches over each and every person with *hashgacha pratis*, guide you in the way that is good in His eyes in all respects.

You write that you are a *shamash* in the *beis medrash* in the Kfar; you have surely heard the teaching of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the important work of a *shamash*, in the phrasing: "Call to the sun (*shemesh*) and light will shine," and "Do not read it as *shemesh* (sun), but as *shamash* (sexton)." This means that a *shamash* must illuminate the *shul* (*beis medrash*) with true light, and also, quite simply, that it should be bright. As explained in *Shulchan Aruch*, a *beis medrash* must be well-lit, and it must also be clean. In a physical sense, this is achieved through proper maintenance, and in a spiritual sense, it is achieved by ensuring that the order in the *beis medrash* is maintained, and that *Siddurim*, *Tehillim*, *Chumashim*, and the like are always ready for use.

In connection with this, it is understood **what** your place should be, and in what manner you should maintain all of this in its entirety throughout the whole year—and all the more so in the days preceding the month of Tishrei, the *yemei hateshuvah*, and the month of Tishrei (which, as explained in many places, is the "seventh month," replete with *Yomim Tovim* and *yemei ratzon*, etc.). At that time, the **responsibility** of the *shamash* is **many times greater**. Hopefully, you will do all of the above with *simcha* and a good heart, for "one who comes to purify himself is assisted."

With blessings for good tidings and for a *kesivah vachasimah tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe,
Secretary

## 915

B"H, 21 Elul, 5726
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 14 Elul, requesting a blessing in connection with your future position at the Beis Rivkah Seminary in Kfar Chabad.

Regarding such matters, we have been promised in our holy Torah—the Torah of life:

a) "One who comes to purify himself"—and it is well known how our Alter Rebbe emphasizes that this includes purifying *others*—"is assisted," and furthermore:

b) "If you have labored and found [success], believe it."

It is my firm hope that you will apply yourself to your position with the appropriate *mesiras nefesh* and dedication, in the education of the "children of the Omnipresent" (as it were), and that the aforementioned promise will be fulfilled for you.

It is surely unnecessary to emphasize that if every single one of the Jewish people is expected to be a living example of a person who conducts their life according to the instructions of our Torah—the Torah of life—then this is all the more true for an educator and guide.

Especially in an institution whose purpose is to prepare teachers, that is to say...

## 9116

B"H, 23 Elul, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and scholarly R. Schneur Zalman, may he live, a man of noble character and a scion of distinguished ancestors, and to the entire family, may they live:

Peace and blessing!

I was saddened to hear the news of the passing of the esteemed and G-d-fearing R. Avraham, of blessed memory.

May the Omnipresent comfort you among the other mourners of Tzion and Yerushalayim.

From now on, may you find only goodness and kindness all the days of your life.

With appreciation, respect, and blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*.

***

On the face of it, the style of the blessing of consolation—linking the matter of personal comfort with the mourning for Tzion and Yerushalayim—is difficult to understand.

However, in this very point lies the essential element of consolation. It consists of three points, though time does not permit an elaboration:

a) This individual mourning is, in truth, also the mourning of the collective. This is emphasized by associating the mourner with the mourners of Tzion and Yerushalayim—that is, all of Klal Yisrael.

b) The consolation of the individual is a guaranteed consolation, just as the consolation of Tzion and Yerushalayim is a guaranteed consolation, which is one of the foundations of our faith—a faith of life.

c) The consolation is a **true** consolation, similar to the consolation of Tzion and Yerushalayim, regarding which it is said: "And you shall say on that day" (for now, this is not understood at all), "I will thank You, Hashem, **for You were angry** with me; Your anger has turned away, and You comfort me." The "I will thank You" refers to the "You were angry." Such is the blessing and the promise in the consolation of the individual—"among the other mourners of Tzion and Yerushalayim," may it come to pass speedily in our days.

## 917

By the Grace of G-d
Days of Selichos, 5726
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life.

Peace and Blessing!

In addition to the annual themes—the matters that every Yom Tov, and Rosh Hashanah in general, brings with it from year to year—

Matters which must also be contemplated and experienced *kechadashim* (as **new**), just like all matters of Torah and mitzvos, which are the **life and life-force of a Jew (for they are our life and the length of our days), and the essence of life is always new and fresh, even for a person who has already lived many years—**

**There are also special matters that are connected to specific years, and are therefore of particular significance in the year in question.**

**The coming year, 5727, which is approaching us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, is a post-Shemittah year, when a special matter comes to the fore—the mitzvah of Hakhel (gathering), which is "a firm pillar and a great honor for our religion."**

**In the time of the Beis HaMikdash, in the post-Shemittah year, the people were required to be gathered—men, women, and children, even very young children—in the Beis HaMikdash to hear a selection of passages from the Torah, which were read by the King. This was to be done at the first opportunity in the year when they could be gathered (Sukkos, when Jews would come to Jerusalem).**

**And although since the destruction of the Beis HaMikdash the mitzvah of Hakhel is not practiced—until the Beis HaMikdash is rebuilt, speedily in our days—nevertheless, Torah and mitzvos are eternal. Thus, even those mitzvos that are only practiced *bizman habayis* (in the time of the Temple) have their spiritual, inner content—a special significance (at the designated time of the day or year) in all times and places. This must be expressed, and one must fulfill it in an appropriate manner (e.g., tefillos at the time of day when the korbanos were brought, etc.).**

***

The mitzvah of **Hakhel** had two points that, on the surface, seem to be a contradiction: On one hand, it required *Hakhel es ha'am, ha'anashim v'hanashim v'hataf v'gercha asher bish'arecha*—a gathering of the highest to the lowest of the Jewish people, which demonstrates that every single person, regardless of their status or situation, has a connection to it. On the other hand, it required that the selected passages of the Torah be read to the gathered assembly by the highest among the Jews, the King.

One of the explanations for this is:

Torah must animate a Jew—all Jews without exception, *anashim, nashim, taf, gerim*—permeating him through and through, every person’s entire existence, to the fullest extent and in all details, until all his senses and feelings are permeated with Torah and mitzvos, with Elokus.

And in order to achieve the aforementioned at the deepest level and in the fullest measure, the Torah is read at that time by the King, of whom it is said, "his awe is upon you." He awakens the feeling of *eimah* (awe) and *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke), which nullifies the "I" and the *yeshus* (self-centeredness) of the listener.

***

The significance and instruction of the mitzvah of **Hakhel** for each and every one of us is that we must utilize the days of *hisorerus* (awakening) of the month of Tishrei to gather Jews—men, women, and children, even very young children—to gather them in a holy "place," in a holy atmosphere, and utilize it for the purpose that is the foundation of the mitzvah of **Hakhel**: *Lema'an yishme'u ulema'an yilmedu v'yire'u es Hashem Elokeichem v'shamru la'asos es kol divrei haTorah hazos*—"In order that they may hear, and in order that they may learn, and fear Hashem your G-d, and observe to do all the words of this Torah."

It is especially the duty of anyone who is a "king," a *gadol* in his environment—a Rav in his community, a *mechanech* in his classroom, a father in his family—to let the word of Torah and mitzvos be heard in his circle, with a strength and seriousness that will create a deep impression and lasting influence on the listeners. This should be felt not only in the month of Tishrei, and not only throughout the entire year, but throughout all seven years from one **Hakhel** until the next; an influence that should be expressed in daily life, in conduct according to Torah and mitzvos with *yiras shamayim*, and together with this—*b'simcha u'v'tuv leivav* (with joy and goodness of heart).

***

May it be the will of the Almighty—whom Jews crown on Rosh Hashanah as **Melech Yisrael** and as **Melech al kol ha'aretz**—that He grant every single person the ability to carry out the above to the fullest extent.

And this will also bring closer and hasten the time when we will fulfill the mitzvah of **Hakhel**, with all its details, in the Beis HaMikdash, with the coming of Mashiach Tzidkeinu, *b'meheirah b'yameinu*.

With the blessing of *Kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 919

B"H, 28 Elul, 5726
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter—which was received after a long delay—in which you write about your daughter, *tichyeh*, and her conduct, etc.

We see tangibly that very often one can accomplish more through friends and acquaintances than through the direct influence of relatives and parents, etc. They should speak with her once, twice, or more, with words that come from the heart. Surely you can find such people who will do this, in a way that she will not know that the request and the impetus for this came from you (the parents).

It is understood that you are correct in writing that cutting off the relationship with her entirely, or having her live elsewhere, is not the right approach. Rather, it is possible to carry out the aforementioned [suggestion] in a way that cannot be interpreted as giving a *hechsher* to her undesirable conduct. Surely a way can be found for both matters to be fulfilled, and may you be able to share good news regarding this.

This is especially relevant as we are in the month of Elul, and the words of our Rebbe, the author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, in his book *Likutei Torah* (Devarim, p. 32b) are well known. He explains this based on the parable of a king in the field before he enters the city, where all the townspeople go out to greet him, and he receives them all with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to everyone—see there.

It would be appropriate to have your *tefillin* checked, as well as the *mezuzos* in your home, to ensure they are all *kosher* according to the law—provided that the *tefillin* and *mezuzos* have not been checked within the last twelve months. Also, every weekday before putting on *tefillin*, set aside a few coins for *tzedakah*.

Your wife, *tichyeh*, should observe the good custom of *kosher* Jewish women to set aside money for *tzedakah* before lighting the candles every *Erev Shabbos* and *Erev Yom Tov*.

With the blessing of *Kesivah v’Chasimah Tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

Secretary

P.S.

It is well known the story of the righteous Rabbanit, Mrs. Rivkah, regarding the response of her father-in-law, the Tzemach Tzedek (whose birthday is today), to her son, the Rebbe (Rashab), that Shabbos Shuvah means "a *Shabbosdige* Teshuvah." During the weekdays, that which is forbidden is not in the house, whereas on Shabbos, even that is present in the house; therefore, one must know beforehand—regarding everything one wishes to do—whether it is permitted. And the fact that they placed a wick for oil in the candle of Teshuvah and in the candle of Chaim provides the strength to fulfill this (*Kuntres Tzav*).

Their *pidyon nefesh* was received.

## 9223

[5726]

In our times, for several reasons (including *dirash*), it is not appropriate to commit oneself—and certainly not another—if the plan is for the wedding to take place after a long time. On the contrary: the shorter the time between the decision and the wedding, the more praiseworthy it is.

#### ***9223***

Published in *Likkutei Sichos* Vol. 14, p. 303.

**In our times**: A response to someone who wanted to become engaged with the understanding that the wedding would take place after a long time. See also above, letter 9134, and the references in the notes there.

## 924

[5726]

**Question**

In the *Sefer HaMaamarim* of the Maharash, *Toras Shmuel 5628*, in the maamar "Lehavin M'she'arzu"al D'Adam Kadma'ah...", section 2, page 66, it is stated:

"And so it was with Moshe, of whom it is said, 'And you shall give of your splendor upon him'—a literal giving, **such that he lacked** that light which was given to Yehoshua, and likewise to the Elders, as it is written, 'And I will take of the spirit that is upon you...'"

However, in Rashi on *Beha'aloscha* 11:17, it is stated: "'And I will place upon them'—to what is Moshe likened at that time? To a lamp placed upon a candelabrum, from which everyone lights, **and its light is not diminished at all**."

This question was posed to the *Harav HaChossid* [name omitted] and others, but no answer was found in their mouths.

***

**Response:**

1) Is this based on the *Derech Mitzvosecha*, [section on] the appointment of a king?

2) (See *Sifri* there).

3) How many **seconds** did **everyone together** dedicate to contemplating and searching for a resolution to the above?

In addition to the above, one must investigate the following: In Rashi and the *Sifri*, why is this not explained in the same way regarding the "giving" to Yehoshua, especially since that is a greater innovation?

One must conclude that the case there is different, because it is written, "And you shall give." Based on this, the difficulty in the maamar is **strengthened** (even without the aforementioned), as it states, "and likewise to the Elders, etc."—yet in their case, the term "giving" is not used. What is the necessity to explain that Moshe also lacked something in the case of the Elders? It can be said: The two opinions regarding the Elders are the two opinions in *Bamidbar Rabbah*, chapter 15: 

a) Regarding the Elders, it was like a lamp lighting another lamp (Section 19).

b) That the Elders took from the reward given to Moshe (Section 25) [and based on this, it is understood what the difference between them is]. And the conclusion there—"nevertheless, Moshe did not lack anything"—is simple: because Hashem filled the deficiency. Based on this, it is understood: 1) Why the terminology was changed in this section from the terminology in section 19: "Moshe did not lack anything from his own" [because according to this opinion, he did lack at the time of the act]. 2) That here it adds: **"At the end of forty years,"** which is not in the previous one, even though the verse it cites is also stated at the end of forty years. 3) The change in the proofs of the two sections. And this is well understood.

However, regarding the first opinion concerning Yehoshua, as mentioned above, it interprets **"And you shall give"** (and it is impossible to say, even with difficulty, that this is a borrowed term, for the **explanation** is that there must be two matters: "And you shall lean [your hand]" and "And you shall give." Based on this, the *Midrash Rabbah* (Chapter 21, 15) is understood: "And you shall lean"—like lighting a lamp from a lamp; "And you shall give"—like pouring from one vessel to another).

Now, according to the explanation in the maamar, a difficulty arises: If in the case of Yehoshua it must be in a manner of lacking (due to the disparity in value), then all the more so regarding the Elders! Therefore, it is necessary to bring the matter of the Elders into the maamar as well, and it explains that indeed, it is so, and likewise with the Elders. So that the other opinion regarding the Elders is not entirely refuted—according to the explanation in the maamar—it can be said that according to this opinion, Moshe descended at that time from his level (during the descent of Bnei Yisrael from their level, as in "Did I give you greatness for any reason other than..."). And Rashi, in his commentary on the Torah, whose primary concern is the *peshat*, explained the opinion of "like a lamp from a lamp," **in continuation** of the commentary:

1) Before this (11:16) that the strength of Moshe weakened (like a female—a source for *Beriah, Yetzirah, Asiyah*);

2) After this (11:22) **which implies** that Moshe spoke a difficult word [and the opinion of R. Shimon there is that even at that time Moshe was at the level of "In all My house he is trusted," etc.—like the opinion brought in the maamar];

3) In *Shemos* (32:7).

And note *Torah Or* (3, 1).

## 9132

B"H, 28 Tishrei, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the annual dinner of Yeshivas Achi-Temimim in Newark, may they live:

Peace and blessing!

The matter of chinuch — the upbringing and education of the young generation — is always one of the highest and most important tasks of every nation, and especially of the Jewish people. The holy Torah, **Toras Chaim** — the true guide in Jewish life (**Torah from the word hora’ah**) — places the strongest emphasis on chinuch in daily life (**"And you shall teach them to your children,"** etc.). From the time of Avraham Avinu (**"In order that he may command his children,"** etc.) until this very day, chinuch has been and remains the primary duty of Jewish parents in particular, and of the Jewish community in general.

This year, the matter of chinuch is especially highlighted, as it is a post-Shemitah year, the year of **Hakhel**. This is the special mitzvah that was performed once every seven years, in the time of the Beis HaMikdash, when all Jews — parents and children, even very young children, and even "strangers" (**"and your stranger who is within your gates"**) — were required to gather in the Beis HaMikdash to hear how the **Melech** **himself** read certain portions of the Torah, in order to become imbued with the spirit of Torah, mitzvos, and yiras-shamayim.

This great event specifically underscored the importance of chinuch for young and old alike: it reminded and urged the leaders of the people, and the parents themselves, to fulfill their duty to the fullest extent, and it once again emphasized the significance of chinuch for children of all ages; even those who were still too young to understand (**"and your children who do not know,"** etc.) were required to be present at **Hakhel** as a preparation for later, for Jewish chinuch begins from the earliest childhood.

Although the mitzvah of **Hakhel** cannot currently be performed as it was in the time of the Beis HaMikdash, it remains valid today in its spiritual sense, in that it reminds and calls upon everyone — parents, ordinary Jews, and especially activists, community leaders, and those in positions of influence — to fulfill their duty (which is also an extraordinary zechus) in the field of chinuch al taharas hakodesh, each person according to his or her full capabilities.

It is to be hoped that all participants and friends of Yeshivas Achi-Temimim will, on the occasion of this annual event, express the spirit of **Hakhel**, as mentioned above, in a practical way, by strengthening and expanding all efforts for the benefit of this educational institution, which is one of the main pillars of chinuch al taharas hakodesh in your community.

With respect and blessing for success and good tidings,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 933

933

B”H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, 15 MarCheshvan, 5727

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter...

May it be the will of Hashem that you bring good tidings in their content.

In this year, which is *temimah* (bringing the leap month) and whose months are *shleimim* (Cheshvan and Kislev are full) — may there be *temimus* (wholeness/integrity) and *shleimus* (completeness) in all matters of the year, both physical and spiritual, general and specific.

Especially since immediately following Rosh Hashanah — both in the Diaspora and in the Holy Land, where Rosh Hashanah is also two days, even at the time when they would determine [the months] based on visual sighting (for the Bnei Yisrael in the Diaspora and for most of the inhabitants of Eretz Yisrael, and often even in Jerusalem itself) — it was Shabbos Kodesh, of which it is said, "there is no sadness with it," and "you shall not spread your Shabbos" is not said regarding it. On the contrary, regarding it, it is said, "The blessing of Hashem, it enriches," and one delights in it — from above and from below — physical *taanug* and spiritual *taanug* together.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

***

Regarding memorial services (*azkaros*) and the like that are held for towns, etc. — the **general** matter requires study in the *sefarim* as to what the proper approach should be. Regarding their character and content **in practice** (those that have come to my attention) (most of the speeches, etc.) — in my humble opinion, it should be negative.

***

**Temimah (bringing:** *Arachin* 31a. See also *Reshimos HaTzemach Tzedek* on *Tehillim* on the verse "The Torah of Hashem is perfect (*temimah*)" (Section 4, 8).

**Shleimim... full:** See *Rambam*, *Hilchos Kiddush HaChodesh*, ch. 8, law 6.

**At the time... itself):** *Rambam*, *Hilchos Kiddush HaChodesh*, ch. 5, laws 5-8 (and so it is ruled in *Shulchan Aruch Admur HaZaken*, 600:4. And not like Rashi in *Rosh Hashanah* 18a, beginning of the page (unlike *Tosafos* there). See *Lechem Mishneh*, *Hilchos Kiddush HaChodesh*, ch. 3, law 10).

**And often:** In *Zohar Chadash*, Vol. 3 (231a), "Rosh Hashanah was always two days... and not one."

And it can be explained that this is the addition (and precision) of the Alter Rebbe in *Likutei Torah*, *Drushei Rosh Hashanah*, "He will revive us after two days" (*Devarim* 63b).

***

**933**

General-specific. Published in *Likutei Sichos*, Vol. 8, p. 369, and completed according to a photocopy of the letter. For its content, see also the following letter, 945.

**Reshimos HaTzemach Tzedek on Tehillim**: *Yahel Ohr*, p. 67 and onwards.

"Rosh Hashanah is always two days, even at the time when they would sanctify based on visual sighting" — the emphasis here is "even at the time, etc." — and not "always" in the literal sense. See *Pri Etz Chaim*, *Shaar Rosh Hashanah*, end of ch. 4: "The two days of Rosh Hashanah... are always practiced... Before the destruction, we had the power... on the first day, but now after the destruction, it is necessary to observe two days, as is written in the *Zohar*."

— And in *Yerushalmi Eruvin* (ch. 3, law 10) that the two days of Rosh Hashanah are a decree of the early prophets, and in *Tosefta Rosh Hashanah* (ch. 1, law 5) that in the days of Moshe, two days of Rosh Hashanah occurred.

**No sadness with it:** *Yerushalmi Berachos* 2:7.

**And "spread... not said":** *Zohar Chadash*, Vol. 3, 88b. *Torah Or*, beginning of *Parshas Chukas*. *Derech Mitzvosecha*, *Mitzvas Lo Teva'aru Eish*.

**Regarding it, it is said:** *Yerushalmi* there.

**And spiritual taanug:** See *Shulchan Aruch Admur HaZaken*, 288:3.

**The blessing of Hashem, it enriches:** *Mishlei* 10:22.

**Memorial services and the like:** Written in the margins of the previous letter, in the copy sent to Moreinu HaRav Tzvi Harkavy.

Additional letters to him — above, Vol. 23, 5759, and in the references in the notes there.

## 9334

B"H, 16 Marcheshvan, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the honorable, distinguished, and esteemed individual, a person of stature and elevated character, who seeks the welfare of his people and possesses noble qualities, a scion of a distinguished lineage, R' Schneur Zalman, shlita,

Greetings and blessings!

It is my hope that by the time you receive this letter, you have already received my regards sent from here via the guests from Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, who visited here (and who brought regards from you, and again, thank you). It is a established principle that a *shaliach* fulfills his mission, and they will convey not only my regards from here, but also at least the points of what was discussed here during the seventh month, which, as our Sages expound, is "satiated" (*meshuva*) with everything.

I am writing to you now regarding a matter I have learned of: the details concerning one of the great doers of *tzedakah* in general, and *tzedakah* connected to the dissemination of Torah and its *mitzvos* in particular, a man of character and many accomplishments, etc., Yitzchak Polak, shlita, of 22 Spinoza St., Tel Aviv. There is surely no need to elaborate on the essence of the matter, as based on the documents sent to me, many of our brethren—both those of the *mari Torah* (masters of Torah) type and the *mari ovdin tovin* (masters of good deeds) type—have already appealed to you with a heartfelt and soulful request to grant him clemency as soon as possible and to the maximum extent. And this is not only based on his past, but—I am firmly confident—also based on his future. I mean that he will not only continue his aforementioned good deeds, but also regarding his *tzedakah* and his good conduct in matters between man and his fellow, in addition to matters between man and Hashem.

And since his health is also not in order, there is, in addition to all of this, another dimension of kindness and mercy—abundant and great mercy.

It is understood that I am not entering into the essence of the legal case, its proceedings, and so on, especially since many others who have appealed to you have written about this in detail. I am writing only regarding the practical outcome—in the language of Chassidus, regarding the "therefore" (*b'chen*)—the release of the aforementioned from prison and his return to his home and family, at the earliest possible time, in a good and successful hour.

Perhaps this letter does not conform to protocol, but you surely remember my approach that matters outside of protocol are often the most successful, especially regarding you and your affairs.

I was saddened to learn some time ago that you had entered a "house of doctors" (I do not "subscribe" to the name "hospital," especially since it is the opposite of the house's purpose and goal; rather, it describes the state of the person **before** they enter the house and its treatment). Although the information included an explanation that it was for check-ups, even that is seemingly superfluous, as one should maintain a person in his established status as being healthy, fit, upright, and so on. However, I was relieved to hear a few days ago that you have already returned home and to your work, and my hope is that you have also returned to complete health.

May it be the will of Hashem that—just as a person fulfills his obligation regarding the acceptance of *tzedakah*, Heaven forbid, for the entire year by requesting and receiving *lekach* on the eve of Yom Kippur—you, too, will have fulfilled the matter of receiving help from doctors for the entire coming year, for good, through the aforementioned entry and exit.

With appreciation, honor, and blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. As a continuation of the "above-protocol" conduct mentioned above, I was happy to learn these past few days from a tourist, one of the American *bnei Yisrael* who was in Moscow on Shabbos Nachamu and the following Shabbos and prayed there in the *shul*. He told his acquaintances, **speaking innocently**, how on Shabbos Nachamu they spoke with him (after seeing that he was not to be suspected, etc.) about your visit to New York, and about the friendship and warmth, etc. And on the following Shabbos, they continued the conversation with him regarding your visit here on Motzaei Shabbos Nachamu—or as they put it, "in Lubavitch"—and the magnitude of their joy regarding the aforementioned, etc. Furthermore, the initial acquaintance of several of the *shul* congregants with the aforementioned tourist was as is customary there: they passed by him in haste and words were tossed from their mouths: "From where?" "A New Yorker." "A Lubavitcher?" "No" (I do not know him), "but I have heard," etc. The tourist is still under the impression of the congregants' joy over your visit to the Lubavitch gathering, etc.

## 9235

[16 MarCheshvan, 5727]

In response to the contents of your letters:

a) Regarding the specific matter of leaving the field of the Rabbinate—Heaven forbid, Heaven forbid to even think of such a thing. As for those who have already left (in our times), we (and I take the liberty of including myself among those who feel this way) are pained by it, etc.

If you are considering a path where you would do both—you must take into account from the outset that a commercial venture or the like, as you describe it, has no set time limit, and because of the way it occupies the mind, it possesses a unique power of attraction (for "a novelty is dear to a person," etc.). You must estimate for yourself whether you are capable of limiting yourself in this regard to the extent required.

Furthermore, one must carefully consider the nature of the impression this will make on the *baalei batim* and how it will affect your standing once the matter becomes known (for it is impossible to keep it hidden, and it is only a matter of time—a short time, relatively speaking—until it becomes public).

b) Regarding a school for (Torah and) vocational training—for understandable reasons, *Anash* in Chabad have only engaged in this as an addition and as a secondary supplement to a Chabad *yeshiva*. That is to say, in a place where a *yeshiva* already exists, and after a period of time it becomes apparent to all (even to a critic or a skeptic) that a certain student is unable to continue in the *yeshiva*, then it is the duty of the administration of the institution where they are currently studying to save them from going out into the world by providing a school where they spend part of the day learning a trade, and the like.

c) Regarding the founding of a *yeshiva*—even though our Sages of blessed memory have said regarding such matters that one should "magnify Torah and make it glorious," in the current situation, this is a matter of controversy, etc., etc. Consequently (as you yourself wrote), it is not worthwhile and is not the right course of action.

## 936

B"H, 20 Marcheshvan, 5727
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R' Shlomo HaLevi, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Motzaei Shabbos, along with the enclosure. May it be the will of Hashem that you bring good tidings among us.

This is especially pertinent as we stand on a day of auspiciousness, the birthday of the Rebbe (Rashab), may his soul be bound in the bond of life.

Regarding this day, it is said that for every person, their *mazal* is strengthened; how much more so for a *tzaddik tamim*, whose days are complete (*temimim*) and who "comes in days," lacking not a single day.

And in the case of a *tzaddik* who is a *Nasi* of Israel, when he ascends, all those who follow in his footsteps—his students, and the students of his students, and so on—ascend with him, and this is well understood.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 9,337

[Late Cheshvan 5727]

Regarding your questions in the aforementioned letter, and since time does not permit an elaboration at all:

1) We have spoken many times that the simplest example for understanding "knowledge and free will" is that a person who knows the future is not in contradiction at all (or more accurately, it is not relevant at all) to the (free) choice of the one who is known. In other words: what contradicts choice is compulsion, **not** knowledge.

2) From this it is understood that this is not at all a matter of Hashgacha (or knowledge) at the time of the event.

3) Regarding how every detail, even in inanimate objects, relates to the general intent—this can also be explained **simply**: that **any** change that occurs in any place whatsoever has consequences that are felt throughout the entire world, because the whole is a unified reality.

4) According to the opinion of the Moreh Nevuchim **and all** Jewish philosophers that there is no Hashgacha Pratis except regarding man, etc.—one can resolve the aforementioned difficulty that all events in the inanimate, vegetative, and animal realms also influence man, yet the details are not under Hashgacha; for it is the **sum total** of **many** events that influences man, and according to them, it makes no difference **in practice** which parts comprise that sum total or how it is gathered. And this is clear. A **tangible** example: the basic calculations of insurance companies. And this is clear.

## 9138

9138

B"H, 1 Kislev, 5727
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., R' Sh. Y. (may he live),

Shalom u'Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your prompt letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh, and many thanks for the good news contained therein.

Regarding your question concerning your birthday — for long days and good years:

Given the reasons from the past (as they remain in their place), it is my opinion that it is very appropriate to mark this day (especially since this year is a Shnas Hakhel) with a gathering of friends and associates, limited in number (since you do not desire excessive publicity).

And if "when ten sit together, the Shechinah rests among them," even if they are not speaking words of Torah, etc. (as per the words of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, in Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 23, "that I heard from my Rebbes" [the Maggid and the Baal Shem Tov, as explained by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, on this]), how much more so at the aforementioned gathering, where they will surely speak words of Torah — in Nigleh and Chassidus, and in Nigleh and Chassidus together. And "a note from Heaven descends" — that Hashem should fulfill the blessings of those gathered, who are marking this for your honor (may you live), in their entirety.

And [may it be] in a manner appropriate to what is mentioned in the chapter of Tehillim, which is the custom of the ancients for one to recite in their upcoming year: "He established it as a testimony in Yehosef... Open your mouth wide and I will fill it," with all the commentaries thereon, and according to what is explained in the Tzemach Tzedek’s notes on this verse (which are printed together with the Tehillim).

With blessings for long days and good years in personal matters and in general matters (including, of course, the most essential matter — the publication of Volume 12 of the Talmudic Encyclopedia, a mitzvah in which he is particularly diligent, and in close proximity to this — the 13th volume, etc.), and for good news as mentioned above.

**M. Schneerson**

939

P.S. From time to time, I have the opportunity to see your writings in various journals regarding matters of *refuas hanefesh* (healing of the soul). For someone like yourself—and especially based on what I recall from our conversation in the past—it is superfluous to emphasize that *refuas hanefesh*, concerning every Jewish soul, is bound up with the extent of its *hiskashrus* to Torah, about which it is said, "for they are our life and the length of our days," and to the fulfillment of its *mitzvos*, about which it is said, "and he shall live by them." And if, for every person, the health of the body is bound up with the health of the soul, then for a Jew, this matter is emphasized and highlighted to an even greater degree.

If you have recently published any books or *kuntreisim* or the like, I am sure that, in accordance with your good custom, you will send them to our library, and I thank you in advance.

## 6,140

B"H, 17 Kislev, 5727
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your notification that a daughter has been born to you, mazal tov!

May it be the will of Hashem that you and your wife, may she live and be well, raise her to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, in prosperity.

It is known from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory, that our custom is to say "to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds" even upon the birth of a daughter, based on the words of our Sages (Berachos 17a): "Through what merit do women attain [the reward of the World to Come]? Through sending their sons to study Torah... and by waiting for their husbands to return from the beis medrash..." 

With blessings for mazal tov.

I wrote to you previously regarding a daily shiur in Tanya (without a neder, of course). This is relevant and connected to your request at that time for a blessing, and to your being mentioned at the tziyun of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory (similar to the words of our Sages regarding prostrating oneself on the graves of the righteous). Furthermore, there is a special connection to being a conduit and vessel for blessing through the portion of Torah in which the one giving the blessing labors specifically, and so on. And this is understood.

May it be the will of Hashem that, at the very least, from now on you will observe (without a neder) the daily Chitas shiurim.

***

 **It is known from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory**: See his Igros Kodesh, Vol. 1, p. 210 (also recorded in Hayom Yom, 25 Menachem Av).

 **Similar to the words of our Sages regarding prostrating oneself on the graves of the righteous**: Sotah 34b.

## 6141

6141

B"H, 17 Kislev, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants in the annual Chanukah dinner of the Parents and Teachers Association of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch in Montreal,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I was pleased to receive the notification regarding the upcoming annual Chanukah dinner, which this year will mark the 25th anniversary of the existence of the Lubavitcher Yeshiva in Montreal.

On this occasion, it should also be emphasized that the current year holds special significance for chinuch, being a year of **Hakhel**, as this matter was discussed in the letter for Rosh Hashanah. The mitzvah of **Hakhel**—gathering the people: men, women, and children, in the Beis HaMikdash, to hear sections of the Torah read by the King, in order to awaken in them yiras Hashem and to strengthen their daily conduct according to Torah and mitzvos—has evoked in everyone, man and woman, an intensified sense of responsibility for **chinuch al taharas hakodesh**—a responsibility and duty that must be fulfilled every year, and in this year of **Hakhel**, even more so.

Although in the present time the responsibility for chinuch has, to a great extent, been transferred to the educational institutions with their teachers and educators, this does not mean that parents have been absolved of their personal duty to fulfill the mitzvah of **"v’shinantam l’vanecha"**—to implant in their children Torah, yiras shamayim, and the performance of mitzvos in daily life. This must be expressed, first and foremost, in the education, guidance, and influence within the home, and also in active cooperation with the educational institution and teachers, to help them carry out their shlichus—as representatives of the parents—to the fullest extent, and on their part, to fulfill the **"v’shinantam l’vanecha"**—these are the students.

Since the dinner is taking place during the Yom Tov of Chanukah, and a few days after the **Yom HaGeulah** of the Alter Rebbe, the Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, it is to be hoped that all participants will express the spirit and content of these luminous days through intensified activity for the benefit of the institution, which is conducted in the spirit of the Baal HaGeulah—which means for the benefit of the chinuch of the students, may they live.

May Hashem Yisbarach help that the harmonious cooperation and fruitful activity should constantly rise and grow, in accordance with the directive to **"maalin bakodesh"** (increase in holiness), as this is also brought out in the mitzvah of the Chanukah lamp—**"mosif v’holech"** (increasing and continuing)—to light another glowing candle each night of Chanukah, and to spread as much as possible the light of **"ner mitzvah v’torah ohr."**

With blessings for success and for a happy and bright Chanukah.

#### ***6141***

**Letter for Rosh Hashanah**: See above, letter 6137, and the notes referenced there.
**"V’shinantam l’vanecha"**: Vaeschanan 6:7.
**"These are the students"**: Sifrei and Rashi on the verse.
**"Maalin bakodesh"**: Berachos 28a, and elsewhere.
**"Mosif v’holech"**: Shabbos 21b.
**"Ner mitzvah v’torah ohr"**: Mishlei 6:23.

## 7144

B"H, Yom HaGeulah, 19 Kislev, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Congregation of Yeshurun, lovers and supporters of Torah and mitzvos,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

In connection with the upcoming annual dinner of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch on Sunday, Parshas Beshalach, 4 Shevat, I turn to the lovers of Torah in general, and to the friends of the Lubavitcher yeshivos in particular, to utilize the coming weeks to ensure that this annual undertaking is carried out with success in all respects, both financially and spiritually.

If in every year a Jew must remember and fulfill his obligations toward **chinuch al taharas hakodesh** (education in complete purity), then this year—a year of **Hakhel** (as discussed in the Rosh Hashanah letter of this year)—is a time that calls upon all Jews, men and women, young and old, to strengthen the cause of education to the greatest extent.

The coming weeks until the annual celebration are especially illuminated by the bright days—19 Kislev and 24 Teves—which are connected to the Alter Rebbe, Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch and founder of Chabad. The celebration itself takes place during the week of 10 Shevat—the yahrtzeit-hilula of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the founder of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim here in this country, ztzkllh"h, nb"m, zya.

It is well known to what extent the Nesi'ei Chabad of all generations have placed emphasis on the study of Torah and chinuch al taharas hakodesh. Suffice it to mention that the first sefer the Alter Rebbe printed was **Hilchos Talmud Torah**, where, right at the beginning, he brings down the halachic ruling that the education of a Jewish child begins from the moment he begins to speak.

In this spirit, the Lubavitcher yeshivos encompass the education of Jewish children from their earliest youth until adulthood; an education in accordance with Hakhel—**"In order that they may hear, and in order that they may learn, and fear Hashem, and observe to do all the words of this Torah"**; an education that aims to turn the students into educators, **"neros leha'ir"**—shining lights, who illuminate their entire surroundings with **"ner mitzvah v'Torah ohr."**

I wish to hope that all the friends of the Lubavitcher yeshivos, with the askanim of the yeshiva at their head, may they live, will mobilize all their strength to ensure the success of the annual celebration, which is so vital for the existence and further development of the Lubavitcher yeshivos. And whoever adds, they add to him blessing and success in everything one needs, both materially and spiritually.

With respect and blessing for great success in all the above, and with the blessing of Chag HaGeulah,

**M. Schneerson**

## 3745

By the Grace of Hashem
Motzaei Shabbos, 20 Kislev, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed...
Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters...

May it be the will of Hashem that you bring good news in all of these matters—a double good (the supernal, hidden good that manifests within the revealed and manifest good).

Enclosed is the *maamar* "Podeh B'Shalom" — delivered fifty years ago, in the year [5677], by my father-in-law, the Rebbe (Rabbi Shalom DovBer) *n.e.*, and which was repeated in public at the *farbrengens*.

[It discusses] the "day of good tidings," the 19th of Kislev, the sixth day "on which 'it was good' was doubled, the day of the great *hillula* of our holy Rebbe *n.e.*"

And the 20th of Kislev—the day on which the redemption was **publicized** and the joy was great, etc. Especially in this year, which is also the Shabbos (the elevation and drawing down of *taanug*) of the 19th of Kislev.

You should certainly endeavor to have it studied in public and in private in the days that follow, particularly during the upcoming days of Chanukah, the days of *pirsumei nisa* of the cruse of oil, the secrets of the secrets of the Torah, and in a manner of "increasing and ascending" in light.

And in this year, which is a "complete" year (bringing the leap month) and whose months are full (Cheshvan and Kislev are full)—may there be completeness and perfection in all matters of the year, both physical and spiritual, general and particular.

Especially since it immediately follows Rosh Hashanah—both in the Diaspora and in Eretz Yisrael (where Rosh Hashanah is also two days, even at the time when they would determine the calendar based on the sighting of the moon—for the children of Israel in the Diaspora and for the majority of the inhabitants of Eretz Yisrael, and often even in Jerusalem itself)—it is a day of *Shabbos Kodesh*, of which it is said "there is no sorrow with it," and the prohibition "do not spread out your Shabbos" does not apply. On the contrary, it is said of it: "The blessing of Hashem, it enriches," and one delights in it—from above and from below—physical *taanug* and spiritual *taanug* together.

With blessings,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 9140

9140

By the Grace of Hashem, 21 Kislev, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the Chanukas Habayis celebration of the "Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch" girls' seminary in Casablanca, may they live:

Shalom and Bracha!

I received with pleasure the news regarding the Chanukas Habayis celebration of the girls' seminary, which will take place on the night of the second day of Chanukah, may it come upon us for good. May it be the will of Hashem that the celebration be worthy of its name, with outstanding success in all details, both materially and spiritually.

It is unnecessary to elaborate on the great value of this joy, given this important achievement in education on the foundation of purity and holiness.

I have already stated that this year is especially a year of *segulah* for all matters of kosher education, as it is the year of **Hakhel**. This is the year following the seventh year, the *Shemitah* year, in which, at the time the Beis Hamikdash existed, a great mitzvah was added—a "strong pillar and great honor in the religion" (*Sefer HaChinuch*), the mitzvah of "Assemble the people, the men and the women and the little ones, and your stranger who is within your gates, so that they may hear and so that they may learn and fear Hashem your G-d, and observe to do all the words of this Torah." And, following the principle of our Sages, of blessed memory, that "whoever occupies himself with the Torah of the *Chatas* is as if he offered a *Chatas*," so too, the "Torah" of the mitzvah of **Hakhel** in this time is to increase efforts and engagement in expanding education on the foundation of purity and holiness. And if we are commanded to pursue holy education every single year, how much more so in this year, the year of **Hakhel**, which emphasizes in particular the obligation of the community and the obligation of the individual to act and to accomplish, to the greatest extent possible, for the education of the sons and daughters of Yisrael—an education saturated with *yiras Hashem* and *ahavas Hashem*, *ahavas haTorah*, and *ahavas Yisrael*.

Especially since the celebration takes place during the days of Chanukah, there is an additional point here: one must not be satisfied with the achievements of the past, but rather must increase efforts and endeavors in all matters of kosher education, as per the instruction of the days of Chanukah—whose mitzvah is to kindle the lights in a manner of **"adding and increasing, adding and shining,"** by spreading the "lamp of mitzvah and the light of Torah."

All the education activists and participants in the joy of the aforementioned Chanukas Habayis are worthy of blessing for having merited this important achievement in the development and expansion of the girls' seminary, founded by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *Nasi* of our generation, *zechuso yagein aleinu*—an educational institution conducted in the spirit of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*, whose day of redemption we have recently celebrated, and who sacrificed himself for the dissemination of Torah and mitzvos in general, and for education in particular.

May it be the will of Hashem that the inspiration of these days of *segulah* and days of light will stand by all those who work and act for the education of the sons and daughters of Yisrael in the path of Torah and mitzvos, and may the success that has shone upon them until today continue to light their way in the future, to go from strength to strength. And may we all merit, together with all our brethren the Children of Yisrael, the "psalm of song for the dedication of the house"—the great and holy Beis Hamikdash, which will be built speedily in our days by Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With great respect and with a blessing for abundant success and good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9292

By the Grace of G-d
Days of Chanukah, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. Devorah Leah
May she live

Blessings and peace!

I received your letter with its enclosure in due time. Please forgive the delay in sending this confirmation, which was due to several reasons, primarily based on the teaching of our Sages that "merit is brought about through a meritorious day."

These days, the days of Chanukah, have the mitzvah of lighting candles from the time the sun sets, in a manner of "increasing and going on" from day to day. The lighting is done in a place (and in a manner) that illuminates the outside as well—but with a light that comes from within—or in the words of our Sages, "at the entrance of **his house from the outside**."

Just as the results of the first Chanukah lasted throughout that year and the years that followed—when they entered the Sanctuary of your house, cleared [the idols], purified [the Sanctuary], and lit the candles—so too, the results of the days of Chanukah each and every year serve as a remembrance (and in a manner) of what was done for our ancestors in those days.

Another characteristic point regarding Chanukah is that although the reason for lighting the Chanukah candles is the miracle of the seven-branched Menorah, the fulfillment of the mitzvah is through an addition to that reason (eight candles).

Seemingly, "light" and "joy" are two separate matters. Moreover, the verse distinguishes between them: "Light is sown for the righteous, and joy for the upright of heart." As our Sages emphasize, not everything is for light and not everything is for joy; the righteous are for light, and the upright are for joy (Ta'anis 15a). Yet, there is certainly a great connection between them. This connection is understood based on what is said: "From the mouth of the Most High, evil does not emerge," and in the well-known expression, "Everything the Merciful One does, He does for the good." However, human intellect is limited by nature, and the concealment of the world around us—and the darkness within it—further intensifies this limitation. As a result, one fails to penetrate to the depth of matters. But when, through the kindness of G-d, the darkness surrounding a person is illuminated—and the channel and path for this is our Torah and its mitzvos, of which it is said, "A mitzvah is a candle and Torah is light"—this light illuminates and reveals the truth of every matter and its consequences, which ultimately leads to joy.

Regarding the mitzvah of the days of Chanukah and their content, women are obligated just as men are. According to the commentary of Rashi, the foremost of the commentators, it was through a woman that the miracle was performed (Shabbos 23a).

The explanation and the lesson of all the above—there is surely no need to elaborate regarding you.

Best regards to your son, may he live—and to both of you, with wishes for an illuminating Chanukah and for the continuation of this light throughout all the days that follow.

With blessings,

## 953

953

[Days of Chanukah, 5727]

Regarding your note on Rashi (and the same difficulty applies to the Sifri there) that he did not include (Haazinu 32:48) "on this very day" [in the list of instances where the Torah uses this phrase] (Lech Lecha 17:23, 26). One should add that the force of the difficulty is that Rashi’s commentary there is in the same vein as his commentary on Haazinu.

However, as with all of Rashi’s commentary on the Torah, this too is resolved simply: Avraham Avinu is not in the same category as the three instances Rashi cites, because the verse itself concludes and explains it: "on this very day... as G-d had spoken to him."

#### ***953***

Copied from a photocopy of the original handwritten letter, on the margin of a letter from R. Shneur Zalman Shmerling, dated 28 Marcheshvan, 5727.

Additional letters to him—see above, Vol. 17, p. 34, and the references in the notes there.

**Regarding your note on Rashi, etc.**: In his letter: During the farbrengen on Shabbos Shuvah, [the Rebbe] explained the Rashi that states that "on this very day" is written three times [the sicha—in Likutei Sichos, Vol. 19, p. 339 and onwards]. At the time, I found it difficult why Rashi does not mention the "on this very day" regarding Avraham Avinu, "on this very day Avraham and his son Yishmael were circumcised."

**Rashi’s commentary there**: On that very day that he was commanded, in the daytime and not at night, he did not fear the nations or the mockers, etc.

**In the vein of Rashi on Haazinu**: The Holy One, blessed be He, said: "I will bring him in at midday, and whoever has the power to protest, let him come and protest."

**As G-d had spoken to him**: That is to say, the reason he performed the circumcision on that very day was "as G-d had spoken to him," and he did not fear the nations or the mockers; whereas here, Rashi writes that in three places the Holy One, blessed be He, said it must be specifically at midday, etc.

This resolution was also explained in the sicha of Parshas Haazinu, 5741. And in Likutei Sichos there, note 2, another resolution to this is explained.

## 957

B”H, Zos Chanukah, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter...

As we stand at the conclusion and seal of the days of Chanukah, the day of Zos Chanukah, may it be the will [of Hashem] that the lighting and the light of these candles, and their effect, continue throughout all the days that follow.

This effect is *pirsumei nisa* (publicizing the miracle). In the language of Chassidus, this is the concept of "until the foot ceases from the marketplace"—that the aspect of the "foot," which is the spark of Elokus residing within Knesses Yisrael (as it is written, "and the earth is My footstool"), should be prevented and cease [from being trampled]. This is especially true in this generation, the *ikvos meshicha* (the heels of Moshiach), which is literally the aspect of feet and heels.

[The goal is to remove this spark] from the "marketplace," which is the aspect of *reshus harabim* (the public domain), the *turi deproda* (the mountains of separation).

It should be noted that in the days of the wicked Greek kingdom, when the *paritzim* (the men of Greece) entered the Beis Hamikdash and desecrated the Altar, etc., and took all the vessels of the Sanctuary, the Bnei Yisrael—through their *mesiras nefesh*—were victorious over them. They rebuilt the Altar, inaugurated it, and did the same for the Menorah, etc. By lighting its candles on the 25th of Kislev, they inaugurated them for the holiness of all the days of their existence.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

***

The Hachnosas Sefer Torah in Kfar Chabad should follow the order found in the letter of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding this, but without publicizing at all that it is in his memory, etc.

The time for the entry should be one of the days between the 10th and 13th of Shevat, Purim Katan, or the like.

***

See Shulchan Aruch Admur, *Mahadura Basra*, end of Siman 1: "He shall recite the section of the *korban* immediately... on the day, etc." I am puzzled, as I have not seen people practicing this. Perhaps it is because Admur did not include it in the *Seder Birchas Hanehenin*. But should the explicit ruling in Shulchan Aruch Admur, as mentioned above, be nullified because of this difficulty?

Seemingly, one should distribute charity for the needs of the many (see *Magen Avraham* 217:2), which is within everyone’s ability. However, I have not seen this practiced either, and it would seem worthwhile to establish this custom. One could connect this (charity) and explain it based on what is written in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, "Katonti," that every act of *chesed*, etc., must be accompanied by an increase in one's own humility, and consequently, there is an increase in the *chesed* one performs (see *Ohr HaTorah*, Vayeira 97, end of side b and onwards).

## 958

By the Grace of Hashem, Zos Chanukah, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Tuesday and those preceding it. The *pidyon nefesh* will be read, G-d willing, at the *tziyun*.

As we stand at the conclusion and seal of the days of Chanukah, which follow closely upon the 19th of Kislev—the "Day of Good Tidings"—we must explain the common denominator between the days of Chanukah and the 19th of Kislev.

The miracle of Chanukah was with oil—which alludes to the *pnimiyus haTorah* (the inner dimension of Torah)—for the lamps of the *Mikdash*. Their place was specifically in the *Heichal*, where not everyone could enter, and the time for their lighting was during the day.

However, in the days of Mattisyahu ben Yochanan Kohen Gadol and his sons, who sacrificed themselves for *Kiddush Hashem*—the true *yichud*, as the Sages say, "with all your soul, even if He takes your soul"—the miracle occurred. Through this, they were commanded regarding the Chanukah lamps, whose *mitzvah* is for every single person to light them at the entrance of their house, from the outside, and specifically after sunset.

All these matters are reflected in the study of *pnimiyus haTorah*—the "oil of Torah."

Initially, it was hidden and concealed from all but the most select few, and even then, it was practiced with great modesty, not in public. But in these latter generations, it is a *mitzvah* to reveal it—beginning in the days of the Arizal, and culminating in the redemption of the 19th of Kislev, which initiated the primary effort of *hafatzas hamaayanos chutzah* (spreading the wellsprings outward), until every person can understand and grasp how *Hu memale kol almin* (He fills all worlds) and *Hu sovev kol almin* (He encompasses all worlds), and so on.

May it be the will of Hashem that each of us acts in this regard, in all three particulars:
1) In the manner of *hafatzah* (dissemination);
2) The wellsprings themselves;
3) Until they reach even the "outside."

And may this be done with vitality, light, and a state of *mosif v'holech v'or* (increasing and brightening).

With blessings to continue the light of Chanukah throughout the entire year,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S.

In response to your questions:

a) It is well known that the Sages ruled that a groom is forgiven for all his sins, and likewise a bride.

b) It is well known that sadness is **utterly** rejected in *Chassidus* (and *a fortiori* despair—especially when it has no basis). This is particularly true when one sees tangibly that it detracts from the vitality in fulfilling *Torah u'mitzvos*.

c) From this, it is understood that the *Sitra Achra*—who is an "expert" in his craft—uses the above as his primary tool, with stubbornness, etc. Is it really necessary to explain that one should not listen to an "old and foolish king"?

d) The advised counsel for an inappropriate mood—in this specific case—is the study of *nigleh* and *Chassidus* with vitality and abundance, both by oneself and with others. After all, the "task" is, in any case, to become a *lamdan* (scholar), in the literal and simple sense of the word.

e) A special *segulah* for increasing *Siyatta Dishmaya* in the above is the *tzedakah* of *hafatzas hamaayanos chutzah*. *V'ka'l*.

f) The expression "where his heart **desires**" in the words of the Sages refers to which *masechta*, etc., to study (*Avodah Zarah* 19a); regarding the **place** of study, the expression is "where he **wants**" (*Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah*, end of section 240).

g) Since a beautiful dwelling expands a person's mind, one should endeavor that their living quarters not be cramped.

h) We conclude with goodness—that each of them should experience true and inner joy.

## 8105

B"H, 21 Teves, 5727
