## 9176

[Thursday, 23 Teves, 5727]

Regarding comforting mourners via letter:

On the face of it, the mitzvah of comforting mourners is exactly as its name implies—that the mourner should be comforted thereby. This is especially true according to what is written (Rambam, Hilchos Avel, beginning of Chapter 14) that this is an act of *gemilus chasadim*, and *gemilus chasadim* can be performed even through a letter. Furthermore, the fact that it can be done through a messenger (Shmuel II 10:3) proves that it is not a mitzvah that must be performed *b’gufi* (personally). And what is written in the Rambam (ibid.)—"And these are the acts of *gemilus chasadim* performed *b’gufi*"—is intended only to distinguish it from *tzedakah* (which is mentioned there in Halacha 3). The act of carrying the bier on one’s shoulder (which is a physical act) serves as proof. This can be further reinforced by the continuation there (Chapter 14, Halacha 6), that this is an act of *gemilus chasadim* with the living and with the dead. Since for the dead there is no difference between speech and a letter—and see Shabbos (152a), "a dead person who has no..."—it is possible to say that comforting mourners is a *gemilus chasadim* performed solely for the dead (and it could be said that the Raavad and Rambam argue on this—Hilchos Avel, Chapter 13, Halacha 4. But this is not the place to elaborate).

And although there must be an opening [of conversation] first by the mourner, it is logical to say that there is no need for an opening for each person **individually**. Once he has opened [the conversation] to one person, the other present individuals may also offer comfort. This is the simple meaning of the verse regarding the necessity of the opening: "And no one spoke to him... for the pain was very great. After this, Iyov opened his mouth... and Elifaz answered" (Iyov, end of Chapter 2; Moed Katan, end). Furthermore, and most importantly: if the letter is opened by the mourner (even if he knows its content is comfort) and the mourner opens it to read it, there is no greater "opening" than that.

Based on the above, for someone who, due to circumstances beyond his control, is unable—despite his desire and will—to come personally to comfort the mourner, there are two paths before him: through a messenger (as mentioned above regarding the written word) or through a letter (and it seems to me that there are many *teshuvos* that end or begin with the formula for comforting mourners). Each has its own advantage, and it is best to combine both.

9160

B”H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, after midday,
Brooklyn, N.Y.
24 Teves, 5727

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter...

And on the day of the histalkus and hillula of the Alter Rebbe—who from his earliest days on earth was “bound in a single bond with the Holy One, blessed be He,” and at the time of his histalkus “lifted his soul to Him with joy and a good heart,” and “all that he labored in throughout his days ascended with the root of his soul as he ascended at that hour”—

And from above to below, it is a general principle that “all the toil of man that his soul labored in during his lifetime, above in a state of concealment and hiddenness, is revealed and shines in a state of revelation from above to below at the time of his passing,” and “the kindness of Hashem shines from eternity to eternity upon those who fear Him, and He works salvation within the land.”

And year after year, these days—when they are remembered (as they should be, for then all the illuminations and influences) are brought about.

And the body follows the head; all those who study his Torah, etc., which, as his name **Shneur** implies, is exactly so—the **nigleh** of Torah and the **pnimiyus** of Torah (**Toras HaChassidus**), **a study that leads to action, the fulfillment of mitzvos with fear and love, as we are commanded and as is explained well by the Baal HaHillula in his holy Tanya and his maamarim of Chassidus.**

**May it be the will that in our generation, the footsteps of Moshiach—which is the Erev Shabbos after midday (in the count of the six thousand years of the world’s existence)—we complete the preparation for receiving the Shabbos, and with the beginning of “those who taste it have merited life,” to taste from every “dish” of the day of Shabbos while still on Erev Shabbos.**

**And just as the essence of the day of Shabbos is rest, and we are commanded to honor it and delight in it—so too should this preparation be with rest, honor, and delight.**

And may we merit soon, in our time, the fulfillment of the promise, “And I will feed you with the heritage of Yaakov your father,” a heritage without boundaries, and as it is written, “And you shall spread out to the west, and to the east, and to the north, and to the south.”

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

Regarding your note on what was explained that in a case of *ones* (duress), we do not say “it is as if he performed it”—see the Yerushalmi, Kiddushin (Chapter 3, Halacha 2).

It is discussed at length in *Beis HaOtzar* (by Maharil Engel), Rule 27. And although seemingly it is simple in Tanya, Chapter 32, that one cannot say “it is as if he performed it,” it can be explained according to what is explained in the *Kuntres Acharon* on the *maamar* beginning *Ayin Es Chayim* regarding *neran*. But this is not the place to elaborate.

And as for “tossing oneself about with this,” etc.—in my opinion, it is highly questionable whether you should continue in this, for ultimately, “one does not confer a benefit upon a person in his absence [or against his will].” And what will be if, **Heaven forbid**, the request for resignation is accepted?!

## 6159

[Teves, 5727]

Please request from the secretariat a copy of the text for the soldiers in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. The points are:

The saying of the Baal Shem Tov that **everything** one sees, etc. — is a directive for fulfilling one’s role as a human being, and all the more so regarding a constant matter (which continues for a long time).

The point of the military and the **foundation of its existence** is **absolute obedience**. Even regarding a command that is logical — it is **forbidden** to wait to fulfill it until one contemplates and understands it with one’s intellect (for by doing so, one could endanger the **entire** army and the **war**) — rather, the main thing is "we will do." This is also the case regarding a soldier who is a great expert in military tactics — **"we will do" must precede "we will hear."**

All this applies even if the commander is physically flawed, G-d forbid, and full of shortcomings, etc., provided that he has "ordination" (has been appointed as commander) by the General Staff.

And as mentioned above, the fate of the **entire** country depends on the fulfillment of all this.

And if this is the case with a commander of flesh and blood, how much more so with the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He.

#### ***6159***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 14, p. 295 (dated approximately 5729), and completed according to a copy; it is addressed to R' Moshe Peller.

**The saying of the Baal Shem Tov**: See also above, Letter 5159, and the references in the notes there.

**The point of the military**: See also above, Vol. 14, Letters 4991, 5235; Vol. 18, 6822; Vol. 19, 7042.

**"We will do" must precede "we will hear"**: See Shabbos 88a.

## 270

[Beginning of Shevat, 5727]

As we spoke when he was in my room—he must return to Eretz Yisrael, settle there regarding a livelihood, and find a shidduch. Given his age, it is advisable to find a shidduch as soon as possible (especially since G-d-fearing Sephardim generally marry at an earlier age), and therefore, as mentioned above, this should be done promptly. However, he must set aside fixed times each day for Torah study and set aside at least a maaser of his earnings for tzedakah. Through this, Hashem will grant him success in his ascent in yiras shamayim, Chassidus, and so on—in addition to the blessing in gashmius in the literal sense. And as with all good matters, all of this must be done with true joy and strong bitachon in Hashem.

He should discuss with the yeshiva administration when he will travel and be successful in his journey.

As a shlichus: If it is possible **in ways of peace**, then upon his return to Eretz Yisrael, he should, on Shabbos and Yom Tov, share appropriate points from what was discussed here in the maamarim or sichos, etc., at gatherings of our fellow Sephardic Jews or in their shuls.

## 771

B"H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Bo, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the 27th annual dinner of the Merkaz HaYeshivos Tomchei Tmimim Lubavitch,
May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom u’vracha!

With this, I send my greetings and blessing to the esteemed askanim, guests of honor, and all participants in the annual celebration of the Merkaz HaYeshivos Tomchei Tmimim Lubavitch.

This year, the annual celebration has been scheduled for the first day of a week that holds special significance for Lubavitch institutions, and consequently, for all friends and supporters of the Lubavitch yeshiva. This is the week of the yahrtzeit of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, the founder of the Lubavitch yeshivos in America.

The concept of a yahrtzeit is to refresh and strengthen the connection with the one whose yahrtzeit it is, through matters of goodness and holiness that held deep and internal significance in the life of the individual during their time in this world. By doing so, one provides true nachas ruach to the soul of the one whose memory is being preserved and sanctified; and simultaneously, one acquires a great zechus by uniting with the spirit of the one whose yahrtzeit it is, continuing his holy work in an intensified measure.

It is known what a place the Lubavitch yeshivos occupied in the life of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and with what mesiras nefesh he strove to ensure their existence and development. The greatest nachas ruach one can provide for his soul is to help his institutions fulfill their mission to the maximum extent—both in quantity, by increasing the capacity to accept as many students as possible, and in quality, by strengthening and deepening the education of the students in the spirit of Torah with yiras shamayim and mesiras nefesh.

Every additional student in the Lubavitch yeshiva is not only an achievement for the student himself, but also an achievement for generations to come, because through him, a new Jewish generation is established, and in time, a Torah-true Jewish home. Added to this is the special quality of the Lubavitch approach to chinuch—to implant in the students a deep sense of responsibility and mesiras nefesh for a fellow Jew, in accordance with the great principle in the Torah—**"Love your fellow as yourself,"** as a foundation in daily life.

I hope that each and every one of the participants, and the friends of the Lubavitch yeshiva in general, will make a special effort to ensure the success of this year's dinner in all respects. The zechus of the one whose yahrtzeit it is, the founder of the yeshiva, will surely stand by everyone to be blessed by our Father in Heaven, from His full, open, holy, and generous hand, in both gashmius and ruchnius alike.

With respect and blessing for outstanding success and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***771***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 11, p. 236.

**Great principle in the Torah - "Love your fellow as yourself"**: Kedoshim 19:18 and in Toras Kohanim and Rashi.

## 9 Adar

B"H, 11 Shevat, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter of Thursday, along with the enclosure.

At an opportune time, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires for the good in all the matters about which you write.

Regarding matters of health, a person must do what is incumbent upon him through natural means. Especially since the Torah states, "and he shall surely heal" (*v'rapo yerapei*), which grants permission to a physician to heal; therefore, you should act according to the instructions of a specialist doctor.

Furthermore, and most importantly, contemplate the concept of *Hashgacha Pratis*—especially as explained by our teacher, the Baal Shem Tov, as will be explained to you by the *anash*—may they live—who are in your camp and vicinity. From this, one arrives at the immediate conclusion, in the style of the Sweet Singer of Israel: "Hashem is my shepherd, I shall not lack," and "Hashem is with me, I will not fear."

It is appropriate that you have your *tefillin* checked—if they have not been checked in the last twelve months—and also that you maintain the three daily *shiurim* of *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*, as is well known.

With blessings for good tidings in all that is mentioned.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

Your *pan* has just been received and will be read at the holy resting place.

## 970

B"H, 12 Shevat, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Rabbi Kalman, known as Dr. Kahana,

Shalom u’Bracha!

Thank you for your thoughtfulness in sending me the two publications regarding autopsies. Since they were received during these auspicious days, close to the day of the Hilula of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will take the liberty of enclosing a letter I wrote to several of my friends, which I hope will be of interest to you.

In closing, much like the opening, may it be Hashem’s will that an end finally come to autopsies, and also, of course, to the "autopsies" performed on the living souls of our fellow Jews through obstacles and concealments in their path of ascent in holiness—living according to the Torah of life and the mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them." May all those who have been instrumental in the aforementioned autopsies now act with double the wisdom and utilize the characteristic of the Jewish people—who are the boldest among the nations—to fight the wars of Hashem, to compel all of Israel to walk in the path of the Torah, and to strengthen the breach. Through this, may we merit the fulfillment, speedily in our days, of the prophecy in the words of the great teacher, the Rambam: "A King from the House of David will arise, who studies the Torah and occupies himself with the mitzvos like his father David... and he will fight the wars of Hashem"—this is our righteous Mashiach—"and Israel will be great sages and know the hidden things, etc., and the earth will be filled with the knowledge of Hashem as the waters cover the sea" (end of Hilchos Melachim).

With respect and blessing.

P.S. On this occasion, I would like to draw your attention to something I have seen in several Pagi publications: the depiction of the Luchos with a semi-circular top. This is a custom of the nations of the world, which is the opposite—if one may make a distinction—of the words of our Sages, of blessed memory, who stated that they were six [handbreadths] long, six wide, and three thick (Bava Basra 14a). In our publications, especially those for children, we are precise about this (as enclosed).

## 9176

B"H, 15 Shevat, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. Devorah Leah
May she live

Blessings and peace!

It was with sorrow that I learned of the state of your health. My hope is strong that it is steadily improving, and regarding your efforts in the natural way—following the doctor's instructions—may it be Hashem’s will that the full verse be fulfilled in this: "And Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you **do**," with a speedy recovery.

This is especially relevant as we stand on the day of Rosh Hashanah La'ilanot, when new powers are added to the world of vegetation. And since "man is the tree of the field," and furthermore, all parts of the inanimate, vegetative, animate, and speaking levels are found within man—in the style of our Sages, of blessed memory, that everything that exists in the world has its counterpart in man (who is called a *olam katan*), except that the "speaking" part of man, and even the "animate," relate more to the *neshamah* and its matters, whereas the "vegetative" part pertains to the realm of the body, including its healing and its being in proper health, etc.

However, even the body and its matters in every single one of Bnei Yisrael are included in the life of the spirit. And in the style of the great teacher, the Rambam—whose profession was that of a physician of the soul and body alike—the body being healthy and whole is one of the ways of Hashem (Hilchos De'os, beginning of Chapter 4).

With blessings for a speedy recovery.

## 978

B"H, Erev Shabbos, Parshas Im Kesef Talveh Es Ami,
5727. Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration of the Shomrei Shabbos Free Loan Society (Gemilas Chasadim),
May Hashem keep them alive.

Greetings and Blessings,

I received with pleasure the news that you are holding your annual meeting on Motzaei Shabbos, Parshas Im Kesef Talveh Es Ami.

May it be the will of Hashem that it be a successful and auspicious occasion, especially since this year is the year of "Hakhel," which adds to the matter of Gemilas Chasadim and Tzedakah.

For the concept of Hakhel is the gathering of people who are distinct and different from one another, to the point of extreme diversity—in the words of the verse, "men, women, and children, and the stranger who is within your gates." This is especially so according to what is explained in many places: that all participate in Hakhel, from the greatest of the great down to a day-old infant, all together at one time, with one call for all, by the one who is unique among the people—the King.

This is also a core aspect of Tzedakah and Gemilas Chasadim: to bring the poor and the rich closer together, specifically in a manner of reconciliation and a pleasant countenance, so that the distinction between the giver and the recipient is not felt. It is through the combination of both of them together that the mitzvah of the King, the King of the kings of the world—the mitzvah of Tzedakah—is fulfilled. This is especially true regarding Gemilas Chasadim, which is greater than Tzedakah, for the giving and receiving of the loan money (where the distinction between poor and rich exists) is only a temporary matter, as he returns it when the time of repayment arrives.

May it be the will of Hashem that the Gemilas Chasadim and Tzedakah performed in this year of Hakhel will, as our Sages have stated, hasten the true Redemption and bring it in our days. May the Righteous One of the world (all of whose dealings are acts of Tzedakah with His creations) fulfill His promise and the prophecy to save His people and bring them from the north country and from the ends of the earth—a great congregation—and as the verses continue, "They shall come and sing in the height of Zion, and shall flow together to the goodness of Hashem"—through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, very soon.

With respect and blessings for good tidings in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. As is my custom—though, without a vow—my contribution to your blessed activities is enclosed.

## 939

[Shevat 5727]

Regarding your writing about the distress of [the situation in] your community—my words have already been stated and are well-known (based on the halachic rulings of the great Torah authorities): Anyone who has the ability to influence others toward Yiras Shamayim, especially in the area of Torah-true education, and abandons the "poor of his city" and his country (even for the sake of the aforementioned matter)—such a person is a deserter, abandoning the front line. This is a front line in the war against assimilation, Heaven forbid, in the most literal sense; it is a matter of *pikuach nefesh*. And in a case of *pikuach nefesh*, we even desecrate Yom Kippur and Shabbos, etc., based on a doubt or a double-doubt. How much more so is this the case when it is near-certain (based on past experience) that one will save [souls]. And this is understood.

#### ***939***

**My words have already been stated and are well-known**: See also above, Vol. 21, Letter 7998, and elsewhere.

**The poor of his city**: See Bava Metzia 71a.

**We even desecrate Yom Kippur and Shabbos, etc., based on a doubt or a double-doubt**: See Yoma 83a and following.

**They too were part of that miracle**: Megillah 4a.

## 6,181

B"H, 2 Adar, 5727
Brooklyn.

Avreich Avraham Shmuel
HaKohen
Sheyichyeh

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you ask about the timing of your return here.

It is understood that in the middle of the school term, it is not at all desirable to change from one yeshiva to another. Therefore, this matter should be discussed closer to the end of the school year at Tomchei Temimim in Kfar Chabad, that is to say, in proximity to the upcoming month of Elul. This is especially true since a group will surely travel here at that time, and there are several advantages to traveling with a group.

In the meantime, you should **certainly** conduct yourself in accordance with the instruction of Chazal: "You have labored (and the promise will be fulfilled) and you have found," both in Nigleh and in Chassidus, and ensure that your learning leads to action—the fulfillment of mitzvos with hiddur, as instructed by Chazal.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

...Regarding your writing about adding a name and which one to choose—he should choose a name based on the advice of a Rav who is a *moreh hora’ah* in his place (meaning the place where he learns Torah and davens, etc.).

Now, there are those who say there is a practical difference regarding the time of Bar Mitzvah and the like. ## 9184

7 Adar, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter...

As we stand in the days of Adar Rishon—which is the month of intercalation and addition—the instruction regarding the intercalation of the year (as discussed below) is present in this month with greater intensity and strength.

The purpose of the month of intercalation is to fill the deficiency of the days of past years, so that the festivals arrive at their proper time, etc., as explained in the words of Chazal.

Moreover, from time to time—**and as is the case this year—the fulfillment is greater and in addition to** the deficiency of past years, such that this addition fills and negates the deficiency of the present and the near future.

**And now, according to the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov, that in everything a person sees or hears, there is an instruction for him in the avodah of Hashem—and all the more so regarding a matter of Torah (the word *hora’ah*—instruction) and its mitzvos—**

**In this case, the instruction is clear: that it is in the hands of each and every one (for the intercalation of the year changes and acts upon the life of each and every one) to fill everything that was lacking in the past,**

**And furthermore, it is within his ability to anticipate the future, so that nothing will be lacking in it.**

**And there is a special emphasis on the matter of intercalation and the instructions within it, since they were commanded regarding this, together with the mitzvos upon which the Exodus from Egypt depends, and as a prerequisite to them—**

**To the point that they said: The Torah should have only begun from "This month shall be for you"—which is the first mitzvos that Yisrael were commanded: the commandment to sanctify the months and intercalate the years.**

With blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 985

B"H, 10 Adar, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Regarding what you wrote about establishing a Tehillim society — the doubt in this matter is incomprehensible. Since time immemorial, in every place where Bnei Yisrael have resided, there has been a Tehillim society (and those who teach Mishnayos) after davening. It is only in our generation that the number of those following this custom has diminished, until the well-known efforts of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael, began regarding this (several decades ago)—efforts which also include an appeal to every individual to renew this ancient custom of our ancestors. And this is simple to understand.

It is appropriate that you have your tefillin checked if they have not been checked in the last twelve months.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 6,188

[22 Adar, 5727]

Out of affection for the matter, and although time is short, I will record at least two or three comments:

**In the introduction (by the author):** The uniqueness of the Book of Tehillim —

See Bava Basra (14b) that it alone bears the title "Sefer" (Book). And note Sifrei (Ki Seitzei 24:1): "Sefer" — implying it is unique in that it is enduring. Zohar Chadash (56a) and Ohr HaChama there. Torah Or (by the Alter Rebbe) in the Additions (118d, 124a).

This is explained in many places, and see also the letters of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the recitation of Tehillim.

**At the beginning, on the verse (1:1) (see there):** Why was the mitzvah of building the Mishkan not transmitted by Moshe Rabbeinu to Yisrael while standing?

- In Megillah (21a), it is learned from the verse that they studied Torah while standing; if so, the section of the mitzvah of building the Mishkan should also be included in this. The innovation in Yalkut Shimoni (Divrei HaYamim I, 28) is that the **transmission of the scroll** of the Beis HaMikdash was also done while standing.

- Yet, for the Mishkan, there is no need for such a scroll, since it was built immediately following the command, and Moshe was with them.

- This is implied in the Yalkut Shimoni passage, that the scroll of the Beis HaMikdash was transmitted from recipient to recipient and does not speak to all of Yisrael. This is also implied by the continuation of the maamarim in Midrash Shmuel, Chapter 15.

**At the end. And regarding this connection: Torah and Peace:** Note Sifrei, where the Rambam concludes Hilchos Chanukah and Sefer Zemanim: that the entire **Torah** was given to bring peace to the world, etc.

## 993

993

B”H, Rosh Chodesh Adar adjacent to Nissan, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Honorable Rabbi, the famous Gaon, wise in Torah and understanding, occupied with communal needs, possessor of noble character traits, etc., etc., Moreinu HaRav Yitzchak Nissim, Shlita, Chief Rabbi of Rishon LeZion.

Shalom and Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the telegram regarding the location of the assembly of European rabbinical activists. It is understood that I will exert effort in this matter, in addition to what has been done in the past.

According to the information I have received here, which I investigated once more after receiving the telegram, the gathering is to take place without the participation of the rabbis of the United States, and only—from the rabbis of Europe. This means that the efforts in this regard must be directed toward the initiators of the gathering (and those slated to participate in it—all of whom are located in Europe), and primarily Rabbi Broyde, shlita, who visited Eretz Yisrael, tichyeh v’tizkeh, and according to reports here, your honor and others have discussed these matters with him. The rumors here regarding the details of this deliberation and its results are unclear—and it is to be hoped that there will be benefit if all of this is communicated through those who do His will, with the necessary detail.

I must add that in my opinion, any assembly whatsoever, even the smallest one, in the city originally intended, if it includes people coming from another city, is liable to cause great damage—and not only in terms of its effect on the situation in Eretz Yisrael, tichyeh v’tizkeh, but also in the United States and other places.

And from one matter to another in the same vein, I must add, based on the position of the Gedolei Yisrael of the previous generation, which in my opinion is clear: any assembly that has the character of a global gathering of rabbis and leaders of Yisrael, in whatever place it may be, is fraught with danger to the religion and Torah and mitzvos among our people Bnei Yisrael wherever they may be; a serious danger on the spot, and a danger many times greater in the assembly that will follow it (and in the time between one assembly and the next—a time of the rule of the secretary, etc.). All the Gedolei Yisrael of the previous generation opposed such assemblies, to the extent that even assemblies that were held in certain countries by decree of the government, as was the case in Russia where the majority of the Ashkenazi brethren were located at the time, were viewed as a harsh decree. And surely for your honor, shlita, there is no need for elaboration.

May it be the will of Hashem to mend the breaches of His people Yisrael wherever they may be, and may these days, in which we are commanded to increase in joy, be like those days when "the Jews had light and gladness, and joy and honor"—"light," this is Torah, etc.—so may it be for us.

With respect, esteem, and blessing.

934

By the Grace of G-d, Rosh Chodesh Adar adjacent to Nissan, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the 25th Annual Gathering of the "Netzivei HaYeshiva" supporters of Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch in Montreal, may they live:

Peace and Blessing!

This year, as is known, is a year of **Hakhel**, when there is a special mitzvah (during the time of the Beis HaMikdash) to gather the entire nation—men, women, and children (**the men and the women and the little ones**)—to encourage them in matters of fear of Heaven, Torah, and mitzvos (**so that they may hear and so that they may learn and fear Hashem your G-d, and observe to do all the words of this Torah**).

In general, there are distinctions in the obligations regarding the mitzvos of the holy Torah. There are mitzvos that obligate both men and women, and there are mitzvos that obligate specifically men or specifically women. As for children, there is an obligation upon the adults to provide them with the proper Torah and mitzvos education, but the Torah does not directly obligate children until they reach the age of maturity (boys at 13 and girls at 12).

An exception is the mitzvah of **Hakhel**, which obligates **everyone**—men, women, and children, even very young children, without exception.

There is a similarity between the mitzvah of **Hakhel** and the concept of **Purim** (which we will celebrate this month), in that the events of Purim also affected **all** Jews equally—men, women, and children (**all the Jews, from young to old, little ones and women, in one day**). This was the first time in Jewish history that the **entire** nation stood in danger of total annihilation, G-d forbid.

And since the decree of Haman the Wicked encompassed the **entire** Jewish people, the salvation could likewise only come through means that also encompassed the **entire** Jewish people. Therefore, Esther’s demand was—**go, gather all the Jews**—to assemble **all** Jews to fast and do teshuvah. Our Sages of blessed memory tell us that even the small children, the *tinokos shel beis rabban*, were drawn into this fast, to the point of an act of literal *mesiras nefesh*. Furthermore, it was specifically in the merit of the small children, whom Mordechai the Tzaddik gathered and taught Torah, and who declared that they stood with Mordechai for life—and G-d forbid the opposite—that the decree was nullified and the miracle of Purim occurred.

In our time, and in free countries, Jews do not stand, G-d forbid, in danger of a decree of Haman, but the danger is no less serious if it is in the form of assimilation. Where life is emptied, G-d forbid, of Jewish content, where children are robbed of their right to a Torah-true education, the children are the first and innocent victims; and when one loses the children, G-d forbid, one loses everything.

In this regard, Torah education is a life-and-death issue today no less than in the time of Mordechai and Esther. And since this year is a year of **Hakhel**, the reminder is twofold, for both—the mitzvah of **Hakhel** and the events of **Purim**—underscore the vital importance of *chinuch al taharas hakodesh*, especially from the earliest youth. This is the true protection against all various decrees, G-d forbid, so that it should not come to a danger in the first place, and one should not need to rely on miracles.

In light of the above thoughts, it is to be hoped that all participants in the annual gathering of the Netzivei HaYeshiva will appreciate even better and more thoroughly the life-vital work of the great fortress of Torah and education, the Lubavitcher Yeshiva in Montreal, and the great and eternal merit they have in its support. And just as all things of goodness and holiness must continue to rise (**we ascend in matters of holiness**), one will certainly not be satisfied with the achievements of the past, but will see to it that today surpasses yesterday, and tomorrow surpasses today, to enable as many Jewish children as possible to receive the proper *chinuch al taharas hakodesh*.

May the Almighty grant that the merit of spreading Torah and mitzvos should sustain everyone and their families, in all matters, both general and personal. May it always be in a manner of **increasing in joy**, in the simple and also the deeper sense of the joy of Purim—**the Jews had light and gladness, and joy and honor**—"light" refers to Torah, etc.

With blessing for success and good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 995

B”H, 7 Adar II, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. [Name], may she live.

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter, and may it be Hashem’s will that you share good news among us.

The entire month—the month of Adar—is successful for Yisrael in all their affairs, both for men and for women. This is even more pronounced regarding Adar and Purim compared to Chanukah, for regarding both, our Sages of blessed memory stated that they (the women) were also included in the miracle, with the added distinction that the Megillah is named solely after Esther.

Since we are commanded to increase in joy from the moment Adar enters—and women are included in this, as mentioned above—and a commandment of the Torah also implies the granting of the strength and ability to fulfill it, may it be Hashem’s will that the reasons for true joy increase, in a way that is good, visible, and revealed, for you and for all those associated with you, may they live.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***995***

Printed in *Heichal Menachem*, Vol. 3, p. 133.

**The entire month—the month of Adar—is successful for Yisrael**: See *Taanis* 29a, bottom of page and onward.

**Our Sages of blessed memory stated**: *Shabbos* 23a; *Megillah* 4a.

**The Megillah is named solely after Esther**: See also above, Letter 919.

**To increase in joy from the moment Adar enters**: *Taanis*, ibid.; *Magen Avraham*, *Orach Chaim*, end of section 686.

## 976

976

B"H, Taanis Esther, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the annual banquet of the Ladies Auxiliary of Brownsville and East New York for the Lubavitcher Yeshivos Tomchei Tmimim, and to all the participants,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life,

Shalom u’vracha!

I have already noted on various occasions that this year is a *segulah* year for activities connected to *chinuch al taharas hakodesh*, as it is a year of **Hakhel**. In the time of the Beis Hamikdash, during this year following the *shemitah* year, the entire nation—men, women, and children (**ha’anashim v’hanashim v’hataf**) —would gather to encourage and strengthen them in matters of *yiras shamayim*, Torah, and *mitzvos*.

The *mitzvah* of **Hakhel** is distinguished by the fact that it obligates **all** Jews—men, women, and children, even very young children.

Since this banquet is taking place in this month, and the essence of this month is **Purim**, it is worth noting that there is a similarity between the **mitzvah of Hakhel** and the concept of **Purim**, in that the events of Purim also affected **all** Jews equally—men, women, and children (**kol hayehudim minar v’ad zaken taf v’nashim b’yom echad**). Therefore, when it was necessary to nullify the decree of Haman the wicked, Esther demanded—**lech kenos es kol hayehudim**, to gather **all** Jews to fast and do *teshuvah*. And our Sages of blessed memory relate: when was the decree nullified? When the young children, the *tinokos shel beis rabban*—whom Mordechai HaTzaddik had gathered and taught Torah—were prepared to go to *mesiras nefesh* together with Mordechai HaTzaddik.

The *mitzvah* of **Hakhel** and the concept of **Purim** remind us that the only way to ensure that a Haman does not arise in the first place, and that we do not need to rely on miracles, is by ensuring that **all** Jewish children, from their earliest youth, receive a Torah-true education in *mosdos* of Torah *al taharas hakodesh*.

I hope that this dual reminder will evoke a double enthusiasm among the esteemed leaders and members of the Ladies Auxiliary and all the participants in the banquet, to strengthen and expand your most important work. May Hashem Yisbarach grant you success in this, and may the merit of *hafotzas* Torah and *mitzvos* stand for you and your families, that all matters, both materially and spiritually, should be in a manner of **marbin b’simcha**.

With blessings for success, good tidings, and a *Purim sameach*,

**M. Schneerson**

## 997

997

[Text of the telegram for the festival of Purim 5727]

A joyous Shabbos Zachor—the remembrance of the blotting out of Amalek—and a joyous Purim, with active farbrengens.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 9898

B"H, Purim D'Shushan, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. David Rokach
Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 5 Adar II, along with the enclosure, in which you write regarding your position in South Africa, the conditions involved, and your current situation, concluding with the question of whether you should remain in your place or return to Eretz Yisrael.

It is well known in general, and especially to those who observe the situation of our people, Bnei Yisrael, wherever they may be—and even more so in the Diaspora—that the vital and primary issue regarding the survival of our people, both in the Diaspora and in our Holy Land (may it be rebuilt speedily), is the issue of the education of the younger generation. It must be a traditional Jewish education, founded upon the Torah of the Jewish people and its mitzvos—practical mitzvos in daily life. This is not like the opinion of those who err, thinking that this concerns only those abroad and less so, or not at all, in Eretz Yisrael. For there, too, the issue is vital, and it is what provides the hope for the fulfillment of the promise that "the land will not vomit out its inhabitants," Heaven forbid. In general, the point is that because of our sins (the cause), we were exiled from our land (the effect), and the only hope to remove the effect is solely by removing the cause, and the matter is understood. Surely for someone like yourself, who was in the Holy Land (may it be rebuilt speedily) not long ago and saw up close the phenomenon of the "Canaanites," the *yordim*, the secularists, etc., further elaboration is unnecessary. I will only add that the education of Bnei Yisrael in the Diaspora is vital also for the survival of Bnei Yisrael in Eretz Yisrael. And this is not only from the perspective of *aliyah* and fundraising and so on—which we see tangibly with our own eyes—but also from an inner perspective, which is also fundamental: because the entire Jewish people is one body, and the strengthening of one part of the body, or Heaven forbid its weakening, affects all parts of the body.

From what has been said above, my position regarding your issue is also understood. Your educational work in your current location is in the category of a mitzvah that cannot be performed by others, and therefore it is your holy duty to continue in this. And the merit of the many will assist you to increase your efforts to instill in the students a love of Hashem and a fear of Hashem, which are the source and root for the fulfillment of the positive and negative mitzvos in daily life, including persistence and diligence in the study of Torah, the Torah of life. May it be His will that you succeed in this, going from strength to strength, with joy and goodness of heart.

The time is appropriate—these days of Purim—especially in light of the account of our Sages, of blessed memory, that the nullification of Haman’s decree was brought about by the *tinokos shel beis rabban* (schoolchildren) who were educated by Mordechai in a spirit of *mesiras nefesh* for Torah and mitzvos.

With respect and blessings for good news regarding all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. It is understood that you have permission to share the content of my letter and my opinion on this matter if you find it appropriate.

I would also like to note that Dr. Chaim Chamiel, whom you mention in your letter, is, I believe, the one who sent me his books, and we are in correspondence. I have heard much about his heartfelt attitude toward Torah and mitzvos.

## T'sha

B"H, 11 Nissan, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever you may be,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

The Yom Tov of Pesach, the season of our freedom, carries a special significance this year in light of the following brief introduction:

It is observed that when a person is in a receptive mood, a relevant phenomenon makes a stronger impression upon them. When one is in a joyful mood, they receive a matter of joy with greater enthusiasm. Conversely, in a depressed mood, an undesirable phenomenon evokes a greater sense of dejection. The same is seen in connection with one's physical state: when the body is healthy, it is strengthened by all healthy things to the fullest extent; when the body is weakened, even a mild harmful thing can have a severe effect on one's health.

This is similar to and expressed in the halachic principle: "Like finds its like and is aroused."

***

This year is a year that was ushered in from the very beginning with the mitzvah (and in the mood) of **Hakhel** — the special mitzvah in the year following Shmittah: "**Assemble the people, the men, the women, and the children**" — to gather all parts of the Jewish people. The purpose, as the verse explains immediately, is that there should be fear of Hashem, and that one should learn and fulfill the Torah.

Likewise, the reason and essence of the festival of Pesach, which is **Yetziat Mitzrayim** (the Exodus from Egypt), was—unlike other exiles (Bavel, Media, Persia, and Greece), where not all Jews left Bavel, etc.—that "with our youth and with our elders, with our sons and with our daughters," all Jews, from the smallest to the greatest, left Egypt. And the purpose was: "When you bring the people out of Egypt, **you shall serve the Almighty on this mountain**"—to become an *eved Elokus* (servant of the Almighty) and to receive the Torah at Mount Sinai.

Therefore, even though Pesach is a *mitzvah asei shehazman grama* (a time-bound positive commandment, from which women are generally exempt), women must nevertheless participate in it. And regarding children—the introduction to the Yom Tov at the very beginning of the time of Yetziat Mitzrayim, the Seder of Pesach, is based on "**And you shall tell your son**" (instructing and informing your son)—with many details and matters aimed at drawing the children into the subject of Pesach, even before one fulfills the mitzvos of Pesach, matzah, and maror. And this applies to all children.

The Seder is not limited to wise children, but to all types, from the wise one to the one who does not know how to ask.

And one must inform everyone that "**Because of this**—in order that we should fulfill the mitzvos—**the Almighty took us out of Egypt.**"

***

Such a total liberation as occurred from the exile of Egypt did not happen in the later exiles, but it will be repeated at the time of the true Redemption from the current exile, as it was divinely promised ("**As in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show you wonders**"), when all Jews, young and old, children and women, with all that they possess, will be redeemed by Moshiach Tzidkeinu. And the purpose is that "you shall walk in My statutes... and you shall be My people, and I will be your God" (keeping the Almighty’s laws and being *His* people).

And just as the Redemption from Egypt could only come about when the Jews, with *mesiras nefesh*, cast off the *avodah zarah* (idolatry) of Egypt and yearned and looked forward to when they would receive the Torah, so too must the preparation for our Redemption be made now—by definitively casting off the various *avodah zarahs* of our time. And "with our youth and with our elders, with our sons and with our daughters"—everyone must extract themselves, along with their wives and children, from the state of being *avdei Paroh* (servants of Pharaoh)—slaves to the ideologies that rule in the outside world—and become *avdei Hashem* (servants of the Almighty), in a total commitment to the Almighty, and thereby attain true *cherus* (freedom) through a daily life of Torah and mitzvos.

***

May the Almighty grant that the coming Yom Tov this year, in the year of **Hakhel**, be received with a special enthusiasm, as mentioned above; an enthusiasm that should express itself during the days of the Yom Tov and in all the days to come, as commanded regarding Hakhel: "And they shall observe to do all the words of this Torah"—to observe in order **to do** (not to be *yotzei* with a good Jewish heart and a highly ethical sermon—however good those may be) **all** the words (not choosing what is, according to one's own opinion, "appropriate" for today's time and convenient) of **the** Torah (as the Rambam interprets **Torah** as a **psak din**—every verse and every word, and likewise—Torah Shebe'al Peh).

And this will hasten the true and complete Redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, immediately, in our very days.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 926

926

B"H, 11 Nissan, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

And may this freedom and joy continue throughout all the days of the year.

Especially since the avodah of Hashem, as we are commanded in our Torah—the Torah of life—encompasses all of a person’s affairs and continues throughout the entire day and night, as it is said, "In all your ways, know Him."

With holiday blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9708

B"H, 28 Nissan, 5727 - Shnas Hakhel
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, communal activist, possessor of noble character traits, a choice individual, elevated above the people, who seeks the good of his people, a branch of the tree of his fathers, R' Schneur Zalman, shlita,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter sent after the Yom Tov, and I am writing immediately regarding its conclusion, in which you write about your visit to Canada (Montreal, Toronto) and subsequently to Iceland. I was very pleased to learn that you are traveling by airplane—I heard and my soul was revived.

I am hastening to write this urgent note because it is my desire—and it would be a source of satisfaction for me—to send my representatives from here to Canada to bring you a blessing as my shluchim, for "a person's agent is like the person himself." I am writing to ask you in which place and at what time it would be convenient for you to receive my shluchim. It is my hope that by that time, I will have the great pleasure—which will surely be pleasant for you as well—of having published more matters of Chassidus. Thus, when my shluchim travel from here, they will be able to deliver to you not only oral messages, but also words of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, that have been published in print for the first time.

As is the custom of Chassidim, not only to open with a blessing but also to conclude with one, I send you my heartfelt wishes that your aforementioned trip by airplane be with great success in all respects, and as we discussed during our face-to-face meeting, which is still engraved on my heart—"You shall be blessed above all peoples."

Especially since these are days of auspiciousness, the days of the month of Iyar, where every single day of this month has a special mitzvah within it—the mitzvah of Sefiras HaOmer—the essence of which is not only to sanctify the person with "holiness from above," but also to bestow "abundant influence in all the worlds."

With blessings for proper health, for joy and goodness of heart, and for abundant success in all your affairs, with appreciation and honor,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. I have just been informed by my secretaries, Mr. Nissan, may he live, and Dr. Mindel, that his older sister and her family, may they live, have received an exit permit and will be leaving there in the coming days to ascend to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established.

On this occasion, I thank you once again for the great help and your efforts in this matter.

[Nissan 5727]

There is no need to establish an office, as there are already more than enough. As for distributing the sichos, since they are not proofread, and outside of the *Tmimim* [students of Tomchei Tmimim] there is a risk that errors will be attributed to me—despite all declarations to the contrary—this could lead to undesirable results.

*V’dai l’meivin* (and a word to the wise is sufficient). This is not the case with the *sefarim* of our *Rebbeim* that are being published; in addition to their holiness and absolute truth—which is, after all, the main thing—they are also proofread, etc. The same applies **regarding** **editing** the *shmuessen*, *talks*, *Idishe Heim*, etc.

## 911

B"H, 1 Iyar, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Mordechai Newman, Tel Aviv

Shalom u’Bracha!

It was a pleasant surprise to receive the book you published, which the author writes was sent at your request.

Beyond the actual receipt of the book, this also shows that our meeting remained not only in my memory but in yours as well.

It is my hope that since we last met, you have continued your activities and are doing everything in your power to fulfill your role as a "publisher" (*motzi la’or*), in complete accordance with the literal meaning of these words—that is, that the printed materials you produce should bring forth light (*yafiku or*) to the readers. In the style of our Sages, of blessed memory, "light" refers only to Torah—our eternal Torah, the Torah of life, as it is written: "For the mitzvah is a lamp and the Torah is light" (Mishlei 6:23). This light shines in every place and at every time, and with even greater intensity in the land that all the nations of the world call the Holy Land—the land upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are always, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year, as the words of Hashem state in His Torah.

With respect and blessing,

P.S. My hope, based on our conversation when you were here, is that if among the books you have printed and published since then there are any that might interest me, you will send them to me, including a catalog. Thank you in advance.

## 915

[6 Iyar 5727]

[1] It is appropriate and correct, provided that the translator is appropriate and correct.

[2] **Many times** it has been discussed and stipulated that their arrival here is on the condition **and with the intent** to study with diligence, etc., etc. — and in accordance with the ruling of the Rambam. And it is a **great** wonder regarding his aforementioned question.

***

915

Published in *Heichal Menachem*, Vol. 3, p. 203. Written in response to a question from several students of the *kvutza* who came from Eretz Yisrael to study at 770:

A proposal was raised that, since there are those... who do not understand the *sichos* of the Rebbe *shlita* in Yiddish, [they should] translate the *sichos*... of this year into *Lashon HaKodesh*... And my question is: (a) Is this appropriate and correct? (b) Is it appropriate and correct that the *bochurim*... [from the *kvutza*] should perform the work of translation.

**Ruling of the Rambam**: *Hilchos Melachim*, Chapter 5, Law 7.

## 9156

9156

B"H, 7 Iyar, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students graduating from the "Beis Rivkah" school — elementary and high school — may Hashem grant you life.

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter regarding your graduation from the "Beis Rivkah" school—which, as I have emphasized many times, signifies a transition to a higher level in matters of holiness, Torah, and mitzvos—I hereby send you my greetings and blessing that your graduation should be in a good and auspicious hour, and that you should continue to ascend in all matters of goodness and holiness with great success.

Since this year is a year of **Hakhel**, all the matters of this year are illuminated by the content of **Hakhel**.

In general, the concept of **Hakhel** was to **gather** all Jews, men, women, and children, with the purpose of strengthening yiras shamayim and the fulfillment of mitzvos in the daily life of the entire Jewish people.

In personal life, just as a person is called an "olam katan" (a world in miniature), possessing a whole range of powers—the powers of the soul and the body—the concept of **Hakhel** should serve as a reminder of the necessity for a constant "mobilization" of all these powers for that same purpose: to strengthen yiras shamayim and the fulfillment of mitzvos in one's personal daily life.

It is worth noting that since one was required to bring even the very young children (taf) to **Hakhel**, the women (the mothers and older sisters) had a special task to bring them and look after them, etc. This emphasizes even more the special duty and privilege of Jewish daughters in the strengthening and dissemination of Torah and mitzvos al taharas hakodesh.

May Hashem Yisbarach grant that the idea of **Hakhel** in connection with your graduation, as mentioned above, should always accompany you on your life's path, and that you should be a source of influence and encouragement for your entire environment as well.

With blessings for success and for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 9119

B"H, Lag B’Omer, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Twelfth Annual Convention of N'shei U’Bnos Chabad, may they live:

Blessings and peace!

It has been emphasized many times that this year is a year of special significance, being a year of **Hakhel** — the special mitzvah in the year following Shmittah to gather all Jews, men, women, and children, with the purpose of strengthening yiras-shamayim and the observance of mitzvos in daily life.

And although the mitzvah of **Hakhel** was connected to a specific time and a designated place (the Beis HaMikdash), the Torah is eternal, such that this aforementioned mitzvah is also — in its spiritual sense and content — valid in all times and places, and today perhaps more than ever before.

The spiritual sense and content of the mitzvah of **Hakhel** is to strengthen the eternal bond between the eternal Torah and the eternity within every Jew and all Jews, which is the Divine soul, a **chaleik Elokah mima'al mamash**, which gives life to all Jews, men, women, and children.

* * *

**Lag B’Omer**, when this letter is being written, also has a connection to the aforementioned content, in the two main aspects of the day:

On this day, the **tikkun** regarding the matter of **shelo nahagu kavod zeh lazeh** (not treating one another with respect) was achieved, and the destruction among the students of Torah in the time of Rabbi Akiva was halted. It is understood that this tikkun was achieved through a strengthening of **yiras-shamayim**, **ahavas-haTorah**, and **ahavas-Yisrael** in the eternal bond that unites Jews with the Ribono shel Olam, Jews with Torah, and Jews with one another.

Lag B’Omer is also the hillula of Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai, who said: **Yecholni liftoir kol ha'olam kulo min hadin** — "I can exempt the entire world from the judgment of Heaven" (Sukkah 45b, Avos D'Rabbi Nosson, end of ch. 16). He was able to find a merit in every Jew (due to the Divine soul that gives life to all Jews, because of which a Jew neither can, nor wants to, be severed from Elokus).

* * *

In accordance with what has been said above, this year's convention — whose theme and leitmotif is the **netzius (eternity) of Torah** — has a special significance.

The role of the Jewish woman and Jewish daughter in strengthening the bond between Jews and Torah is particularly emphasized in the mitzvah of **Hakhel**, in that not only were they required to participate in the mitzvah, but they were also required to bring the young children. For the upbringing, care, and chinuch of Jewish children, from birth until adulthood, falls upon the woman to a very great extent. She, the Jewish mother, places the primary imprint upon the child and shapes his inner development.

May Hashem Yisbarach help that the convention be permeated with the spirit of **Hakhel** and **Lag B’Omer**, as indicated above, to strengthen the bond of the eternity of the Divine soul with the eternity of Torah and mitzvos in daily life, first and foremost in the circle of one's own family, and also in the broader circles of Jewish women and daughters.

May the light and warmth of Chassidus, with the emphasis on **ahavas Hashem**, **ahavas haTorah**, and **ahavas Yisrael**, enliven your multifaceted activities in an increasing measure and with increasing success.

With blessings for success and for good tidings in both spiritual and material matters alike,

**M. Schneerson**

## 920

920

B”H, Lag B’Omer, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, distinguished for his Torah and fear of Heaven, engaged in communal affairs, etc., Rabbi Sh.Y. [Zevin]—may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

I was distressed to hear that your health is not as it should be. May it be the will of Hashem that your recovery be swift and complete, and may you share good news regarding this.

Enclosed is a copy of the Tzemach Tzedek’s notes (on Nach) regarding the verse, "Heal me, Hashem, and I shall be healed"—the conclusion and seal of the Haftorah for this Shabbos: "If you walk in My statutes... I will give your rains in their time... and all the blessings enumerated in the parsha, in general and in particular: 'And you shall dwell in your land in safety... and I will place peace in the land... and I will be to you a G-d and you shall be to Me a people,' from now and forever." As is stated on this auspicious day, the Hilula of Rashbi (Zohar Vol. III, 290b), "For there Hashem commanded the blessing, life forevermore," "Length of days and years of life (etc.—meaning) and peace they shall add to you."

With respect and blessings for a *refuah* and good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. I have received the 12th volume of the *Entziklopedia Talmudit* that you sent. Many thanks for the shipment and for your thoughtfulness, etc. The extent of the pleasure and satisfaction, etc., is beyond words. For just as with the previous volume, so too with those that preceded it: in such a case, an additional volume is not merely an addition in its own right, but an addition to all the preceding ones as well. As we have discussed several times—and I believe I have written this to you as well—regarding the *Entziklopedia*, as long as the entries for the letter *Tav* have not been printed, there is room for further perfection even in the entries for the letter *Aleph*. Certainly, for one of your stature, elaboration is unnecessary; I write only to wish you continued speed regarding the upcoming volumes, speedily in our days, amidst proper health, joy, good, and tranquility of soul and body.

A note on the *Dvar Malchus* of **Mishlei**:

Seemingly, there is a contradiction from *Yoma* (86a), "I will heal their backsliding"—that a portion of his name is upon him (Rashi there). It can be said that there, it refers to a healing from Above that comes through *teshuvah* from *yirah*, which in any event is not above the *sefirah* of *Binah*. This is unlike the case here, where "For I am Hashem your healer" refers to *Arich* (from *Ohr Yakar*, *Yair Nasiv* 124; see *Ohr HaTorah* by the Tzemach Tzedek, *Beshalach*, p. 589). On the other hand, even in a healing where a human hand (a doctor) is involved, there are instances where "one is healed, and it is not in the category of healing (that is only) from here on (and consequently a trace remains), but rather the reality itself [is changed], etc.," or that the human action is only a "matter of trial" (*Responsa Tzafenas Paneach*, sec. 67; *Tzafenas Paneach* on Rambam, *Hilchos Issurei Biah*, ch. 15, law 5). And no trace remains at all. Wishing you a *refuah sheleimah*—perfection in the ultimate sense.

## 9263

[28 Iyar, 5727]

...Regarding the content of your letter concerning the Holocaust, etc., and the staggering question: What is the meaning and explanation of this, etc., etc.?

While from the perspective of human emotion—flesh and blood—this is an entirely exceptional matter, and consequently the question regarding it is also entirely exceptional; yet, upon even a **slight** contemplation of the essence of the question—the core of which is, "Shall the Judge of all the earth not do justice?"—there is **no** difference between the greatest Holocaust and the smallest burden. In the phrasing of Chazal, "suffering without sin," whether it concerns one individual or the largest community—Heaven forbid.

For, logically: If there is no Judge and no judgment, then one cannot ask questions or seek "logic," justice, and order in what occurred in a place of **total lawlessness**. But since there is a Master of this world—a Master in the fullest sense of the word, in absolute perfection—then it is **obvious** that even the smallest detail must align with and be in absolute accordance with justice and righteousness. A burden multiplied six million times changes the quantity, **not** the quality.

It is also understood that the above is not a **justification** for the question. What I intended to point out is that for all those who justify their "rebellion" against the Ribono shel Olam—Heaven forbid—because of the Holocaust, etc., there is **no** foundation, logic, or reason for this, as stated above. And "Why does the way of the wicked prosper?" is an ancient question, dating back to the days of Moshe Rabbeinu—who received the Torah from Sinai and **transmitted it**, etc., until the end of all generations. Therefore, even before the Holocaust, people should have been standing with the aforementioned bewilderment. If, for whatever reason, the success of the wicked did not unsettle them before the Holocaust, and they lived their lives according to the instruction of the Torah given by Hashem, then even after the Holocaust, there is no logic or reason to change this [although Michael, the minister of Yisrael, will teach merit that after the Holocaust, a person is not held accountable for his anguish, as it touched his own family, and it was of a staggering quantity, even if the quality was the **exact same**].

Furthermore, it should be added that similar to the Holocaust, there was the destruction of the First Beis Hamikdash, and with greater intensity—the destruction of the Second Beis Hamikdash, and with even greater intensity—the Middle Ages, when, by the way of nature, there was no escape for Bnei Yisrael during the Crusades, etc.

It is a wondrous thing that specifically during these three aforementioned periods, there was a **flourishing** of Torah Shebaal Peh (in its various stages), which not only did not diminish—Heaven forbid—the matters of Torah and mitzvos, but on the contrary, the motto was, in the words of the Anshei Knesses Hagedolah, "Make a **fence** for the Torah."

As stated—even in this, there is no answer to the question (which arises from a broken heart). My words have already been stated many times: in general, there is no room in logic for a question from a created being to the Creator, for there is no comparison between them, and consequently, the created being’s intellect cannot grasp the "intellect" of the Creator.

And all the more so, it is a *kal v’chomer* from a small child, who has no basis to question the conduct of a great, elderly sage—even though, a short time ago, this sage was also a small child, and the small child has the potential to become a great sage, perhaps even greater than the one questioning him, and the rest is understood.

Regarding your letter about a place to settle in the future—certainly, the convenience and means of settling for individuals of a certain age are more available in the United States than in other countries, and in a more stable order and with more tranquility. And regarding an environment of cultured people (and woe to culture **in and of itself**, "independent"—and the aforementioned Holocaust will prove it) and an atmosphere of Torah, etc.—there is no greater possibility than in New York, the place of two and a half million of our brethren, may they increase. However, **in every place** one must search, etc., and that is the case here as well.

924

It is understood and simple that this includes, and first and foremost, in the style of the verse, "And Israel saw the great hand which **Hashem wrought** in Mitzrayim" and those who assisted them, and delivered the many into the hands of the few who went with *mesiras nefesh* to the "aid of Israel against an enemy that came upon them." And then, certainly and surely, it will be as the conclusion of the well-known prayer of thanksgiving—(that each person should increase in *Torah* and *mitzvos*, together with the thanksgiving for the miracle itself)—to thank and praise Your great Name.

These are days of *segulah*—the beginning of the third month, and the days of preparation and *hagbalah* for the Giving of the Torah and for the receiving of the Torah, *Toras Chaim*, a living Torah. As in the saying we heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, "A Torah that makes for life"—a life worthy of the name.

These are days when the Children of Israel were chosen to be a *segulah* from among all the nations, a kingdom of priests and a holy nation.

With a blessing—in the traditional formula—for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness, in good health, with honor and appreciation, awaiting good tidings.

**M. Schneerson**

## 925

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants in the annual luncheon of the N.Y. Committee for the Seminary for Teachers and Schools for Girls in Kfar Chabad in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, may Hashem grant them life:

Blessings and peace!

The annual luncheon, which takes place this year on Tuesday, the 3rd of Sivan, a few days before the Yom Tov of **Matan Torah**, and in a year of **Hakhel**, will surely be imbued with the impression of both these themes: the preparations for **Kabbalas HaTorah** and the **significance of Hakhel**.

Both in **Kabbalas HaTorah** (every year) and in **Hakhel** (once every seven years), we find two primary common features:

Firstly, in both instances, the bond and unity of the Jewish people is expressed. At **Matan Torah**—**"And Israel encamped there"** (in the singular)—the Jewish people were gathered at Mount Sinai, as Rashi notes in the name of the Mechilta: **"Like one person with one heart."** **All** Jews—men, women, and children—were united with one and the same thought: to accept the Torah and mitzvos. And regarding **Hakhel**, the Torah states: **"Assemble the people, the men, the women, and the children"**—gather the people, men, women, and children, also with the purpose **"that they may hear and that they may learn... and observe to do all the words of this Torah"**—to hear, to learn, and to observe and perform all the mitzvos of the Torah.

Secondly, in both cases, the central place of the Jewish woman is emphasized: at **Matan Torah**—**"Thus shall you say to the House of Jacob"**—these are the **women**; and at **Hakhel**—"the men, the **women**, and the children."

The bond and unity of Jews among themselves, and of Jews with the Ribono shel Olam, is possible only because Jews—all Jews without exception—possess a Divine soul, a *chelek Eloka m'ma'al mamash*, and because the Torah and mitzvos—which are *Elokus mamash*—unite Jews with the Ribono shel Olam.

And in this bond and unity, Jewish women occupy a central place.

Therefore, this year’s event—taking place a few days before **Kabbalas HaTorah** and in the year of **Hakhel**—should be especially permeated with the content of both these matters, particularly since the work of the committee is to strengthen and expand the educational institutions in Kfar Chabad in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, which are engaged in the education of the future educators and builders of the Jewish people.

May the Hashem Yisbarach grant success to your work in an ever-increasing measure, and may this merit stand for you all, together with your families, to be blessed by the Ribono shel Olam in everything you need, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for success and good tidings.

## 926

[Yemei Hagbalah 5727]

The annual luncheon (on the upcoming 11th of Sivan) is taking place this year during the days that are still connected to the Yom Tov of Shavuos, and surely all the participants will be under the fresh impression of **Zman Matan Toraseinu**.

Jewish women have a special wealth to draw from the influence of the Yom Tov of Kabbalas HaTorah. For, as is well known, women were the first to whom the Ribono shel Olam offered the Torah HaKedosha, and they accepted the Torah immediately, as our Sages, of blessed memory, explain the words: **"Thus shall you say to the House of Yaakov"**—"these are the women"—**"and tell the Children of Yisrael"**—"these are the men." This underscores the great zechus of Jewish women—and along with it, their great responsibility—for Torah and mitzvos.

And although every year all the themes of the Yom Tov are repeated, this in itself is an indication that our connection to Torah and mitzvos must be renewed and refreshed to a greater degree from year to year, especially considering that human capacities also increase from year to year.

It is therefore entirely understandable that your important work to support the holy mosdos haTorah of Lubavitch must be strengthened and expanded from year to year, especially since the mosdos haTorah themselves are constantly growing and require increased assistance more and more.

May the Ribono shel Olam grant that this annual undertaking be met with great hatzlacha and bring about a strengthened revitalization in your work, in both quantity and quality. In this zechus, may you all, together with your families, be blessed with an abundance of blessings in everything you need, in both gashmius and ruchnius alike.

With blessings for hatzlacha and good tidings.

#### ***926***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 33, p. 232.

**"Thus shall you say to the House of..." "these are the men"**: Yisro 19:3; see Mechilta and Rashi there.

By the Grace of G-d
Tuesday, 5 Sivan, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter...

As we stand in these auspicious days, which you have begun—

On the day of Rosh Chodesh, when they arrived at the desert of Sinai and Israel encamped there as one man with one heart;

And immediately the following day, it was said to the House of Jacob (these are the women) and told to the Children of Israel (these are the men): "You have seen what I did to Egypt, and I bore you on eagles' wings, etc. And now, etc., if you will indeed keep My covenant (regarding the observance of the Torah), you shall be My treasure among all the peoples, etc., a kingdom of priests and a holy nation"—

And the conclusion and seal of these days of preparation is on the fifth of the month, when—

Israel said, all of them with one mouth, "All that Hashem has spoken, we will do and we will hear"—

And our Sages have said that at that moment, the Holy One, blessed be He, rejoiced with them, gave them His Torah, and blessed them with peace.

May it be G-d’s will that all that is stated above shall be realized for us as well.

And through tranquility of soul and tranquility of body, may the blessing be fulfilled in each and every one—in the well-known phrasing—of receiving the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

And no nation or tongue shall have dominion over them, as it is said: "It shall be well with them and with their children forever."

With the blessing of a happy holiday,

**M. Schneerson**

## 3930

[Sivan 5727]

Regarding your comment concerning "Mivtza Tefillin" in light of what the Rambam writes regarding the protection of a mezuzah (Hilchos Mezuzah 5:4) — my appeal here is directed to **everyone** who has the ability to act in this matter (even within the realm of uncertainty; see Shabbos 55a). The general basis for this is founded upon what is explained in many places, including:

A clear, explicit ruling of the Rambam himself in Hilchos Avodas Kochavim (11:12, **at the end**), that it is permitted. And in the matter at hand, it is explicitly stated in Hilchos Teshuvah (10:5, **at the end**) that this is an obligation. Furthermore, one who does not utilize this opportunity to the full extent required transgresses the positive Torah commandment of "You shall surely rebuke your neighbor" (Vayikra 19:17), and is held accountable for the sins of those whom he did not bring to **the act** of donning tefillin (Hilchos Deos 6:7). See at length in the Commentary on the Mishnah, beginning of Perek Chelek. There it states, "**We encourage them** (those who have not yet grasped the truth to the point of being like Avraham Avinu, a"h) to do this (to perform the mitzvah for the sake of its reward) **and we strengthen their intention**." And furthermore, and this is essential: every single day and every time one dons tefillin, he recites the blessing over them before performing the act, "Who has sanctified us with His mitzvos **and commanded us**," etc. Through this, it is clear (and not merely something we say) that he is performing it *lishmah* (for its own sake), even if he also intends his own benefit; he is considered a **"perfect tzaddik in this regard"** (Pesachim 8b and Rashi/Tosafos there).

Regarding what the Rambam wrote concerning the mezuzah, there it speaks of those who "nullify the mitzvah" (and as for his addition, "rather they have made..." — it must be that this is merely for the sake of embellishment. And what the Kesef Mishneh writes there is to resolve what the Rambam wrote **as if** it were so). Furthermore, it should be noted: the Rambam regarding the mezuzah speaks of one who performs the mitzvah [in a specific way], whereas in the matter at hand, it concerns one who strives to have another person don tefillin. I will not elaborate further on this here.

[And regarding the comment on the statement that the mitzvah of tefillin is "great" because of...: the connection between the "greatness" of the mitzvah and this [effect] is based on the words of our Sages, "Great is teshuvah, for it lengthens..." (Yoma 86b).]

## 9331

B"H, 11 Sivan, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch
For the Chag HaSiyum, Montreal, may they live

Greetings and Blessings!

In connection with the Chag HaSiyum on the upcoming 13th of Sivan, I send my greetings and blessing to those completing their studies, as well as to the Roshei Yeshiva, administrators, educators, and all the students, may they live.

Since the Chag HaSiyum takes place immediately following the days of completion of **Zman Matan Toraseinu**, and furthermore in a year of **Hakhel**, it is to be hoped that the celebration will surely be permeated with the spirit of **Kabbalas HaTorah** and **Hakhel** together. By this is meant: a firm resolution to give expression to an internal "Hakhel" — the mobilization of all one’s *kochos hanefesh* and capabilities — for Torah and *mitzvos*.

This means, first and foremost, increased *hasmadah* and *shekidah* in the study of Torah—study that leads to action: the fulfillment of the *mitzvos*, the 248 positive *mitzvos* and 365 negative *mitzvos*, which encompass the **entire** person, with his 248 limbs and 365 sinews, both physically and spiritually.

In this, *Zman Matan Toraseinu* emphasizes that although Torah requires intellectual understanding, it must nevertheless come in a manner of *kabbalas ol*: **Naaseh** is a prerequisite to **Nishma**.

The intellect itself must also understand that this is the order of conduct according to Torah and according to the intellect of Torah (not the intellect of the *nefesh habehamis*).

Added to this is the common point of **Matan Torah** and **Hakhel** — the unification and bond of Jews, which also emphasizes the shared responsibility to strengthen one another in the study of Torah and the fulfillment of *mitzvos*, with an internal feeling of *ahavas Yisrael*, to the fullest extent of the powers and possibilities with which *Hashgacha Elyona* has gifted each person.

May Hashem Yisbarach grant success to each of the students completing their studies, and to all the students of the Yeshiva, may they live, in fulfilling their *shlichus* as students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch: to spread the light of Torah—*Toras HaNigleh* and *Toras HaChassidus*—which is one Torah for us all, in a manner of *mosif v'holech mosif v'or* (increasing and continuing to increase in light), with joy and goodness of heart.

With blessings for outstanding success in both material and spiritual matters, and for good tidings.

**M. Schneerson**
