9375

B"H, 5 Tammuz, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

...As we stand before the auspicious days of 12-13 Tammuz, may it be the will of Hashem that the merit of the Baal HaGeulah and Simcha — my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi of our generation — stand for each and every one of us, within the rest of our brethren, the Anash, may they live and be well, to draw down Hashem’s blessings in all that is needed, both spiritually and materially.

This includes, obviously and simply, great success in spreading Yiddishkeit and Torah (both the revealed and the inner dimensions) and the mitzvos, and doing so with true tranquility, joy, and goodness.

This applies with even greater intensity and strength starting from this year, forty years since his redemption, for "after forty years, a person attains the perspective of his Rebbe" — the end of his Rebbe’s **intellect, understanding, and wisdom** of his teachings.

And it is not only that one reaches the perspective and teachings of his Rebbe (by being meticulous—throughout this time—in the matters and the precision of the words, etc.), but that after forty years, Hashem grants him "a heart to know, eyes to see, and ears to hear" the very inner intent of the events of these days. In the words of the verse: "All that Hashem did before your eyes in the land of Egypt... those great signs and wonders."

In particular, according to the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov that everything a person sees and everything a person hears is an **instruction** from Heaven in the service of Hashem—and one must attain the "perspective of his Rebbe" (this refers to the Holy One, Blessed be He) in this instruction.

The study, contemplation, and precision in the maamarim of Chassidus from these days, and in the sichos and the reshimus of the Baal HaGeulah regarding them, will certainly add understanding, depth, and light to this "attaining the perspective of his Rebbe," and to the imprisonment, the freedom, the exile, and the redemption.

With blessings,

**Menachem Schneerson**

Surely, during these days of redemption, and in the days preceding and following them, you will study the maamarim of Tammuz, 5687—forty years ago—the year of the redemption.

I am certain you will inform me regarding yourself **until now** in detail. Thank you in advance.

## 9339

9339

B"H, 9 Tammuz, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished individual, a man of noble character, a scion of a noble lineage, R' Schneur Zalman, shlita,

Greetings and blessings!

In connection with the festival of the liberation of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, on 12-13 Tammuz—which at the time served as a turning point in the life of Judaism in the countries of the USSR, and as is tangibly evident throughout the years that have passed since, in addition to the turning point in his own life, since the culmination of the liberation was his departure from that country and his standing at the helm of Jewish life in all the Diaspora—

We have published a collection of Chassidic maamarim that he delivered during that time, while in prison (reciting them to himself and writing them down), during his exile, and during the days of the liberation. In them, the perspective of the master of the celebration and the liberation regarding the episode of the imprisonment, the freedom, the exile, and the redemption is reflected in a manner characteristic of Torah, and specifically the Torah of Chassidus.

This year is unique, as it is the fortieth year of the aforementioned period. Our Sages have informed us that "after forty years, a person attains the mind of his teacher," based on the verse, "And Hashem has not given you a heart to know, and eyes to see, and ears to hear, until this day"—referring to the great signs and wonders.

May it be the will of Hashem that we soon merit to see the liberation and redemption of all of Jewry in the USSR—a liberation in goodness, kindness, and mercy, and in the language of the verse: "With our young and with our old, with our sons and with our daughters," until "not a hoof shall remain."

And after having seen great signs and wonders in those days, and also in these days in the Holy Land, may it be that from here on, signs and wonders will only be necessary in a state of ease and expansion, in the style of our Alter Rebbe in his well-known Iggeres HaKodesh: not in order to weaken the power of the Sitra Achra—for the evil will be separated from the good and all workers of iniquity will be scattered—but rather to draw down even higher lights, to go from strength to strength, from good to even greater good (Iggeres HaKodesh, end of Epistle 26).

With appreciation, honor, and blessings for the festival of the liberation.

The temimim, Rabbi Chaim Lieberman, may he live, has presented me with his most precious gift—a compilation from the Bichovsky notebook, including teachings, aphorisms, and stories from our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, etc. Many thanks, many thanks, especially in these auspicious days.

## 9442

B"H, 13 Tammuz, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

Your letter was received with a delay. You are surely aware that since the histalkus of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, I have not traveled from New York, not even for a short trip.

It is understood that there is no room here for requests for forgiveness or apologies, as the content of your letter is not of the type that requires this, **and on the contrary**.

"By the way," it is appropriate to comment regarding the direction that has been given recently concerning trips to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. Even though our Sages of blessed memory said regarding matters of Torah and mitzvos that a person should always engage in them even if not for their own sake, for out of "not for their own sake" one comes to "for their own sake," it still requires study whether the aforementioned is included in this, and a word to the wise is sufficient.

As in my previous letter, I will permit myself once again to arouse [you] regarding the obligation of a father to his son to marry him off. Although the method of action in this changes according to place and time—since the goal is to succeed in a specific place and time—the obligation itself is a directive of our Torah, which will not be exchanged, etc.

I will conclude in the manner of the beginning of your letter to me, with an apology for my intervention in a matter that I have already spoken about and which surely concerns you most deeply, and the hope that you will pardon and forgive.

You surely know the significance of these days, the 12th–13th of Tammuz, the geulah of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, from his imprisonment exactly forty years ago.

I will conclude with the blessing of the Chag HaGeulah, and with respect and tidings of good news.

#### ***9442***

**You are surely aware**: A response to an invitation to visit Eretz Yisrael. See also above, letter 9427.

**Our Sages of blessed memory said**: Pesachim 50b, and elsewhere.

**The obligation of a father**: See Kiddushin 29a.

**Our Torah, which will not be exchanged, etc.**: The essence of the ninth of the Thirteen Principles of Faith.

**Forty years**: See also above, letter 9433, and the references in the notes there.

He will compel all of Israel to walk in its ways and strengthen its breaches, he will fight the wars of Hashem and succeed, he will build the Beis Hamikdash in its place, and he will gather the dispersed of Israel—and these days will be turned into joy and gladness and festive seasons.

## T'shma

Regarding the events in Eretz Yisrael during these days, and in the style of a mitzvah that one is precise about:

May it be the will of Hashem that our brethren, the Children of Israel, will discern that "kala ilan" is not "techeiles" (even though its color resembles techeiles), and that one should not be "one who hangs it on his garment and says it is techeiles" (for he transgresses immediately—see Tosafos, s.v. *Shatulah*, Bava Metzia 61b).

For there is a clear *psak din* in the Rambam (Hilchos Melachim, end of Chapter 11) regarding the manner in which the period of Golus concludes and the period of Geulah begins, **and regarding the order**: "A king from the House of Dovid will arise, who meditates on the Torah... both the Written and the Oral, **and he will compel** all of Israel to walk in its ways and strengthen its breaches, and he will fight the wars of Hashem (and even then, there is no certainty until **after all this**), [if] he succeeds **and builds** the Beis Hamikdash in its place (for no one else will do this), and gathers the dispersed of Israel (for until then they will still be scattered), then he is certainly Moshiach."

And there is not a single *posek* who disagrees with this. As for what is found in the commentaries on Tanach and the like—this is akin to one who wishes to begin the holiness of Shabbos from the morning until the morning, because the Rashbam (who was also a *posek*) explains it that way in his commentary on the Torah.

It is **obvious** that the Rambam was aware of the teachings of our Sages in the *sugya* of Moshiach in Sanhedrin, the Yerushalmi, and so on. Yet, he nonetheless **rules the law clearly** as stated above.

***

T'shma

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 15, p. 493. It is addressed to R' Shazar, and a copy was sent to R' Shlomo Yosef Zevin, as noted in the previous letter. Additional letters to him—above, Vol. 23, 8867, and in the references in the notes there.

**A clear psak din**: See also Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 5, p. 149 in the note. Above, letter 8744.

**That the Rashbam... explains it that way in his commentary on the Torah**: Bereishis 1:5.

**The Yerushalmi, etc.**: Beginning of Berachos.

## 960

B"H, 23 Tammuz, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter, in which you write of how you recognized the kindnesses of Hashem and witnessed the magnitude of the miracles, etc., and that you immediately expressed this recognition through concrete action—the fulfillment of the mitzvah of the Ribono shel Olam, the mitzvah of putting on tefillin—and your resolution to ascend in holiness, on the path that leads to the House of Hashem.

May it be His will that the promise of our Sages, of blessed memory, that "one mitzvah leads to another," be fulfilled in you. May your daily conduct increasingly align with our Torah, the Torah of life, and its mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them." There is always room for improvement in all matters of goodness and holiness, for they are infinite, as their source is from the Ein Sof, may He be blessed and exalted.

Currently, this is easier to achieve, as you stand under the impression of these events and miracles. For a miracle—from the expression "I will raise a banner (nes) upon the mountains"—**elevates** a person, bringing about an awakening and a nobility of spirit to recognize the wonders of the Creator and His Divine Providence. A person of reason must inevitably arrive at the immediate conclusion that if Hashem is the Master of His world at the time of a miracle, then He is certainly the Master of the world tomorrow, the day after, and for all time. This obligates a person to fulfill the mitzvos of the Creator, may He be blessed. Even if the past was what it was, from this point forward, one’s life must be ordered in accordance with the command of Hashem, with joy and a good heart. And although it may sometimes appear that there are difficulties, with the appropriate strength of resolve, one sees that these difficulties are, for the most part, illusory, or at the very least, easier than they appeared. In any case, it is well worth overcoming them.

Surely you will maintain a connection with those friends who influenced you for the good, and who will certainly be ready to assist you in the future as much as possible. May the Ribono shel Olam fulfill the requests of your heart for the good, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With blessings for success and for good tidings.

## 9747

[27 Tammuz, 5727]

...The booklet "MiMa'amakim" was received, and thank you very much.

It is a **great** wonder that you are not utilizing every possibility (through the press and the like) to **disseminate** traditional Judaism and its values (including—the dissemination of the wellsprings as well, of course). And if not now, when?!

As for the excuse I heard from another, "What will the editorial board say?", I answered him that its source is impure, and in the vast majority of cases—it also has no basis. And if they do not refrain **at all** from fighting with the editorial board over "raising" their material salary, why would they not conduct themselves in this way (at the very least—with a semblance of this assertiveness) regarding raising the content of the articles, the news, and so on?

#### ***9747***

Printed in "Heichal Menachem," Vol. 3, p. 103, and completed according to a copy.

**And if not now, when**: Avos 1:14.

## ט'שמח

B"H, end of Tammuz, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of the Yeshiva Gedola of Melbourne, may they live:

Peace and blessing!

The *pidyon nefesh* has been received and will be read at an *eis ratzon* at the holy *tziyun*.

We have recently passed the days of redemption, 12-13 Tammuz, when my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zya*, the *Nasi* of the Jewish people, was released from his imprisonment in his native land—where he had been incarcerated for his monumental work in strengthening and disseminating Torah and *mitzvos*, despite the persecution of religion that was then at its peak.

Through the mercies of Hashem, he emerged in victory, for those who had imprisoned him were the very ones who released him.

As my father-in-law, the Rebbe, wrote, his redemption was not merely a private redemption, but a redemption and victory for all matters of Judaism. Therefore, it is a day of *segulah* for all Jewish men and women wherever they may be, and especially for those who walk in his ways and participate in his activities and institutions.

And if this is true every year, it is all the more so this year, which is the fortieth year since his redemption. As is well known, our Sages teach that a period of forty years adds understanding to the depth of a teacher’s mind, etc.

As with every matter of remembrance in Torah and Judaism, the intention is that the remembrance should awaken actual action in the spirit of the days mentioned and observed. Regarding *Chag HaGeulah*, the immediate instruction and conclusion is: if in that country, at that time, and under those conditions, a Jew could act and work for the strengthening and dissemination of Torah and *mitzvos*, then *kal v'chomer* [all the more so] in countries and under conditions that are incomparably more comfortable and favorable.

May it be the will of Hashem that each and every one of us, together with all our Jewish brethren, may fulfill all that has been said with joy and a glad heart.

With blessings for good tidings regarding your great persistence in the study of *nigleh* and Chassidus, and your success in this and in general,

**M. Schneerson**

***

With blessings for good tidings regarding your success in the holy work of disseminating the *maayanos* and Judaism in general—with the appropriate energy and alacrity.

***

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from 18 Sivan, and thank you for the good news contained within it. May it be the will of Hashem that from now on you bring only good news, in a way that is good, both visibly and revealed.

Since we have entered the month of redemption, the details of *Chag HaGeulah* of 12-13 Tammuz are surely known to you...

And surely you, too, will mark the upcoming *Chag HaGeulah* in the manner appropriate to what has been stated. May it be the will of Hashem that you do so with joy and a glad heart.

With blessings for *Chag HaGeulah*.

## 9349

[Tammuz 5727]

Regarding the contents of your aforementioned letter:

Concerning the two candidates for the position of Dayan—since the matter is in doubt, *shev v'al ta'aseh adif* (it is better to sit and do nothing), and you should not involve yourself in the matter.

Regarding the proposal for a *takanas agunos*—in principle, it is correct in my opinion, provided, of course, that it is studied in depth by several *gedolei hora'ah* regarding the specific wording, the timing of its enactment, etc., and as you wrote—that for the time being, you are only discussing the general concept.

However, it is a matter of great concern how one can **absolutely** rule out that this will not provide some assistance to those who are pressuring to "innovate" the Halacha and adapt it to the reality of our times, etc., etc. (which is the opposite of the Rambam’s ruling that **all** reality is only from the truth of His existence). For, unfortunately, among those pressuring are some who, in their private lives, are *yirei Shamayim*, etc., and they turn this defense into an indictment against the Torah, whose foundation is that it shall not be changed, etc. And *d'l* (a word to the wise is sufficient).

In our generation, which is seized by a mania for publicity, the back-and-forth discussion will surely eventually be publicized, and everyone—from "your heads to your water-drawers"—will issue their own rulings, from which it will be a *kal v'chomer* (a fortiori argument) for their proposals regarding the other 612 *mitzvos*, etc. And "whoever permits [something forbidden] to Israel [is liable to] become a leader." And *d'l*.

And if it is impossible to rule this out, I am doubtful whether the whole matter is worthwhile, for when faced with a *bari* (certainty) and a *shema* (doubt) regarding the benefit—the *bari* is preferred.

#### ***9349***

Printed in *Nelcha B'orchosov*, p. 260, from the Rebbe’s holy handwriting on the letter of the inquirer, Rabbi Hillel Medalia, Rabbi of Antwerp. Additional letters to him—above 8335, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

**Shev v'al ta'aseh adif**: *Eruvin* 100a.

**The Rambam’s ruling**: Beginning of *Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah*.

**That it shall not be changed, etc.**: The essence of the ninth of the Thirteen Principles of Faith.

**From your heads to your water-drawers**: Based on the phrasing of the verse—beginning of *Parshas Nitzavim*.

**Whoever permits [something forbidden] to Israel... becomes a leader**: Based on the language of Chazal—*Gittin* 56b. And elsewhere.

**Bari and shema... bari is preferred**: *Bava Kamma* 118a.

## 9550

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants of the Chabad Yeshiva summer camp in Lod, and their counselors,
May Hashem protect them and grant them life,

Shalom u’Bracha!

It was with pleasure that I received your regards at the conclusion of the month in which the redemption of our Nasi, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, took place. The story of his imprisonment and redemption is surely known to you all.

The purpose of days of remembrance in the life of our people, the Children of Israel, is that these days should be "remembered and acted upon." This means that they should bring about an *hisorerus* to perform deeds in the spirit of those days in our current time. In our specific case, this aligns with the hopes of the *Baal HaGeulah*, who dedicated all his days and strengths to the education of the sons and daughters of Israel in the purity of holiness. You have surely heard of the greatness of his *mesiras nefesh* day after day, how he did not recoil before threats, suffering, and so on—and in the end, he was victorious.

From this, it is understood that when one is in a position where they can follow in his footsteps and continue his activities without delays or obstacles—and on the contrary, especially when one is in our Holy Land—how much one must act in this regard with joy and a glad heart. I am confident that each and every one of you will strive to do so, both regarding yourself and regarding exerting a positive influence on your friends. May Hashem, blessed be He, send His blessing for your success and fulfill the requests of your hearts for the good.

With blessings for success and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***9550***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 13, p. 245.

A similar version was sent on the 29th of Tammuz to the "participants of the 'Gan Yisrael' summer camp in Kfar Chabad, and their counselors."

**The days that are remembered and acted upon**: See also above, letter 9667, note s.v. *HaYamim HaEileh*.

## 9353

9353

B"H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Elul 5727
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and involved in communal needs, etc.,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to the notification regarding the scheduling of the wedding of your grandson, the avreich, R' Yaakov (may he live and be well), with the bride, Mrs. Penina (may she live and be well), in a good and auspicious hour,

I hereby express my blessing of Mazal Tov, Mazal Tov, and may it be in a good and auspicious hour. May they build a home in Israel, an everlasting edifice, upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos as they are illuminated by the "light of Torah"—which is the teachings of Chassidus.

And may you derive from them much true, Chassidishe Yiddishe nachas.

With the blessing of Mazal Tov, Mazal Tov, and with the blessing of a complete and speedy recovery,

**M. Schneerson**

To note, according to our Sages, "merit is brought about on an auspicious day" (for then the merit and the good deed are more powerful), especially when the good is threefold, for then it is a *chazakah* (a presumption of permanence) and an "everlasting edifice":

A virgin is married on the **fourth** day (the acronym for *levanah*—the moon—as is brought in many places), the day on which the sun and the moon were suspended.

**On Rosh Chodesh**—the molad of the moon and the unification of the sun and the moon.

**E-l-u-l**—(the essence and the beginning, as per the) acronym: *Ani* (Knesses Yisrael—the bride) *l’dodi* (Hashem—the groom) *v’dodi li* (for they are unified in one word).

**It is appropriate to look into the proposal from Antwerp (for the grandson, may he live and be well) about which you write.**

**I have received the pidyon nefesh, etc., via the esteemed Chossid, etc., involved in communal needs, R' N. (may he live and be well) Mendel, and thank you, thank you.**

## 9354

B"H, Erev Chodesh HaRachamim, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing, and involved in communal needs, etc., Rabbi Yitzchak Moshe, may he live, author of seforim, Chief Rabbi of the Sephardic community in Buenos Aires,

Shalom u’Bracha!

Due to various pressures and reasons—including the nature of the matter itself, your request to provide a suitable guide for your community—my response to your letter has been delayed, and I ask for your forgiveness.

It is unnecessary to explain that the demand for G-d-fearing guides who have influence over the youth is very great, and "the handful cannot satisfy the lion", especially when it comes to the needs of one's own city, which take precedence. This is particularly true when speaking of other countries, where, in addition to all other qualities, one also requires someone who speaks the local language fluently, and so on.

Nevertheless, it goes without saying that we do not ignore any request or appeal in this area, and we have indeed taken note of your request. However, until now, a guide suitable for the conditions and requirements of your location has not yet been found. Surely you have also reached out to the institutions and organizations of our Sephardic brethren in various countries, and may it be the will of Hashem that their efforts succeed.

As we stand on the threshold of the month of mercy and forgiveness, I wish you and all those who gather in your shadow a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and blessed year, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With respect and blessing for good tidings.

#### ***9354***

**And the handful cannot satisfy the lion**: See Berachos 3b.

**One's own city takes precedence**: See Bava Metzia 71a.

## 957

957

B"H, 1st day of Rosh Chodesh Elul, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

...It is certainly unnecessary to emphasize that everything possible must be done to elevate the standard of studies, which depends first and foremost on the state of the teachers—men and women alike—for they recognize that the education of the sons and daughters of Yisrael is a heavenly task. ## 5727

5th of Elul, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. Geula Cohen

Blessings and peace!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 1st of Elul and the one preceding it. You have already received an official response regarding the proposal for participation in a general poll, which is not a practice I engage in at all. In any case, thank you for your consideration.

I must add—and not as an addendum, but because in truth this is the primary intent of my letter—that I felt great disappointment upon reading your first letter. My meaning is as follows:

Ever since our conversation when you visited New York (which I hope you remember, or at least its main points), I have followed, inquired, and investigated whether there have been any results from that discussion. For our conversation, at least as I intended it, was not official, nor was it in the nature of an interview, but rather—as I believe I also stated explicitly—out of the recognition that exceptional ability and potential are at your disposal. On the other hand, our current era, and especially these most recent years, is unparalleled in its potential—potential regarding the strengthening and establishing of the position of our people, the Children of Israel, wherever they may be, and especially in our Holy Land, may it be built and established speedily in our days through Mashiach Tzidkeinu.

Therefore, the demand of the hour is that anyone who can do something in the aforementioned direction has it as their primary duty and initial task, especially since this is for the benefit of the many, and often for the salvation of the many.

This applies even if the ability and potential are only a matter of doubt; how much more so when the past has proven that a specific individual possesses special powers and opportunities to utilize them in that direction, in which case all these matters apply with even greater force and intensity.

I will repeat, albeit briefly, what we spoke about in our conversation:

Experience has proven that certain circles of our people are susceptible to influence, especially the youth and the young, who in the near future will direct the course of events in the settlements of the Children of Israel, including in our Holy Land.

For various reasons, daily life has dissipated the enthusiasm of the youth and the young, and as a result, their activity in the desired direction has waned. This has led to their energy being channeled in undesirable directions, and even to the opposite of what is desired. The justification given is that such-and-such is boring, or that such-and-such activity is old-fashioned and belongs to past generations, and so on.

My suggestion was that you utilize that energy and enthusiasm—which, even though the layer of daily worries—that is, gray, ordinary life—has covered over, I have a strong hope that you will awaken them and bring them to fruition, to ignite the youth and kindle the spark hidden within them toward positive actions that are a necessity for the life of the collective and also for the benefit of the individual.

However, during the years that have passed since our conversation, no actual deed has come to my attention as a result of my words. My meaning is simple: despite my searching, I have not found in those publications where you write, nor in other places that have come to my view, an echo of your activities in the aforementioned direction.

Seemingly, one could excuse this by saying that you do not agree with my opinion. But the necessity to extract the youth and the young from their lethargy is so clear and simple, and the shortage of individuals who have the potential to succeed in this is so great, that in my opinion, it is impossible for there to be any doubt regarding this command of the hour, especially regarding anyone who has succeeded in this field in the past.

Surely there is benefit in meetings with people who hold prominent positions in various circles, to learn their opinions and publicize them, and so on. Since you are engaged in this, you certainly see this benefit tangibly. But this does not exempt one at all from a direct meeting with the active part of the entire nation, and likewise within the nation of the Children of Israel—the part whose measure of energy is greater than in other parts of the nation; that part which has not yet been damaged by a life of compromise over decades until it became second nature; that part which does not fear a challenge and has the courage of spirit to admit it if they find that their path in life was not in order, and to begin a new way of life, in a new direction, and sometimes even an opposite one, from their previous course of life—all of which are qualities that will not be found in party leaders, nor in most leaders of any circle whatsoever.

It is understood that after a few months had passed since our conversation and I did not see any action or results from it, I sought a pretext and reason to write to you and ask you about the aforementioned, but for several reasons, the matter was postponed from time to time. One of the main reasons was that I did not know what your reaction would be if, on the basis of one conversation and one meeting, I were to express an opinion regarding your "life," especially an opinion that demands a change in your activities, and a fundamental change at that. And there was another, more internal reason, and perhaps even a more primary one: the health of your child, etc., which you told me about (in addition to what I heard from others). Sorrow prevents a person from many things, especially matters that require energy and a significant struggle against the current, which leads to isolation, and so on.

My disappointment that I could not reach you and move you to the actions we discussed grew even more in the period surrounding the Six-Day War, and in those days themselves and the days that followed. During this time, the enthusiasm of all circles of our people was at its peak everywhere, and there was a complete lack of direction toward a positive goal and a positive matter of building in spirituality and in physicality. To our great sorrow, the people did not find the leaders who would guide them and direct their enthusiasm toward positive deeds, and not even those who would strengthen the enthusiasm and encourage it. Even in this period, things are "settling down" in the well-known formula, where people move on to the order of the day. And even in these days, I did not find a trace of your activities.

It is simple that what is written above is not by way of moralizing, Heaven forbid, but rather an attempt to renew the conversation, even if in writing, regarding the content of our first conversation, and perhaps now your activities will come in the aforementioned direction. Concretely: to elevate the youth and the young to the eternal essence of our people, which, together with the eternity of the matters themselves, are, in the style of our Sages of blessed memory, "new every day."

For example: propaganda for internal *aliyah*, instead of the "calls to action" that are too numerous to count regarding *aliyah* from affluent countries, whose prospects are extremely slim, at least in the near future. And at the same time, as the experience of absorbing volunteers has shown, the conditions are not at all suitable for absorbing them in the desired manner. Internal *aliyah* has declined in the most alarming way precisely among the Sephardic circles of our brethren since their arrival in our Holy Land. If there were an appeal from a Sephardic woman—an appeal with enthusiasm—that would not listen at all to those who preached for small families, a preaching that for many years, to our great sorrow, succeeded exceptionally well—surely such an appeal would find a correct and deep echo, even to the point of actual change. And in the same way, this applies to the establishment of family life, and so on.

I have brought an example of matters that everyone admits are vital in our Holy Land, from the edge of the left to the edge of the right. But surely the vast majority of our people living in the Holy Land have sobered up from the enticements and incitements to turn away from the path of our Torah, the Torah of life, our eternal Torah. A call to return to the source and the way of life according to the Torah and its *mitzvos* will "also" find a correct echo and will lead to actions in certain circles that will go on to expand and multiply. For the heart of every Jewish man and woman is, after all, sensitive to our Torah and *mitzvos*; one only needs to find the point—in other words, the *mitzvah*—that is appropriate to the state of mind of a specific circle or a specific person, and to begin by speaking to that circle or person about this *mitzvah*, and then, eventually, one *mitzvah* leads to another.

I am aware of the argument and the saying: how can one preach to others before the preacher has reached perfection in their own life? But we see tangibly that this argument is nothing but a cover for the lack of desire to act in the aforementioned direction. For there is only One who is perfect, the Holy One, Blessed be He, and there has never been a shortage of preachers among the Jewish people—preachers for positive things, and also for strange and unusual things. Furthermore, and this is the main point, in our era, time is too short to wait until the preacher and motivator becomes perfect and only then begins to act. There is no other advice but to do both things at once: to preach and motivate oneself, and also the environment.

My letter has become long, and I will summarize the point of what is written above: it is even clearer to me now than at our first meeting—and as was my opinion then, so is my opinion now—that you are gifted with the talent of influence and possess the potential for it. It is a pity for every day that passes while you do not utilize your talent in the direction of returning the youth and the young—and it would be even better to include the adults, although that is more difficult—to a positive life, a life worthy of the name, a life according to our Torah and its *mitzvos*, of which it is said, "**And he shall live** (the Jewish people) **by them**." And one hour sooner is better.

I would be happy to hear if there has been a positive development regarding the child, may he live, and thank you in advance if you will write about this.

With blessings for good news in all the aforementioned, and in the traditional style—for a good and sweet year, written and sealed.

**M. Schneerson**

## 9359

B"H, Tuesday, the day on which "it was good" was doubled, Parshas Ki Seitzei, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Spiritual Committee of Kfar Chabad, founded and directed by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisroel, and at their head, the venerable Rabbi, the chossid, the G-d-fearing man, R. Shneur Zalman, may he live, the Mara D'asra,
May Hashem preserve them and may they live.

Greetings and Blessings!

As we stand in the days of Elul, the month of mercy, which is the acronym for **A**ni **L**edodi **V**edodi **L**i ("I am to my Beloved and my Beloved is to me"), the month in which, as the Alter Rebbe states, one goes out to greet the light of His countenance in the field.

And immediately following this is the month of Tishrei, the general month for the entire coming year, in which "Tishrei" (you will unloose) and "Tashbuk" (you will forgive) and "Tichaper" (you will atone) for the sins of Your people, and "Meshuva" (you will be satisfied) with everything.

My request is for you, the planners and organizers, to invite those residents of Kfar Chabad who came from our country in the past, during this year of Hakhel, who are twenty years of age or older, and who have not yet visited here and have not prostrated themselves at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, our Nasi, and who desire to do so, to invite them in my name to visit here for the month of Tishrei, to prostrate themselves at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and for us all to pray together in the shul of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and to study Nigleh and Chassidus in his Beis Medrash, etc.

* * *

It is understood that this applies only provided that this trip will not cause any detriments to the holy institutions and their affairs—in Eretz Yisroel in general, and in Kfar Chabad in particular.

Likewise, the trip is conditional upon their returning to Kfar Chabad.

And regarding those who are married—that the trip must be with the full consent of their wives, may they live.

* * *

May it be His will that in these days, when, as mentioned above, we greet the King, the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He, in the field—at which time everyone who wishes to go out to greet Him is permitted (and my father-in-law, the Rebbe, adds and explains: and is able) to do so, and He receives everyone with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to all—that the King, the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He, while He is still in the field, will fulfill all the requests and desires of their hearts for the good, for all those who greet Him, within the entirety of Klal Yisroel. May He fulfill (as above) with a pleasant countenance, and may each and every one be inscribed and sealed for a good and sweet year, in revealed and manifest goodness.

With respect and with the blessing of Ksiva Vachasima Tova.

P.S.
It is understood that the matter of travel expenses does not concern the travelers, and it will be arranged without them, with the help of Hashem. Due to the shortness of time, you will surely hasten to arrange all of the above, and first and foremost—to compile a detailed list and send it here in a fast and urgent manner. Thank you in advance for the effort and trouble in all of this.

## 960

B"H, 9 Elul, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished Rabbi, a man of merit, may his light shine and ascend, Rabbi Pinchas Toledano, may he live,
Rabbi of the Sephardic community in London, may it be protected by Hashem.

Peace and blessing!

I received your honor’s letter with some delay, containing a request for a blessing on behalf of one of the members of your community, Mr. [Name], may he live.

I will mention him at the resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May it be the will of Hashem that he brings good news regarding this matter.

This is especially relevant as we are currently in the month of mercy. These auspicious days were beautifully explained by the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, through a parable of a king who, before entering his city, is met by the townspeople who go out to greet him in the field. At that time, anyone who wishes to go out to greet him is permitted to do so, and he receives them all with a friendly countenance and shows a smiling face to everyone (Likutei Torah, Parshas Re'eh, p. 32a, in the discourse beginning "Ani L'dodi V'dodi Li," the acronym for Elul).

Knowing the tradition of our Sephardic brethren, may they live, that from time immemorial they have set times for the study of the inner dimension of the Torah, in addition to the study of the revealed Torah, I am certain that the community leaders and the Rabbis at their head continue in this tradition. This is especially true in our days and in this current era, when the study of the inner dimension of the Torah holds special importance, as explained at length in the introduction of R' Chaim Vital to Shaar HaHakdamos of the Arizal, the living. After all, our holy Torah in general, and the inner dimension of the Torah—the "soul of the Torah," in the language of the Zohar—in particular, is the very gateway to heaven.

With respect and with a blessing for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year.

#### ***960***

**In the introduction of R' Chaim Vital to Shaar HaHakdamos**: Also printed in the supplement to Kuntres Eitz Chaim by the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory, and elsewhere.

**In the language of the Zohar**: Vol. 3, 152a.

## 9654

9654

B"H, 15 Elul, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. A. Sheftel, may he live,
Mayor of Rishon LeZion

Shalom u’Bracha!

It was a pleasant surprise to receive your letter of 30 Av and to see your interest in the situation of the "Achai Temimim" Yeshivah in your city, Rishon LeZion, in addition to the reports I have received from other sources for some time now. Especially since I have a strong hope that this interest of yours is expressed—in accordance with the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory, that "action is the essential thing"—in actual practice, by assisting as much as possible the "Achai Temimim" Yeshivah within the framework of the institutions of our Torah, the Torah of life, which are in your city.

It is understood that if in every place where the children of Israel dwell, and in all eras, Torah institutions have been among the primary and vital matters in the life of our people, the children of Israel, then how much more so in our Holy Land, upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year to the end of the year. This is even more so in our current era, which is full of events, upheavals, and the blurring of boundaries, where the necessity for Torah—which is a language of *hora'ah* (instruction)—in daily life is many times greater and beyond compare.

By *hashgacha pratis*, you have been given exceptional opportunities and the ability to act directly in your city in the aforementioned direction. The measure of good is greater, such that other cities and settlements of the children of Israel in our Holy Land will see this and do likewise, and the merit of the many will assist you.

It is understood that I am interested, as much as possible, in the state of our institutions wherever they may be, and foremost among them are those in the Holy Land, but to my regret, the resources are not at all sufficient for the demand.

Based on the tone of your letter, it is certainly, as mentioned above, superfluous to ask you to continue your help and assistance to the "Achai Temimim" Yeshivah in your city; rather, I wish to thank you for the help in the past and express my strong hope that you will continue to add to this in the future, more and more. And may you also influence your colleagues, may they live, and those who heed your wishes, in the aforementioned direction. May it be His will that you see good fruit from your labor in this, and in general in all matters of the city, that it may be worthy of its name—"Rishon LeZion" (First to Zion)—from which Torah and the word of Hashem will go forth.

With respect and blessing for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year.

**M. Schneerson**

## 5727

By the Grace of Hashem, Days of Selichos, 5727
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel everywhere,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life,

Peace and Blessing!

We stand at the conclusion of 5727, a year of **Hakhel** — the special mitzvah that was performed once every seven years, in the year following Shemitah, to **gather** (*"Hakhel"*) the people—men, women, and children—in the Beis HaMikdash, with the purpose of strengthening and encouraging them in Torah and mitzvos with yiras-shamayim.

As with all matters of Torah, which is **Toras Chaim** ("a guide for life"), the concept of **Hakhel** is reflected in various aspects of daily life as well. We will focus here on one aspect, in connection with these current days of cheshbon-hanefesh (soul-searching), along with the appropriate conclusions and resolutions that serve as preparation for a new and better year in all respects. But first, an introduction:

* * *

Human life is expressed through three general activities: **machshava** (thought), **dibbur** (speech), and **maaseh** (action).

In accordance with the accepted principle that nothing is ever lost, this is also true regarding human **machshava, dibbur, and maaseh**. That is to say, a thought, word, or deed from yesterday, the day before, or even earlier, has not been lost; rather, it continues to have an influence on the present and the future, as one can see quite simply in practical results, both regarding oneself and regarding one’s environment.

Another point in this regard is that although it may appear on the surface that an action already performed has left the human domain—that what was, was, and a person cannot retract or change the past—in truth, this is not so. For the Ribono shel Olam has given man a Divine power—through **teshuvah**—to change even the past. This means that teshuvah does not merely signify the possibility of changing the course of the future; it also has the power to act **directly** upon the past: to alter it, to the point of completely remaking it; until even willful transgressions lose their heavy guilt (*zedonos naasos lo kishgagos*), and even more—they can even be transformed into positive achievements (*zedonos naasos lo kazechuyos*).

And a further point: there are matters that find expression—at special times—with more vitality and feeling than at other times. And this brings us to the special significance of **Hakhel** at this present moment:

* * *

If every year, at this time, a person must make a cheshbon and a summary of his **machshavos, dibburim, and maasim** of the past year, also as a preparation for Rosh Hashanah, when he accepts upon himself the absolute sovereignty of the **Borei Olam** and **Melech HaOlam**, this must be carried out with even greater dedication and feeling at the conclusion of a **Hakhel year**. For the concept of **Hakhel**, in a spiritual sense, reminds and demands that one gather all his thoughts, words, and deeds and place them into his inner "Beis HaMikdash," with complete dedication to submit himself to the *Dvar HaMelech*—to the Ribono shel Olam.

This year, at the conclusion of the **Hakhel year**, a Yid must make a special cheshbon-hanefesh in the spirit of "Hakhel," with a firm resolution:

To change the thoughts, words, and deeds in daily life that require change;

To rectify and improve those that require more perfection;

And to bring more hislahavus and vitality into those matters that were indeed performed with perfection, but only according to the measure of one’s spiritual state in the ordinary months, in order to animate them with the spirit of this present moment—the eve of the **hachtarah (coronation) of the Melech**—when all matters of machshava, dibbur, and maaseh must be in an entirely different mode of elevation,

Until the full revelation of Elokus in one’s personal life, in one’s surroundings, and in the entire world,

In accordance with the prayer: **"Mloch al haolam kulo"** (May You reign over the entire world)... **"Veyeda"** (and may [all] know)... **"Veyavin"** (and understand)... **"Veyomar kol asher neshamah beapo Hashem Elokei Yisrael Melech umalchuso bakol mashlah"** (and may everyone who has a soul in his nostrils say: Hashem, the G-d of Israel, is King, and His kingdom rules over everything).

Reflecting on the fact that nothing is ever lost, one sees that there is no basis for sadness or despondency, not only regarding the future, but also regarding the past. On the contrary, with the full certainty that the Ribono shel Olam is watching over every single person and assists every good movement and action, a person can approach the preparations for the new year with complete simcha. And even if certain matters in the past year evoke deep regret, at the same time there is the overwhelming simcha that the Ribono shel Olam has given the possibility to transform even *zedonos*, Heaven forbid, into *zechuyos*. It is also understandable that when a thing is done with simcha and certainty, it is also done with greater hatzlacha.

May Hashem Yisbarach help every single person, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, to utilize this opportunity to the fullest extent, with simcha and a good heart.

With the blessing of *Kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 744

[5727]

The mission of a man and a woman from Bnei Yisrael is not to ascend and shake and stir the worlds; rather, it is to make for Him, may He be blessed, a dwelling place in the lower realms (and this should be done with joy and a good heart) through **Torah and Mitzvos**. The deed is the essential thing [**if** a shaking of the worlds is required for this, they will be shaken **automatically**]. Regarding the "mainstay of the **home**" [the woman], this applies first and foremost to the affairs of the **home**, and through ways of pleasantness and peace—**which are** the ways of Torah, as it is written, "Her ways are ways of pleasantness, and all her paths are peace"—and specifically in an orderly fashion (in the literal sense), the opposite of the "other side," which is "without order." All of this is within the ten *tefachim* [the realm of the physical world], **where** the Torah was given.

#### ***744***

Printed in *Heichal Menachem*, Vol. 2, p. 90. A response to an individual who wrote: "If I had the strength to ascend and shake and stir the worlds to tell Melech HaMoshiach, 'Reveal yourself, the people are worthy!'"

**To make for Him, may He be blessed, a dwelling place in the lower realms**: See *Tanchuma, Bechukosai* 3; *Naso* 16; *Bamidbar Rabbah*, ch. 13, 6.

*Tanya*, beginning of ch. 36.

**The deed is the essential thing**: *Avos*, ch. 1, mishnah 17.

**The mainstay of the home**: See *Bereishis Rabbah*, ch. 71, 2; *Zohar*, Vol. I, 154a; and elsewhere.

**As it is written, "Her ways are ways of pleasantness, and all her paths are peace"**: *Mishlei* 3:17.

## 976

976

[5727]

Regarding the business—a venture in which he has **no** knowledge **whatsoever**, and has never engaged in, etc., and it is a large operation where it is possible to conceal many things without him even knowing that something was concealed—

If he enters into this, he is relying **entirely** on the partner without any possibility of controlling [or verifying] him.

And it requires further study whether there is room for this.

—Except if, on his side, he also brings in an expert, and that expert of his is also deeply involved in the thick of things and there is no room to suspect him **etc. etc.**—

All of which is far from reality to find. And therefore, the matter does not seem advisable to me.

#### ***976***

Printed in "Nelcha B'Orchotav," p. 205—from a photocopy of the Rebbe's holy handwriting; a response to an inquirer regarding whether to enter into a business partnership, when "he has no knowledge of it whatsoever and has never engaged in it."

## 978

[Summer 5727]

[Question:
Regarding the explanation that the war was a *milchemes mitzvah* (obligatory war), and that the statement of the Rambam (*Hilchos Melachim*, end of ch. 7) applies to it—"And he knows that he is waging war for the sake of the *yichud* of Hashem... he is guaranteed..."—seemingly: (a) A *milchemes mitzvah* can only exist when there is a King of Israel (the implication of Rambam, *Hilchos Melachim*, ch. 5 and onwards). (b) Seemingly, this difficulty can be resolved based on the Rambam (*Hilchos Shabbos*, ch. 2, halacha 23): "Gentiles who besieged cities of Israel... we go out against them with weapons and desecrate the Shabbos for them." (c) The Rambam (*Hilchos Melachim*, ch. 7, halacha 15) states: "And his intention should be solely to sanctify the Name." Seemingly, in the present case, the majority are far from any such matter, for most of them—before they went out to defend, and even afterwards—are not religious. How can it be said of them, "And he will build for himself a lasting house in Israel... and will merit the life of the World to Come"? Furthermore, the Rambam there implies that the one to whom these blessings apply is only one who has no sins. (d) Is this a miracle from Heaven, for seemingly it is impossible that the *Ribono shel Olam* would perform a miracle through those who oppose Hashem?]

**a)** This requires further study—as discussed with Rabbi Y. before the *farbrengen*—for if so:
1) The wars between Yehoshua and Shaul were not *milchemes mitzvah* (and perhaps this is the precision of Rashi regarding "in the days of Yehoshua"—*Sotah* 44a). 2) According to this, the *Shas* does not discuss the status of *all* the wars at the end of the Second Temple period—the time of the *Mishnah*—and many of the *Tannaim* participated in them. 3) They would have no status of *milchemes mitzvah* at all! **And furthermore.** This requires study in *Yosippon* and in *Antiquities* by Josephus; I believe he mentions there that they appointed an anointed one for war. See *Seder HaDoros*, 1, 4825. In any case, this is not what I intended, **as follows below**. As also noted in the *Morgen Journal*. This requires study in the Ramban (*Vayechi* 49:10) regarding the war of Chanukah.

**b)** I **explicitly** mentioned "matters of straw and stubble or souls," meaning the *halacha* in the Rambam there, and it is **explicit** in the *Gemara* and *Poskim* that this applies even in our time (and in *Chutz LaAretz*). And in the Rambam, *Hilchos Melachim* (though it is not certain that this is the definition—in all its details—of the *milchemes mitzvah* of *Maseches Sotah*).

**c)** This war was a ***mitzvah*** according to the Torah (Rambam, ibid.), so the Rambam’s language, "And he knows that he is waging war for the sake of the *yichud* of Hashem," applies to this as well (*Hilchos Melachim*, end of ch. 7—which also applies to a war of "assisting Israel from an enemy that has come upon them"—ibid., beginning of ch. 5. And see *Zechariah* 2:12. And in many places. **And there is no reason** to differentiate in the connection between defending against an enemy and the *yichud* of Hashem, whether or not there is a king in Israel).

**d)** The **majority**, not all.

**e)** **Before** they went out to defend, and perhaps even afterwards, they are not religious, but a portion of them changes and is awakened **at a time of tangible danger**, as in the present case—and if so, at the time of the deed, he is guaranteed that he will not, etc., for he is **waging** the wars of Hashem.
Regarding another main point, this matter was brought up (similar to the **precedence** of Zevulun over Yissachar) that one who fights can be said to have all these blessings, which were not mentioned for one who protects them (and the Jewish people) through **Torah study, even if he intends for the *yichud* of Hashem, etc.**

**f)** On the contrary, the Rambam is "as its literal meaning"—and not like Rabbi Yosi HaGlili.

**g)** It is clear that the fact that 2.5 million Jews in *Eretz Yisrael* (including the *yeshivos*, etc.) were saved is a miracle from Heaven of holiness, etc.
If not: 1) Why and for what did they command to say *Tehillim*?! 2) **What** did they accomplish by saying them?!

**h)** Dr. Kastner was, etc., and yet through him, they were saved, etc. A judge has only what his eyes see, and they should ask the *dayanim* of *Yerushalayim* whether there were miracles. **Especially the Raavad of the Eidah HaChareidis, Rabbi P. Epstein.** And *d'l* (a word to the wise).
